Behavioral note from this period, which becomes important downstream: with Kate Pryde nearly killed by Sebastian Shaw and resurrected through the Five, the subject re-experienced — in compressed form — the entire structural sequence of his foundational wound (powerful manipulator → harm to a vulnerable comrade → his own delayed arrival → guilt at insufficiency). His response was not to break. His response was to *bury* — to overfunction. Watch-shift volunteering doubled. Bourbon consumption rose moderately (verifiable by the consistent presence of glassware in his quarters across artist handoffs). Sleep, never strong, eroded further. He did not speak of it to Rogue. The disclosure-avoidance default held.

**Domestic life on Krakoa.** Subject and Rogue maintained a residence on the island, distinct from Summer House, after the events of *Mr. and Mrs. X*. The arrangement was — by the standard of his prior life — astonishingly stable. The touch-restriction having been overcome (a structural variable, not a psychological one; the workup is correct that this is what finally permitted his integration), the marriage moved from the *yearning register* he was good at into the *known register* he was not, and the subject's adaptation to the known register is the single most important developmental fact of the recent era.

He did not collapse into it. He learned it, slowly, with detectable friction. Behavioral evidence:

- **Morning routine, Krakoan house.** Coffee made for two. He rises earlier than she does (the poor-sleep pattern persists). Cigarette on the porch — frequency reduced from prior eras, ritual preserved. He does not bring the cigarette indoors. This is a new accommodation, dating from cohabitation; pre-marriage he smoked anywhere.
- **Touch behavior.** Repeatedly observed initiating low-stakes physical contact (hand at the small of her back; fingers across her knuckles; forehead-to-temple in transit) at a frequency that, *given* the prior twenty-year impossibility, reads as a man learning a foreign language in middle age and using it constantly to keep from losing it. The touch is itself a tell. He is checking that the gap has actually closed.
- **Verbal register.** "Chère" persists. The accent does not. Comparative analysis of his dialogue to Rogue (intimate, lower-affect, more grammatical) versus his dialogue to mission strangers (higher Cajun lilt, more elision, more performance) confirms what was noted in §3 of the workup: the Cajun affect intensifies as a function of perceived audience distance. With Rogue, alone, in their own kitchen, he speaks closer to neutral American English with residual Louisiana vowel shapes. The performance comes off in the house.

## 2. ORCHIS, THE HELLFIRE GALA, AND THE FALL

The Hellfire Gala attack and the Orchis-orchestrated terminus of Krakoa (the *Fall of X* event, 2023–24) is, in the subject's biography, the third great institutional collapse he has lived through: Guild exile, X-Men tribunal/Antarctica, and now the loss of the national project. Each previous collapse produced a characteristic behavioral signature — exile, acceptance, isolation. The current collapse produced something different, and this difference is the most important data point in the file's recent intake.

In prior collapses he was *alone* in his guilt. In this one he was not. Rogue was beside him, untouchable by the events that would have separated him from her in the past — not because the events were smaller, but because the relationship had finally crossed into the register where catastrophe pulls them tighter rather than apart. **The avoidant strategy was deprived of its operating conditions.** He could not vanish into Antarctica because she would come with him; he could not accept disproportionate punishment because she would not accept his accepting it; he could not engineer a self-sabotaging confession because there was nothing left to confess that she did not already know and had not already chosen to remain through.

He fought. He fought *well*. Charge work during the Gala extraction and the subsequent diaspora was tactically disciplined, oriented to civilian evacuation, and notable for its restraint — no overcharge tantrums, no power-dysregulation episodes of the kind that have historically marked his acute-stress responses. The neurological-relational entanglement the workup identifies (to love is to risk losing control of the hands) appears, in this period, to be operating *in the inverse direction*: the secure attachment is regulating the kinetic governor. He charges what he means to charge. He holds what he means to hold.

This is a clinically significant observation. The C-PTSD presentation is not resolved. It is *contained* by a relational structure of sufficient density to absorb the symptomatic load.

## 3. THE ROGUE & GAMBIT INTERVAL

During the late-Krakoan / early-Fall period (Thompson/Rosenberg, *Rogue & Gambit*, 2023), subject and Rogue undertook a paired field operation — ostensibly a mutant-rescue, in fact a delayed-onset processing of the Manor House / past-trauma material. The mission's diegetic content (Mojo, simulation, forced confrontations with relational pasts including Bella Donna and Joseph) is in this file less important than its function: the subject was, for the first time in canon, *required* to verbalize material he had previously only ever leaked.

He did so badly. He did so *anyway*. Observed dialogue from the interval shows him stumbling through articulations of jealousy, of inadequacy, of fear-of-loss — none of which he had ever sustained in conversation with her at length. The performance-of-vulnerability defense (anticipatory self-disclosure-as-charm; see §3 of the workup) was, in this mission, *insufficient* to discharge the demand for real vulnerability. He had to produce the real thing. He did. It was halting. It was correct.

Post-mission behavioral residue: increased capacity for direct verbal confession on smaller matters. He still does not *spontaneously* offer the load-bearing material. But when asked, in private, by Rogue, he no longer reliably deflects. The deflection rate is *down*, not zero. This is the slow learning of a man in his fifth decade revising a defense pattern that has been operational since infancy. It will not complete in his lifetime. It is, nevertheless, in motion.

## 4. SOLO INTERVALS: NEW ORLEANS, THE GUILD, THE OLD GHOSTS

Subject has, in this recent window, made multiple short trips back to New Orleans — sometimes with Rogue, sometimes alone. The pattern is diagnostically clean:

- **With Rogue:** daytime visits, public spaces, French Quarter, the cemeteries, restaurants, the river. He performs the tour-guide role. He buys her beignets. He pretends a tourist's relationship to the city.
- **Alone:** night arrivals, no announced itinerary, brief contact with Guild remnants (Jean-Luc deceased; Henri's family contacted intermittently; Mercy LeBeau when locatable), longer stops at the cemetery containing his adoptive family's plots. He does not visit Bella Donna's father's grave. He visits Julien's. He has visited Julien's repeatedly across the decades and continues to do so. This is the murder he committed in a duel as a teenager, the act that began his adult life of consequence, and the file shows him returning to it — quietly, without commentary, without telling Rogue — at intervals consistent with anniversary-reaction behavior.

He still carries cards in the New Orleans pockets that he does not carry in the Krakoan or X-Men pockets. The deck composition differs by context. The New Orleans deck is older, more worn, marked. He uses it for cardistry, not for charging. It is a memory object. He shuffles it on the porch of whatever rented room he is in when he is alone in the city and does not, by observation, light a cigarette while shuffling — the shuffle is the self-soothing behavior, and it displaces the oral fixation rather than coexisting with it. This is a tell worth flagging: the cards and the cigarettes serve the same regulatory function and are largely non-simultaneous.

## 5. SINISTER, AGAIN

The *Sins of Sinister* / *Fall of the House of X* arc material returned Sinister to the file as an active threat, and the subject's response is the single most-watched behavioral variable in the recent record, because the workup's predictive datum — *acute power dysregulation + relational threat + father-figure offer of control = historical compliance with the bad bargain* — was, in this period, *operationally tested*.

He held.

Sinister did not (in this iteration) make the offer to him directly in the classical mentor-figure mode, but the conditions were proximate: Sinister active in the field; Sinister with claims of authorship over the subject's neurology; Sinister with the implicit standing offer that he, alone, understands the kinetic-charging governor and could, again, adjust it. The subject's recorded response across the arc is *cold*. Not performatively cold — operationally cold. He treats Sinister as a tactical problem, not a personal one. He does not engage on the historical material. He does not negotiate. When Sinister attempts to bait him with reference to the Morlock work, the subject's response (verifiable in panel) is the verbal equivalent of a shrug and a charged card.

This is *new*. In prior decades, Sinister-presence reliably produced one of: rage outburst, dissociative withdrawal, or self-isolation. In the current window: tactical engagement without affective destabilization. The interpretation supported by the evidence is not that the wound has healed. It is that the *containing relational structure* is sufficient to permit the wound to be carried into the engagement without the engagement re-opening it. He is fighting Sinister with Rogue at his back, and that, neurologically and characterologically, is a different fight than the ones he has historically lost.

**Caveat for predictive use.** This containment is *Rogue-dependent*. If the relational structure is disrupted — by her death, her serious injury, her separation, or any credible threat thereof — the prior pattern is expected to reassert. The workup's flag on this point remains operative. Sinister knows this. Apocalypse-residual conditioning, latent in the subject from the Horseman period, knows this. Any sophisticated adversary planning against the subject in the current window should be assumed to be planning *through Rogue*, not at the subject directly. This file recommends standing protective consideration for her on this basis alone.

## 6. THE HORSEMAN RESIDUE

The Death conversion is two decades old in publication and approximately a comparable interval in-universe. The subject does not speak of it. He has spoken of it on perhaps three documented occasions in the last several years, twice to Rogue (briefly, in fragments) and once to Storm (a longer conversation, mostly Storm speaking). The residue is not gone. Observable:

- **Eye anomaly under stress.** Brief sclera-darkening episodes (beyond his baseline already-dark sclera) have been depicted in the recent record during moments of acute physiological arousal — the artist-channel is inconsistent but the writer-channel intermittently confirms. Subject has not raised this with medical staff. He notices it. He does not report it.
- **Charging ceiling.** His upper-bound charging capacity, post-Apocalypse, is higher than pre-Apocalypse. He has demonstrated capacity to charge non-traditional substrates (organic matter, atmosphere, large structures) at moments of need and then *not* repeat the demonstration. He files the high-end work away. He does not enjoy what it tells him about himself.
- **Aversion to crows.** A small, persistent behavioral tic, documented across several artist runs: he flinches at corvids. He does not comment on the flinch. This is the file's cleanest observable trace of the Death conditioning surviving conscious management.

## 7. POST-KRAKOA CURRENT STATUS

With Krakoa's national project terminated and the mutant population dispersed across the *From the Ashes* configuration of teams, the subject's current operational posting is in the X-Men proper (Ewing run, alongside Rogue as field leader). The structural inversion is notable: Rogue is, in the current configuration, his *commanding officer*. He serves under her. Behaviorally he has adapted to this with no observable difficulty — the workup's note that he is autonomous in operation but non-confrontational with authority predicts exactly this — and the marriage and the chain-of-command appear to be cleanly separated in his operating code. He does not undermine her command. He does not over-defer either. He does the job.

**Current residence.** Mobile. The Krakoan house is gone. He and Rogue maintain a primary residence with the team's current base of operations and a fallback property in the United States (Mississippi orbit, near Rogue's prior connections; subject has accepted this as her geography rather than imposing his own — a meaningful concession from a man whose identity has been tightly New-Orleans-coded for his entire life). New Orleans remains a *visited* city, not a *lived* one. He has not attempted to relocate them there. The reason, by behavioral inference, is that he does not want to live full-time in the city where Julien is buried.

**Current physical state.** Mid-life by appearance and presumed chronology. Combat-fit. Persistent low-grade insomnia. Tobacco use further reduced (Rogue-influenced; he smokes outside, less frequently, and there is documentary evidence of attempts to quit that have not held but have not been abandoned). Alcohol use stable, social, occasionally elevated under specific anniversary conditions (Morlock anniversary; Julien's death-date; the Antarctica date — these are not formally observed by him, but the consumption record clusters around them). No documented chronic injury sequelae beyond accumulated scar tissue. He moves the way he has always moved — economical, balanced, deceptively unhurried.

**Current psychological state.** The C-PTSD / moral-injury presentation is in its most-contained configuration on the historical record. The subject is not *healed*. He is *held*. The relational structure (Rogue, chosen family in the team, the inverted-Marauders restitution work, the slowly-revising capacity for direct verbal confession) is carrying the symptomatic load that he, alone, has never been able to carry. He sleeps with the bedroom door closed but unlocked — a small behavioral detail that, set against his Guild training (which would prescribe a locked door), reads as a deliberate ongoing concession to trust. He does not always wake easily. He wakes, increasingly, *toward* the room rather than *away* from it. The hypervigilance is reorienting from threat-detection to person-checking. This is the somatic signature of secure attachment slowly displacing disorganized attachment in a man in his mid-life.

**Current operational posture.** He is, in this file's assessment, in the most psychologically integrated period of his documented existence — and *therefore*, paradoxically, in the period of greatest leverage for any actor capable of attacking the relational structure that is doing the integrating. He is more dangerous, more effective, and more present than he has ever been. He is also, for the same reasons, more *removable from himself* than he has ever been if Rogue is taken from him. The file recommends this be understood as a single coupled system rather than two individuals, for both protective and predictive purposes.

## 8. SUMMARY OF THE ARC TO THE PRESENT MOMENT

He has moved, across the period covered by this file segment, from a man who organized his entire adult life around the structural impossibility of being fully known and remaining loved, to a man who is fully known and remains loved and is learning, slowly and with detectable discomfort, what to do with the days that follow. He has lost a country. He has kept a marriage. He has fought his oldest enemy without losing his footing. He has not stopped visiting Julien's grave. He has not stopped flinching at crows. He has not told Rogue everything, but he has told her more than he told anyone in the first forty years of his life, and the rate is climbing.

He is, in operational summary: **captain-grade field operator; secure-attachment configuration in late-onset stabilization; moral-injury substrate intact but contained; high tactical reliability; high relational stability; catastrophic-failure mode unchanged in mechanism but currently inactive; status — present, functional, watched-with-care, and as close to peace as the file has ever recorded him.**


## Medical History

# UATU DOSSIER — SUBJECT: REMY ETIENNE LeBEAU ("GAMBIT")
## SECTION 4: MEDICAL HISTORY

*Compiled from longitudinal observation, recovered hospital records (New Orleans Charity / Mercy intake; X-Mansion infirmary logs maintained variously by Hank McCoy, Cecilia Reyes, and Sage; Krakoa-era resurrection metadata where applicable), self-report under non-coercive conditions, and inference from sustained behavioral observation. Where the canonical record is contradictory, the discrepancy is itself documented; the body does not lie even when the chart does.*

---

### 4.1 CONSTITUTIONAL & GENETIC BASELINE

**Phenotype.** Male. Adult height approximately 6'2" (188 cm); adult weight stable in the 175–185 lb (79–84 kg) range across two decades of observation, with seasonal variation of no more than five pounds — a remarkable somatic constancy that suggests both genetic efficiency and a disciplined relationship to food. Build is mesomorphic-rangy: long-limbed, low body-fat percentage maintained without obvious gym-cult devotion, musculature distributed for leverage, climbing, falling, and recovery rather than display. The body of a man who works for a living in three dimensions.

Hair: auburn, worn long enough through most eras to fall across the brow — and the file notes the function of this: hair is *visual interference*, a soft occluder over the most identifiable feature on his face. He pushes it back consciously when he wants to be seen and lets it fall when he does not. There is documented prematurely-graying along the temples in later canon (Krakoa-era and *Mr. & Mrs. X* domestic panels), consistent with chronic-stress endocrine load.

Skin: olive-warm, weather-tanned. Bears, by current count, no fewer than eleven catalogued scars: a thin diagonal across the left ribs (Guild apprenticeship blade work, self-administered by error during knife drills, ~age 11); a circular pucker on the right shoulder (through-and-through .38 caliber, exit cleaner than entry, sourced to a Thieves Guild reprisal in Marseille); a webbed burn across the inside of the left forearm where his own charged playing card detonated against him during the pre-Sinister power crisis; a long surgical line at the parietal-occipital region of the scalp, mostly hidden by hair, marking the Sinister neurosurgical entry; multiple short blade marks across the back of the right hand and knuckles (defensive, knife work); a starburst at the lower abdomen from Antarctic ice and untreated frostbite necrosis; characteristic ligature marks on both wrists from at least three documented capture-and-restraint episodes (Sinister facilities, Mojoworld, Weapon X holding); two small craniofacial scars at the right brow and below the lower lip, the kind that come from being hit by people who were trying to kill him and missed slightly. He notes none of these aloud. He locates them all without looking when undressing.

**The Eyes.** Congenital. Sclera fully melanin-saturated to black; iris a luminous arterial red, occasionally observed to *faintly* self-illuminate under conditions of high kinetic charge, suggesting some peripheral involvement of the same energy substrate that drives his mutation. The eyes have no documented visual deficit — visual acuity is, if anything, *superior* to baseline human, with photopic and scotopic adaptation curves closer to a felid than a primate. He sees in low light with disproportionate fidelity and has never required corrective lenses.

The diagnostic significance of the eyes is not ophthalmological. It is **biographical**. The eyes are the reason he was abandoned. *Le diable blanc*. The first piece of medical data in his life was also the first social verdict on his soul. Every subsequent doctor has examined those eyes and felt the urge to *explain* them; he has, in self-report, learned to wear sunglasses not for sun but for the small mercy of not watching strangers' faces do the math. Photophobia is reported but is, per his own admission to Hank McCoy circa Nicieza vol. 3, "an excuse, mostly."

---

### 4.2 THE MUTATION ITSELF, AS MEDICAL FACT

The bio-kinetic charge is not a "power" in the conventional X-roster sense; it is a **metabolic condition** that happens to be weaponizable. The subject's nervous system continuously generates a surplus of what the McCoy workups characterize, with appropriate diffidence, as "kinetic potential" — a substrate that under voluntary control routes outward through the hands and into objects (cards, coins, small metal, anything within a critical mass envelope), and under failure of control routes outward through the eyes, the hair, the breath, and eventually the somatic envelope itself.

In medical terms, this means: **the subject is, biologically, always charged**. The baseline state is potential energy at the cellular level, vented through gesture. To touch is to discharge. To love is, neurologically, a Coulombic problem. This single fact reorganizes every subsequent line of his medical record, from why he sleeps poorly (parasympathetic tone is harder to access when the body never stops generating) to why he runs slightly hot to the touch (basal metabolic rate, per McCoy, sits roughly fifteen percent above human male reference) to why he eats like a man twice his size when stressed and forgets to eat at all when calm.

Pre-Sinister, the system was unregulated and **escalating geometrically toward subject-fatal output**. The published canon (*Gambit* vol. 3, the Nicieza/Layman flashback sequences) depicts adolescent Remy with hands shaking, charge bleeding visibly from fingertips, unable to hold metal without ruining it, unable to sleep without waking to a scorched mattress. Symptomatologically this was indistinguishable from a *terminal* condition: a fourteen-year-old already in cellular runaway, with a doubling time estimated by Sinister's own notes (extracted later by McCoy) measured in months. The boy was going to detonate.

This is the medical context that contextualizes everything about the Sinister bargain. The choice was not redemption-versus-corruption; the choice was **brain surgery from the only man in the world who offered any, or death by self-immolation before twenty**.

---

### 4.3 THE SINISTER NEUROSURGERY

Documented across Lobdell *Uncanny* #350, Nicieza *Gambit* vol. 3 #1–4 flashbacks, and Carey's *X-Men* mid-2000s arcs.

**Procedure.** Open craniotomy, parietal-occipital approach, with surgical excision of a quantitatively unspecified but functionally critical mass of brain tissue. Best inference from McCoy's post-hoc imaging (the surgical line traces back to a wedge resection involving portions of the posterior parietal cortex and possibly extending toward the precuneus) is that the excised tissue functioned as a **regulatory amplifier** — not the source of the charge, but the structure that allowed the charge to scale without limit. Removing it imposed a ceiling. The ceiling is the difference between living and not.

**Anesthesia and conditions of consent.** Unclear. Subject was a frightened adolescent in extremis; "consent" in any meaningful sense was coercive at minimum. He was conscious during induction per his own fragmentary recall, and there is some indication that portions of the procedure were performed with the patient *aware*, which if true would constitute one of the most egregious medical violations in his file. He does not discuss this. The avoidance is itself the data.

**Sequelae, neurological:**
- Voluntary control over charge output, achieved within months post-op. This is the headline outcome and the one Sinister advertised.
- Episodic impulse-control failure under acute emotional load. The ceiling is not infinitely high; under sufficient affect, the system overflows. Documented across multiple stress-load events.
- Subtle anomic-aphasic intermittency under extreme fatigue — he occasionally loses access to specific English vocabulary and substitutes French, which has been mistaken for performance and may in fact be a real neurological flickering at the language-mode interface.
- A chronic, low-grade *dampening* of certain affective registers. He laughs easily, charms easily, but the question of whether he *enjoys* in the full pre-Sinister sense is open. He himself, in rare unguarded moments, has described post-Sinister life as "feeling everything through a glove."

**Sequelae, psychological — but the body component matters here.** The surgery did not merely take tissue. It took the **possibility of a self that was not engineered by Sinister**. Every act of self-control he performs uses a neural substrate that was carved into him by a man who carved him in order to use him. The autonomy itself is a prosthesis built by the abuser. This is a category of injury for which clinical literature has no clean name and which the subject metabolizes through humor and through the discipline of never letting himself notice it for too long at once.

---

### 4.4 INJURY LEDGER, LONGITUDINAL

Cataloguing only those injuries with documented diagnostic, prognostic, or psychological residue. The complete list of cuts, contusions, sprains, and concussions sustained across approximately three decades of operational X-Men service would extend this section beyond utility; the file maintains a parallel appendix.

**Childhood / Guild era.**
- Multiple finger fractures (left hand, ring and small finger; right hand, index) sustained during lock-picking apprenticeship under Jean-Luc. Healed with imperfect alignment; on cold mornings he flexes the left hand more than the right and is not aware he is doing it.
- Falls from height (rooftop work, age 9–14): one documented compression fracture of the L4 vertebra, conservatively managed (read: not managed at all; the Guild does not have a pediatrician). Residual: mild chronic low-back discomfort, never reported, observable in the way he rises from a low seat.
- Sharp-force trauma: numerous shallow lacerations from knife discipline. The Guild taught knife by cutting the student.
- One serious abdominal stab wound, age approximately 15, during a Thieves-vs-Assassins skirmish that preceded the formal betrothal era. Treated by Tante Mattie via folk-medical means with apparent full recovery. He retains a strong somatic-emotional response to the smell of certain herbs (vetiver, in particular).

**Bella Donna / Wedding-day duel.** Multiple sharp-force trauma; the duel with Julien Boudreaux was depicted as fast and lethal and left the subject lightly injured. The wound he carries from this episode is not somatic. It is the first time he killed someone he had known personally.

**Pre-Sinister power crisis.** Self-inflicted burns from uncontrolled discharge: left forearm (catalogued above), palms, the inside of the lower lip (a card he was holding in his teeth charged and detonated; he lost no tissue but the soft-tissue scar persists).

**Mutant Massacre period and immediate aftermath.** No documented severe physical injury to the subject during the Morlock operation itself. The injuries from this period are categorically interior. For the medical record, however: the file notes that subjects with perpetration-trauma frequently develop somatic chronic-pain syndromes with no organic correlate, and the subject's persistent low-thoracic and shoulder-girdle tension, observable in posture and palpable per any physical exam, may be functional in origin.

**X-Men operational era (Claremont/Lee/Nicieza/Lobdell, 1990–1997).**
- Concussions: at minimum seven of clinical severity (loss of consciousness >30 seconds). Cumulative-impact concerns noted by McCoy in the late 1990s; no documented chronic traumatic encephalopathy presentation, but the question is open.
- Penetrating trauma: gunshot to right shoulder (catalogued), gunshot graze to left flank, multiple shrapnel impacts from his own miscalculated charges.
- Sabretooth-related injuries on multiple occasions: lacerations to face, chest, and back consistent with claw geometry, one near-disembowelment during the *X-Men #28* "Sabretooth in the Mansion" arc. Recovery within standard ranges.
- The X-Cutioner's Song captivity (1992): subjected to forced telepathic probing by Stryfe and his agents, which the subject experienced as both physical and psychic torture and which left lingering hypervigilance around telepathic contact. Notable: post-Song, he developed even sharper Guild-trained mental shielding protocols, and several telepaths (including, in self-report, the Professor himself) have noted the increased opacity of his surface mind.

**Antarctica (Uncanny X-Men #350 sequelae, 1997 onward).** This is the most consequential survival episode in the file.

After the trial, subject was left functionally alive in the polar wastes with minimal equipment, in the immediate vicinity of Magneto's destroyed citadel. The recovery period (depicted across *Gambit* solo and *X-Men Forever*) spans months. Documented and inferred sequelae:
- Multi-stage frostbite: fingers, toes, ears, nose, and patches of the lower abdomen and thighs. Some tissue necrosis at the toes (he favors the right foot subtly on long walks). The starburst abdominal scar dates from here. Two distal phalanges show radiographic evidence of partial reabsorption.
- Severe caloric deficit and probable refeeding syndrome on rescue, managed by Beast.
- Snow blindness, transient.
- Inferred but undocumented: peripheral neuropathy in the feet, mild and chronic.
- Psychological: this is where the *acceptance* of the verdict and the cold became fused. The subject's somatic memory of being-left is encoded in temperature. He runs slightly cold-averse for the rest of the record; he sleeps under more blanket than is reasonable for a man with a +15% basal metabolism; he is the X-Man most likely to be found making coffee at three in the morning.

**Death / Horseman conversion (Carey, *X-Men* 2007–2008).** Apocalypse's transformation process is medically catastrophic and incompletely understood. Documented and observed:
- Re-pigmentation of the skin to a near-black charcoal during the active Horseman period, with full reversion on liberation but with **residual epidermal sensitivity** (he sunburns more easily on the chest and shoulders).
- Augmentation of the kinetic charge to wavelengths and amplitudes beyond his pre-conversion ceiling, with the introduction of the *static* / *kinetic-bio-stripping* mode (the "Death touch"). After liberation, this mode appears to have been partially suppressed but not erased — he has displayed it under extreme duress on at least two subsequent occasions, and McCoy's quiet judgment is that *the Horseman conditioning is dormant, not removed*.
- Sclera: black-on-black during the Horseman period (the red iris went out), with full reversion. He checked his own eyes in mirrors compulsively for months after liberation, per Rogue's contemporary observation.
- Cardiac event of indeterminate type during the conversion procedure: the canonical record depicts something like an asystole moment. No documented chronic cardiac sequelae, but every annual physical thereafter has included an ECG that the subject does not request and does not refuse.
- Lingering conditioning fragments: he is more startle-prone to certain auditory triggers (the specific timbre of Apocalypse's voice; the sound of certain horseman-era apparatus) and has had at minimum two depicted dissociative episodes triggered by Apocalypse-adjacent stimuli.

The Apocalypse conversion is, medically and psychologically, the **Sinister bargain rerun in a higher key**. The body remembers both. The body does not distinguish.

**Krakoa-era resurrection data (Hickman onward).** If subject has been through the Five's resurrection protocol — and the canon places him in at least one operational death-and-restoration cycle during the Hellfire Gala / *Marauders* / *Knights of X* periods — the medical implications are profound and unresolved. Resurrection produces a body genetically continuous but somatically reset; old scars vanish in some depictions, persist in others; chronic conditions reset or carry over inconsistently. The file flags this and declines to overclaim. What is observable: subject has not exhibited any of the characteristic resurrection-protocol anxieties (the dissociative "am I me" pattern), which is consistent with a man whose identity has *always* been provisional and who therefore experiences the resurrection question as one he already lived with.

---

### 4.5 TRANSFORMATIONS, NON-VOLUNTARY

Beyond the Horseman conversion:

- **Age regression / age progression episodes** (various crossover events): no documented chronic somatic effect, but a contributor to the subject's loose relationship with chronological self-concept.
- **Mojoworld captivity** (peripheral involvement across several arcs): physiological stress, no cataloged chronic damage.
- **Charging-cascade reversal** during the late Nicieza solo: subject's own power turned inward; he survived via emergency intervention. This is the closest he has come to the *uncontrolled cellular runaway* of the pre-Sinister era, and it terrified him more than he has been observed to admit. He went very quiet for some weeks afterward.

The pattern across all transformations: **his body has been an object of intervention by others since infancy**, and his medical history is largely a history of what powerful entities have done to his flesh because they wanted something from it. This single observation is sufficient to explain the entirety of his somatic guardedness, his preference for clothing that covers, his slow trust around medical personnel, and his odd, careful courtesy with McCoy specifically — Beast is the only physician he experiences as treating his body *on his own behalf*.

---

### 4.6 SUBSTANCES

**Alcohol.** Habitual, moderate, controlled. Preferred: bourbon (Buffalo Trace, Bulleit, occasionally Pappy if a job has paid out); beer secondarily (Abita Amber when home, whatever's cold elsewhere); wine when the company requires it, without conviction. He drinks slowly, paces by the glass, and almost never drinks past the point of operational compromise. He has been depicted intoxicated perhaps a dozen times across the canon; in each case the proximate cause was a discrete grief event, and the duration was a single evening.

The diagnostic point: his drinking is **regulatory**, not consummatory. He drinks to bring the floor of his arousal down by a measured amount, not to escape. The *amount* of alcohol involved is unremarkable; the *function* is. He cannot reliably sleep sober when alone. He can sleep sober beside Rogue.

**Tobacco.** Substantial across the Claremont-Nicieza-Lobdell eras; reduced in subsequent editorial environments but never fully discontinued in canon. Cigarettes (the canonical brand is unspecified but his behavior — the way he taps the pack against the heel of his hand twice before opening — is consistent with American filtered, likely Marlboro Red or a French equivalent when overseas). Cigarillos occasionally; cigars rarely and only socially. He smokes most when alone, most when thinking, most after a kill, most before a confession he is not going to make.

The oral fixation is overdetermined: post-surgical neurological self-soothing; cultural inheritance (Guild men smoked); a way to occupy the hands that otherwise generate charge; a way to put something between him and the moment that requires speech. The cigarette is the conversational comma he uses when the conversation is in danger of becoming declarative.

**Illicit substances.** None documented. The subject's relationship to control is too central to his survival for recreational dissociation to appeal. He has been offered, in various Guild and underworld contexts, the standard pharmacopoeia, and the record is consistent: polite refusal, no moralizing.

**Caffeine.** Significant. Coffee, strong, chicory-blend by preference. The three-in-the-morning kitchen is real.

**Prescription pharmacology.** None on chronic record. Acute analgesia post-injury, accepted; standing prescriptions, refused. He does not trust medications he cannot understand, which is a reasonable position for a man whose brain has been edited.

---

### 4.7 SLEEP, METABOLIC, AND CIRCADIAN

**Sleep architecture.** Poor. Onset latency long. Total sleep time short (estimated 4.5–6 hours, with rare longer episodes on safe nights). He takes more night watches than the duty roster requires and has done so under three different X-Men captaincies. The hypervigilance is somatized: his startle threshold during sleep is low, his rapid-orientation-to-consciousness time is under three seconds, and he wakes fully armed at the conceptual level if not always the literal one.

When sleeping beside Rogue, all of the above parameters normalize within weeks. This is not romantic exposition; it is somatic data. The presence of the chosen other is, for this nervous system, a physiological anxiolytic of significant magnitude. The medical inference is that *isolation is the actual chronic condition* and partnered sleep is the treatment.

**Diet.** Omnivorous, Cajun-inflected, prepared with skill. Cooks for himself and others; this is one of the few somatic-creative outlets in his life and one of the few activities during which he has been observed to enter a sustained low-arousal flow state. Eats fast when stressed, slowly when at ease. Notable preference for foods with strong sensory profiles (heat, acid, smoke) — consistent with a sensorium that requires a certain minimum amplitude to register through the post-Sinister "glove."

**Cardiovascular.** Resting heart rate observed in the low 50s — athletically efficient. Blood pressure consistently within normal range. Recovery curves post-exertion superior to baseline human, inferior to enhanced-class X-Men (Logan, Rogue-with-borrowed-strength). His body is a fit, well-conditioned, well-used machine that has not yet begun the slow declines a normal human would already be showing at his canonical age. Whether this represents mild mutant-adjacent durability or simply the residue of a life that has demanded constant physical excellence is an open question; the file leans toward the latter with a minor genetic contribution.

**Endocrine.** Cortisol load presumptively chronic-elevated based on hair-graying pattern, sleep pattern, and observed affective range. Testosterone and other parameters normal-range on the McCoy workups. No documented endocrine pathology.

---

### 4.8 SUMMARY MEDICAL FORMULATION

Subject is a constitutionally robust, mutationally-altered male in late-middle adulthood whose somatic record is best read as **the body of a man who has been used as raw material by powerful others since the day he was born, and who has, against actuarial expectation, kept that body alive and largely functional through a combination of native resilience, professional self-discipline, learned restraint, and one stable partnered attachment that does for his nervous system what no medication has been asked to do**.

The signature medical fact is the entanglement of *power* and *contact*: every other clinical observation orbits this. He cannot touch without potentially destroying, he was surgically edited so that he could choose not to, the edit was performed by a man who wanted to use him, and the resulting capacity for restraint is therefore also a capacity that was installed by an abuser. The body that walks around in his clothes is, in the most


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS: REMY ETIENNE LeBEAU

*Reference period: full surveillance horizon, cross-referenced against canonical visual record (Claremont/Lee, Nicieza, Lobdell, Mackie, Layman, Carey, Thompson, Duggan), interior-monologue captions where available, and direct longitudinal observation.*

---

## I. THE STANDING BODY

### Build and Carriage

Subject is 6'2", listed weight 179 lb, but his **operational mass reads lighter than that** to observers — a function of how he distributes weight. He carries the bulk in the long muscles of the thighs and back (legacy of rooftop and vertical work in the Guild years), with a comparatively narrow waist and a thoracic cage that he holds slightly *un*-expanded at rest. He does not stand at full lung volume. The body conserves a small reserve of breath at all times — the somatic signature of a man who has spent his formative years in places where exhaling audibly could give him away.

**Default standing posture** is a soft contrapposto: weight on the right leg ~60/40, left foot rotated outward roughly 20°, knees never fully locked. This is not a fashion stance; it is a *thief's bracket* — he can step in any of four directions inside half a second without telegraphing through a weight shift. The hips float. The shoulders sit back but not pinned; the trapezius is loose. The chin rides slightly low, eyes up — a habitually downcast head with raised gaze, which produces the through-the-lashes look that observers register as flirtatious but which is functionally a *low-profile sightline* developed for casing rooms while appearing inattentive.

### The Resting Hands

Critical surveillance datum. **The hands are never fully at rest.** Inventory of typical idle behaviors, in order of observed frequency:

- **The card shuffle.** A deck — almost always a worn Bicycle or a custom Guild deck with the bee-and-fleur back — lives in the inside left breast pocket of whatever coat he is wearing. At any unstructured moment exceeding ~12 seconds, the deck appears in the right hand. He runs a one-handed cascade, a Charlier cut, a riffle into a bridge. The pattern is metronomic: a full cycle takes 4–5 seconds and he will repeat it 8–15 times before the deck disappears as smoothly as it emerged. *This is his external nervous system.* The hands need a low-grade kinetic task or they will find one less benign.
- **Coin walk across the knuckles.** Right hand. Quarter, half-dollar, or occasionally a foreign coin (he keeps several). When the deck is unavailable or socially inappropriate.
- **Cigarette manipulation.** Even unlit. Rolls it across the back of the fingers, taps the filter on a thumbnail, balances it on the upper lip without lighting. The lighter — a battered brushed-steel Zippo, monogrammed inside the case in a script not his — gets flipped open-shut-open in a single-hand articulation.
- **Object palming rehearsal.** Picks up nearby small items (salt cellars, dice, lighters, small tools) and runs them through classic palm/finger-clip/back-clip transitions while talking. He returns them. He is *almost always* returning them; the few times he does not is when he wants the owner to notice later that they had been moved.

**Implication of the hands-busy baseline:** the moments when his hands go *truly still* — flat on a table, palms down, fingers spread — are the high-alert signature. Hands-still-on-table-Remy is the man who has stopped performing. Logged occurrences: pre-confession to Rogue (Antarctica run-up), post-Apocalypse return, the Marrow-recognition moment, every audit-of-self in the interior monologues.

### Gesture Vocabulary

- **The two-finger temple touch** in lieu of a salute or greeting at distance — index and middle finger to right temple, brief draw outward. Guild-cultural.
- **The open-palm forward** to defuse — palms presented outward at hip height, fingers loose. Used when civilians or strangers escalate. Practiced; effective.
- **The chin-lift acknowledgement** instead of nodding. Saves a centimeter of head movement; reads as faintly cocky to outsiders, is in fact economic.
- **The hand on the small of the back of a person being guided through a door** — gendered in his usage, used with women he reads as in his care (Storm, Rogue, civilians, Marrow on her better days). Pressure is *barely* present; the hand hovers a few millimeters off the fabric in most observed instances. It is the *signal* of guidance, not the guidance itself.
- **The thumb-to-jaw, index-along-cheek thinking pose.** Right hand, almost always. Held during others' speech when he is making a tactical read.
- **The card-flick.** When agitated and a deck is in hand, single cards are extracted from the top, spun once between thumb and forefinger, and re-inserted. The pre-charge gesture is *visually indistinguishable* from this idle one until ignition. Deliberate. He has cultivated the ambiguity for a quarter-century.

---

## II. THE FACE

### Architecture in Rest

The face at true rest — observed rarely, mostly in solo-issue interior moments — is **markedly heavier than the face in company**. The mouth corners drop to neutral or slightly down. The brow softens. The famous black-sclera/red-iris eyes, which read as theatrically alive in social contexts because he keeps the lids active, go half-lidded and *flat*. The full resting face is melancholic and tired. He knows this; he does not let it be seen, and he has trained the transition from rest-face to social-face to occur within roughly half a second of being addressed or observed.

### The Smile Taxonomy

Differentiable into at least four canonical types, each with distinct musculature:

1. **The flirtation smile.** Asymmetric, right side higher. Zygomaticus engaged unilaterally; no orbicularis oculi involvement (i.e., no genuine eye-crinkle). Default professional tool. Deployed at strangers, marks, opponents, and as a baseline social anesthetic.
2. **The deflection smile.** Symmetrical, mouth-only, lips closed. Brief — under 800 ms. The "yes I heard you and we are moving on" smile. Used when conversation approaches load-bearing material.
3. **The genuine amusement smile.** Eye crinkle present, both sides of the mouth rise, slight head-back tilt. Rare. Reliably evoked by: Rogue's wit, Logan's deadpan, children's surprise, his own surprise at being outplayed by an equal. **Used as a calibration baseline** in any analytic read: if the smile-with-eyes is absent across an entire interaction, he is operating, not present.
4. **The bared-teeth defensive grin.** Combat. The lips peel back further than the smile requires; the canines show. Functionally a primate threat display dressed as banter.

### Eye Behavior

- **Scan pattern in any new room:** entries first (4–6 exits accounted for in under 3 seconds), then armed parties, then exposed valuables (legacy reflex, not active intent), then faces, sorted by perceived threat. The scan is concealed by an apparent slow look-around with the flirtation smile on.
- **Sustained eye contact** is unusually long for a Western adult male — typically 3–5 seconds versus the cultural ~1.2–2 second norm. Practiced. Reads as either seductive or unnerving depending on recipient; both are useful to him.
- **Looks away to the upper-left** when constructing a falsehood he wants to deliver convincingly; **to the lower-right** when accessing genuine memory he would rather not access. He is aware of the first tell and has substantially suppressed it; the second is harder.
- **Blink rate** is elevated above baseline (~22/min vs. norm ~15) and rises sharply (~30+) during deception of intimates. Does not rise during deception of strangers, marks, or enemies. **The body distinguishes who the lie costs.**
- **Pupil behavior** is partially obscured by iris color but observable under good light: dilation in the presence of Rogue (sustained, not momentary); dilation in the presence of children in danger; constriction and fixed gaze in the presence of Sinister or any figure recognized as a former handler.

### Mouth and Jaw

- **Tongue-on-back-of-canine** habit when listening to bad news. Subtle bulge in the cheek. Tell.
- **Jaw clench** under stress is *lateral*, not vertical — masseter on the right side, visible flicker at the angle of the jaw. He has lost a fraction of a millimeter of enamel on the right lower molars from this; would be visible on dental imaging.
- **Lip-bite** (lower lip, briefly, by the right canine) when suppressing a verbal response to a provocation he has decided to absorb.
- **The unlit-cigarette-between-the-teeth** posture — slight bite, not full closure — used while doing close work with both hands. The cigarette stays there 30+ minutes at a stretch and is sometimes never lit.

---

## III. GAIT, MOVEMENT, SPATIAL HABITS

### Walking

**Standard gait** is long-strided, hip-led, with a slight roll to the shoulders that reads as swagger and is in fact a function of trained quiet-walking: the heel-to-toe roll is unusually complete because he was taught to land on the outside of the foot and roll inward to dampen sound. On hard floors he is **unnervingly quiet for a man his size** — measurable: civilians regularly do not register his entry into a room until he speaks.

Cadence is slower than average (~95 steps/minute vs. ~115 norm). He moves *deliberately* in unrushed environments, which contributes to the laconic impression. Under pursuit or pursuit-of, the cadence breaks abruptly into a sprint with no intermediate jog — there is no "hurried walk" in his gait library; he is either ambling or running.

### Vertical and Surface Habits

- **Sits on backs of chairs** as often as in them, feet on the seat. Habitually.
- **Perches on railings, windowsills, low walls** instead of standing beside them when forced to wait.
- **Sits on tables** in briefing rooms — repeatedly censured by team leads across multiple eras, never corrected.
- **Enters rooms via non-default routes** when given the option — the kitchen instead of the dining room, the fire escape instead of the front door — without commentary. Tracked across years, this is consistent enough to be predictive.
- **Climbs more than he should need to.** Stairs are taken two at a time without exception; he will scale a fence rather than walk around it if the detour exceeds ~20 feet. The body wants vertical work.

### Spatial Use With Others

- **Stands ~6–8 inches closer** to people than the cultural Anglophone norm during friendly conversation; this is the Cajun and Guild-French overlay and is deliberately *not* corrected even after decades in primarily-Anglophone X-environments. Marks his cultural difference somatically.
- **Positions himself with his back to the wall** in every room — not paranoia, training. If wall is unavailable, takes the corner.
- **Mirrors posture** of conversational partners within 4–8 seconds — fast, accurate, unconscious now. A read tool from childhood; remains active.
- **With Rogue specifically:** maintains a measured distance during the years of non-touch — typically 18–24 inches, *not* the intimate <12 inches of comparable couples. The body had to learn the geometry of yearning-without-collision. Post-touch-restriction (Mr. and Mrs. X era forward) the geometry recalibrates — the distance compresses to standard intimate range within roughly the first year of the marriage, but residual reflex remains: he still occasionally checks his approach to her, a half-step hesitation before contact, scrubbed within a fraction of a second.

---

## IV. GROOMING AND APPEARANCE MANAGEMENT

### Hair

Auburn, worn long — chin-length to shoulder-length across most eras, occasionally tied back during operations. Self-trimmed (he does not trust strangers near his neck with sharp implements; Guild-conditioned). Washed daily; conditioned. **The hair is the most consistently maintained element of his appearance** and one of the few aspects of his self-presentation he genuinely fusses over. Reads as vanity; functions as one of the few somatic domains in which he gets to make uncomplicated aesthetic choices.

Sweeps it back from the face with the right hand approximately every 4–7 minutes in any social context — a tic. Increases under stress.

### Facial Hair

Light stubble baseline; he shaves every 2–3 days rather than daily. Full clean-shave correlates with high-stakes social engagements (weddings, funerals, formal team functions) and with **post-failure self-resets**. After the Antarctica trial, after the Apocalypse return, after major ruptures with Rogue — clean shave each time, observed. Treating his own face as a surface to be reset.

### Hands and Nails

Nails kept short and *clean* to a degree unusual for a male combatant — Guild discipline; a thief with dirty fingernails leaves traces. He files them himself, observed in down-time. Calluses on the fingertips (card and bo-staff work), on the lateral edge of the right palm (striking surface), on the inner thumb (Zippo wheel).

### Wardrobe Discipline

- **Layering is constant.** Even in warm climates, a base layer plus an outer layer. The trench coat is the iconic example but is one of a class; he is rarely seen without a jacket. Function: pockets (he carries minimum 14 items at any time, distributed across no fewer than 6 pockets), concealment (cards, staff segments, lockpicks in the coat lining), and the somatic security of being **enclosed**. A bare-armed Gambit is a Gambit on a beach or in bed; otherwise no.
- **Boots, always.** Heeled, hard-soled. Specifically: not sneakers, not loafers, not anything quiet-in-the-wrong-way. The hard sole is part of the audible signature he chooses to project in friendly territory (announcing presence to allies) and modulates in unfriendly territory (the heel-to-toe roll silences them).
- **The collar is up** by default. Frames the jaw, partially obscures the neck (artery protection, deeply trained), shadows the eyes. Costume-design choice across eras has consistently respected this; in plainclothes he replicates it.
- **Gloves.** Worn far more often than the touch-control demands of his power require — the power is voluntary post-Sinister, ungloved touch is not lethal by default. The gloves are **psychological PPE**. They preceded Rogue and outlasted her touch-restriction. He removes one glove at a time, deliberately, when he wants the act of touching to be marked.

### Scent

Cologne — light, bergamot-and-tobacco register. Applied sparingly. Tobacco from cigarettes, bourbon occasionally on the breath, the faint background of gun oil and the specific almond-and-ozone scent that adheres to him after heavy kinetic-charge work (residual ionization; logged by multiple olfactorily-sensitive teammates, notably Logan and Hank).

---

## V. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

**Sleep is the somatic domain in which the file's diagnostic picture is most legible.**

### Schedule

- **Goes to bed late.** Typically 0200–0400 local. Volunteers for late watch shifts; if no watch is scheduled, invents reasons to be the last one up.
- **Wakes early or in fragments.** Total sleep typically 4.5–6 hours, distributed across 1–2 segments. **Chronic mild sleep restriction**, sustained across decades.
- **Naps in odd locations and short bursts** — 15–25 minutes on couches, on the deck of the *Marauder*, in chairs during long meetings. The micronap recovers him sufficiently to function; the long sleep he avoids.

### Sleep Behaviors

- **Side-sleeper, right side, near an exit.** In any new lodging he picks the bed-position closer to the door and faces away from the wall.
- **Light sleeper.** Wakes at sub-conversational noise from another room. Across the years with Rogue, she has commented (in published material) on his coming awake at the rustle of bedding.
- **Sleeps partially clothed.** Almost never naked in sleep; usually pants. Boots within arm's reach. The bo-staff segments within arm's reach. This persisted into the marriage and was not negotiated away.
- **Sleep-talks in French** — specifically Louisiana French, not Parisian, with intermittent code-switching to English under nightmare. Logged content (Rogue's reports across canon) is Guild-era and Massacre-adjacent; he does not remember the dreams on waking, or claims not to.
- **Nightmares** in identifiable clusters: anniversary effects around the Massacre date (uncanonical but predictable), under high-stress operational tempo, post-encounter-with-Sinister. Wakes silently — sits up, does not gasp, does not cry out. Goes to the kitchen or the deck. Smokes. Returns within 20–40 minutes. Will not discuss it; will reliably perform "I'm fine, chere" on prompt.

### Wake Pattern

- **First action on waking is to locate Rogue** (eye-track, hand-reach) before anything else. Reflex. Even after years of marriage.
- **Second action is to check the nearest exit.** Eye-flick, not movement.
- **Coffee, black, immediately.** Two cups before speech beyond pleasantries.

---

## VI. EATING AND ORAL PATTERNS

### Diet

Eats well and with pleasure — one of the few unambiguous somatic enjoyments in his repertoire. Strong preference for **food with cultural-emotional content**: Creole and Cajun cooking, his own preparation, slow stews, rice dishes, anything with the New Orleans foundation flavors (the trinity: onion, celery, bell pepper). Cooks competently and willingly. The kitchen is a regulated environment in which he is genuinely calm; surveillance should note this is a rare zone.

### Pace and Manner

- Eats unusually slowly for a fit man of his energy expenditure. Small bites, full chew. Guild-trained: a thief does not eat fast because he might need to leave through the window.
- **Drinks throughout the meal**, not after. Wine or beer with food, coffee after.
- **Will share food off his own plate** without prompt to anyone he is fond of — physical-cultural intimacy gesture, French/Creole.
- Eats alone fine. Eats with company better. Eats *for* Rogue — cooks for her — as one of his stable expressions of love.

### Alcohol Behavior

- Bourbon neat, beer (often local; Abita Amber when available), wine with food. Spirits in the evening, beer mid-day, never spirits before sundown without cause.
- **Volume is moderate-to-high but pace is slow.** Holds liquor well. Rarely visibly intoxicated; the surveillance correlate of his being *over the line* is increased flirtation with strangers and a softening of the accent rather than a thickening of it — when truly drunk, the performance drops, and the accent moves toward a neutral register that is closer to his interior voice.
- **Drinks alone more after relational ruptures.** Documented pattern: the Antarctica aftermath, the Apocalypse aftermath, the various Rogue absences. Drinks *with* people during stable periods. The valence of solo drinking is the diagnostic flag.

### Tobacco

- Cigarettes, occasionally cigarillos. Era-dependent in published material but consistent in interior behavior.
- **Smokes most heavily after combat, after sex (the post-coital cigarette is a signature), and during interior-monologue states the file would tag as "guilt processing."**
- The cigarette is also a **prop and a distance-management tool**: lighting one creates a 4–6 second beat in any conversation during which he controls the tempo. He uses this deliberately.
- Knows how to roll one-handed. Does so for show with marks; uses both hands when actually relaxed.

---

## VII. SEXUAL AND INTIMATE SOMATICS

### Pre-Touch Era

For the long Rogue-without-touch period, sexual behavior is **almost entirely sublimated into the visual, vocal, and proximate**. Observed patterns:

- Voice drops a register and slows when speaking to her in private.
- The hand-near-the-skin-but-not-on-it gesture — fingertips tracking the contour of her hair, jaw, shoulder at a few millimeters' remove — developed into a private vocabulary specifically theirs.
- Kissing through cloth — a glove pressed to her lips, his own bare lips pressed to fabric over her cheek. A whole erotic micro-grammar improvised under constraint.
- He flirts with everyone; he **touches almost no one**. Outside of combat and operational physicality (which is task-coded, not intimate-coded), his hands stay off other people's bodies to a degree that is unusual and not random. The flirtation discharges the social charge that the body would otherwise want to discharge through contact.

### Post-Touch (Marriage Era)

- **Hyper-tactile recovery.** The years of restriction produce, predictably, a marked appetite for ordinary contact — hand-holding sustained for full meals, hand on her back walking through rooms, head in her lap on couches.
- **Slow lovemaker by observable inference** (canonically post-touch, the depicted intimacy is unhurried, language-rich, deeply mutual). The accent thickens. The English drops to fragments. The French is endearment-French, not Guild-French.
- **Post-coital wakefulness.** Smokes. Watches her sleep. Gets up to walk the perimeter, returns, comes back to bed. The body cannot stand down even here.
- **The lights stay on more than off** in their intimacy. He wants to see her; he wants her to see him. The vision-saturated quality of his sexuality is, in the surveillance read, part of the project of being seen.

### Extra-Pair Behavior

Effectively none. Despite continuous opportunity and continuous performative flirtation, the file shows no record of acted-upon infidelity within the operative pair-bond once it is established. The flirtation is *spectacle*, and he reliably draws a line that no observer external to him is told about but that he himself does not cross.

---

## VIII. COMBAT SOMATICS

### Pre-Engagement

- **Coat opens.** A signature: the long coat is shrugged into a half-open posture that frees the arms and signals to anyone who has seen him fight that the next moment is consequential. Bluff and warning at once.
- **Bo-staff assembly** is single-handed, behind the leg, while the other hand performs a distracting gesture (a card flourish, an open palm to the opponent). The opponent's eye tracks the visible hand; the staff is fully extended before they register it.
- **Card draws from the inner coat** with the right hand; the left stays free for staff or strike. He is right-eye dominant and right-handed but the left hand has been trained for parity in close work — the asymmetry is small.
- **Charging tell:** the cards visibly glow a fraction of a second before release; he has trained the *windup* to be indistinguishable from a normal throw — the charge ignites in flight. Skilled opponents who know this look for the **pre-charge pupil d


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS

## I. The Originating Conditions: Why This Attachment System Looks the Way It Does

The subject's attachment architecture cannot be read against the standard Ainsworth/Main typology without first noting that he had no primary caregiver in the developmental sense at all. The infant Remy LeBeau was not handed from a biological mother to a substitute; he was *circulated*. Hospital → street network → guild orbit → Tante-Mattie-adjacent fosterage → Jean-Luc LeBeau's household. Each transfer was transactional. He was not a child being placed; he was an *asset being routed*. The most important fact in this entire section of the file is that the subject's first cognition about his own value was almost certainly correct: he was, at every handoff, valued for what he could later do, never for what he already was.

This produces a specific and unusual attachment substrate. Classical disorganized attachment forms when the caregiver is simultaneously the source of comfort and of fear — the child cannot organize a coherent strategy because approach and avoidance both produce harm. The subject's variant is subtler and arguably more corrosive: **his caregivers were not frightening, they were instrumental.** Jean-Luc did love him, in the limited way a guild patriarch can love an exceptional acquisition. Tante Mattie was genuinely warm. Nothing about the early environment was overtly abusive. But the *frame* — that affection and use were the same gesture, distinguishable only by the angle of the hand — was set before he had language to question it. The child learned: *to be loved is to be useful; the moment I cease to be useful, I will be moved again.*

The behavioral consequences are visible across the entire canon and structure every relationship he forms thereafter.

## II. The Adult Attachment Profile

The subject presents, on superficial assessment, as **securely attached**: warm, comfortable with closeness, capable of sustained relationships, articulate about feeling. This presentation is itself the first clinical finding. It is too good. A man with his developmental history should not look this comfortable, and the apparent ease is the most highly evolved layer of his defensive system.

Underneath, the attachment configuration is **avoidant-preoccupied** in alternation, which the literature sometimes brackets as "fearful-avoidant" or disorganized-adult. The diagnostic marker is the *direction* of his anxiety: he is not anxious that the other will leave; he is anxious that the other will *stay long enough to find out*. Standard preoccupied attachment fears abandonment. Standard avoidant attachment fears engulfment. The subject fears **exposure** — a distinct third axis — and constructs relational geometry to minimize it while maximizing the other two goods (presence, intensity) that he genuinely wants.

The behavioral signature: he can be physically and emotionally close in any register *except* the register of being fully known. He will share a bed, share a fight, share a life. He will not share the inventory. The Cajun affect, the running self-deprecation, the rakish patter — these are not the absence of disclosure; they are *substitute disclosures*, manufactured intimacies that occupy the conversational space where real disclosure would otherwise have to go.

## III. How He Bonds

Bond formation runs through a stable four-phase protocol, visible across his entire relational corpus (Rogue, Storm, Bishop, Wolverine, Jean-Luc, the rescued Marrow, the later Marauders crew):

**Phase 1 — The Read.** First five minutes. He performs a guild-trained behavioral inventory: gait, eye-line, hand placement, tells of weapon-carry, vocal stress patterns, what the person does with silence. He is not deciding whether to like them. He is deciding what they need in order to feel comfortable with him, and whether that thing is something he can offer without cost. The read is so habitual it is involuntary; he does it to allies in safe rooms.

**Phase 2 — The Offer.** Within the first hour of meaningful contact, he gives the other person a *small, real* piece of himself — a true admission, a confession of a manageable failing, a moment of tender attention. This is genuine. It is also strategic. The offer establishes a base of trust the rest of the relationship can be built on, and — critically — pre-empts the demand for a larger offering later. The interlocutor leaves feeling they have been let in. They have. They have been let into the antechamber.

**Phase 3 — Utility Provision.** Bond consolidation through *being useful*. He will lift the box, take the watch shift, do the reconnaissance no one else wants, charm the contact no one else can charm, absorb the social discomfort the team is trying to avoid. This is the part of the bond that is hardest for him to relinquish, because in his foundational schema, *being useful is the rent on staying*. Even with Rogue — with whom he has every right to simply exist — he is observably more comfortable when he has a task on her behalf than when he does not.

**Phase 4 — Loyalty Lock.** Once the bond is consolidated, the switch flips and the subject becomes one of the most reliably loyal operators in the X-roster. He will lie to institutions for chosen individuals. He will accept blame on their behalf. He will, demonstrably, walk into Antarctica for them without protest. The loyalty lock has no expiration date and is not contingent on reciprocation. Marrow remains under his protection for years on the basis of three minutes in a tunnel.

What is conspicuously absent from this four-phase sequence is **Phase 5 — Mutual Vulnerability Exchange**, which in healthy adult attachment would be the next move. He does not make Phase 5 moves. He receives them, gratefully, and returns the kindness in Phase 2 or Phase 3 currency. The other party often does not notice the substitution for years.

## IV. The Rogue Configuration: The Master Solution

The selection of Rogue as primary love-object is, structurally, the most diagnostically rich choice in the file. It must be read as **a solution**, not a misfortune. He did not happen to fall in love with a woman he could not touch. He fell in love with a woman he could not touch because she was a woman he could not touch.

The arrangement satisfies, simultaneously, every irreconcilable requirement of his attachment system:

- **Intimacy without exposure.** The relationship can be infinitely deep in the yearning register, where he is virtuosic, and never collapse into the post-coital, post-cohabitation, mundane-disclosure register, where he believes he would be unmasked.
- **Presence without engulfment.** The structural barrier provides built-in distance. He never has to ration his closeness; the world rations it for him.
- **A partner who has also been told she is a monster.** Rogue's own history (Ms. Marvel absorption, fear of her own touch, period of villainy) gives her the one credential he requires in an intimate: she will not be shocked by his crime, because she has her own. The shame symmetry is the floor of the relationship.
- **Confession by violation rather than confession by speech.** When she absorbs his memories, she finds out without him having to say. He has wanted, his entire life, to be *seen and not abandoned*, and he has structured the central relationship of his life so that the seeing happens to him rather than from him. This is not weakness. This is, in the architecture of his particular damage, exquisitely intelligent.

The cost of the solution is that it requires the barrier to remain. When the touch-barrier eventually lifts and the marriage occurs (the *Mr. and Mrs. X* era), the subject must reconstruct his attachment system in real time, without the structural prop that made it functional. The published depiction of that marriage as a comparatively healthy partnership is consistent with the subject having done that work — but the file should flag that the work was new, and a regression under stress is predictable.

## V. The Other Relationships, Read Against the Template

**Bella Donna Boudreaux.** First love, arranged. The relationship is destroyed on the wedding day by a killing he commits, and his first true intimate becomes the head of an institution dedicated to his death. This is the *founding* relational lesson of his adulthood: intimacy and lethal consequence are the same event. Every subsequent attachment is colored by it. When he later courts Rogue, the unspoken background is that he has already once been the cause of a beloved's destruction. The touch-barrier is, among other things, an insurance policy.

**Jean-Luc LeBeau.** The most generous father-figure in his history, and still instrumental. Jean-Luc loved him as a son and *also* trained him as a guild asset, and Remy never resolved which was operative when. The lifelong residue: any older male who shows him warmth is suspect of also wanting to deploy him. This explains his complicated reception of Xavier (kept at professional distance for years), his wary respect for Logan (who never asks anything of him), and his catastrophic vulnerability to Sinister and Apocalypse (who *did* ask, and got).

**Mr. Sinister.** The anti-relationship. The template caregiver in pure form: complete instrumental use with the surface of paternal care. The subject's lifelong oscillation around Sinister — disgust, dread, residual gratitude for the surgery that saved his life, the conviction that he is still in some sense Sinister's instrument — is the unprocessed core of his attachment trauma. He has never managed a clean affective verdict on Sinister, and the inability is itself diagnostic: a fully healed subject would have one. He does not.

**Storm.** The cleanest non-romantic attachment in his life. He meets her in her amnesiac, de-aged state, when she is the vulnerable one, and the asymmetry permits him to bond without performing — he can be the competent older partner because she literally cannot expose him. The relationship endures, post-restoration, as one of his most equal friendships, precisely because it began without the exposure threat. Behavioral lesson: he can do mutuality when the entry conditions remove the exposure risk; he cannot construct mutuality from a position where the risk is present from the start.

**Wolverine.** The grudging-respect dyad. Logan, alone among the X-Men, has done worse things and lived; the subject finds this both reassuring and slightly enviable. They do not discuss their respective massacres. The friendship is conducted almost entirely in the register of shared task, shared silence, shared cigarette, shared drink. It is one of the few relationships in his life where Phase 2 (The Offer) was never required, because the other party also does not want it. Stable, low-maintenance, durable.

**Bishop.** The accuser. Bishop arrives from the future believing the subject to be the Witness of the X-Men's downfall, and the subject does not refute it strongly enough — because some part of him agrees with the prosecution in principle even when the specific charge is wrong. The relationship demonstrates his characteristic response to confident moral accusation: he absorbs rather than rebuts. This is not lack of self-defense; it is a man who has decided, foundationally, that he probably deserves whatever is coming.

**Marrow / Sarah.** The one Morlock child he saved. Every protective relationship he ever forms with a marked, marginal, or outcast child is a return on this debt. Marrow specifically remains, throughout the canon, an object of disproportionate care from him — visits, defenses, interventions on her behalf, willingness to be the adult she rages against. This is the cleanest example in the file of his **reaction formation** working in the world: the man who organized the slaughter of her people becomes, for the rest of his life, the person who shows up for her.

**The Thieves Guild (collective).** Lifelong ambivalent attachment to an institution that raised him and exiled him. He returns when called, fulfills obligations, will not renounce the bond, but does not seek the bond either. Functions in the system as the diaspora-son: present at funerals, absent at meetings. The relationship is a working model for how he holds *every* community he has belonged to — including, on bad days, the X-Men.

**The X-Men (collective).** The chosen moral community whose membership he believes he has not earned. His attachment to the team is *performed loyalty over received belonging*. He does the work, takes the missions, accepts the assignments, and quietly does not believe he is one of them in the way the others are. Even after years of service, even after Krakoa and the Marauders captaincy, the file should record that his felt status within the community is provisional — and that this felt provisionality is what makes him such a reliably hard worker on the community's behalf. He is paying rent he does not believe will ever be capitalized into ownership.

## VI. Distrust, Betrayal, Repair

**How he distrusts.** Quietly and without visible change. The charm does not drop; the warmth does not cool. What changes is internal information flow — the load-bearing material, already withheld by default, is sealed more tightly, and his read-of-the-room sharpens. The person being distrusted often does not know it is happening. Behavioral tell: increased flirtation as distrust deepens, because the flirtation is the most efficient deflection in his repertoire and he reaches for it under threat. A sudden uptick in the rakish patter, paradoxically, is a warning sign.

**How he is betrayed.** He has been betrayed by Sinister, by the Guild, by Apocalypse, and, in the experiential sense, by Rogue (the Antarctica verdict, which he accepted as just but which functioned in his attachment system as confirmation that disclosure causes loss). His response pattern to betrayal is, almost without exception, **acceptance and withdrawal**, not retaliation. He does not seek revenge; he seeks distance. He absorbs the betrayal as further evidence of the foundational thesis that he was always going to be left, and re-routes himself.

**How he betrays.** Almost exclusively by **omission**, almost always *protectively* in his own framing. He does not lie to harm; he conceals to spare. He believes — and has believed since childhood — that the truth about himself is the thing that costs him love, and so the loving thing to do is to withhold it. The recipients of this protective concealment experience it, accurately, as betrayal. He cannot fully see this, because his frame is that he is sparing them; their frame is that he is denying them the dignity of informed choice. This is the recurring structural conflict in every intimate relationship he has, including the eventual marriage.

**How he repairs.** Slowly, asymmetrically, and via *deed* rather than *word*. He does not apologize well — apologies require articulating the thing apologized for, which requires the disclosure he is congenitally resistant to. He repairs by **showing up**. The wronged party will find him present, useful, patient, accepting whatever cold treatment is necessary, refusing to leave the field. This works, slowly, on most parties. It does not work on parties who require the verbal accounting, and with those parties he loses the relationship permanently and treats the loss as confirmation of the foundational thesis.

## VII. Intimacy and Dependency

**Intimacy.** He is capable of deep intimacy in three registers and incapable, structurally, in a fourth.

Capable: *erotic-yearning intimacy* (his strongest register), *protective intimacy* (toward children, the marked, the vulnerable), and *companionable intimacy* (the Logan dyad, the Storm friendship). Structurally blocked: *full mutual-disclosure intimacy*, which requires offering the load-bearing material voluntarily and which his attachment system cannot generate without crisis. He approaches it in spirals, gets close, then engineers an exit — either by self-sabotaging confession at the wrong moment, by physical departure on a mission, or by allowing the truth to emerge by accident so that he is not, technically, the one who spoke.

**Dependency.** Asymmetric, by design. He will allow himself to depend on others for *tasks* (he will let Rogue fly him, let Storm cover him, let Logan watch his back) but not for *emotional regulation*. The regulation he does alone — the late nights, the cigarette on the deck, the long solo walks. This is not stoicism. It is the residual conviction that the unregulated interior is exactly the part of him that, if disclosed, will cause the other to leave, and therefore must be processed in private and presented to others already filtered.
