His partners are systematically given the polished output and not the raw material. Over years, this reads to them as a wall they cannot find the door in.

He accepts dependency *on him* readily — perhaps too readily; he is comfortable being the depended-upon, because that is the form of relating in which he is most certain of his place. Reverse the polarity and he becomes uncomfortable. Asking for help is the move most absent from his repertoire.

## VIII. The Template, Stated Plainly

Reduced to its operating diagram, the relational pattern repeated across every significant relationship in his life:

1. **Encounter another person, read them.**
2. **Identify what they need and offer a real, small, manageable piece of self.**
3. **Become useful to them in ways that exceed obligation.**
4. **Form a fast loyalty lock; treat the relationship as binding from his side regardless of reciprocity.**
5. **Conceal the load-bearing material indefinitely, framing the concealment as protective.**
6. **As the relationship deepens, increase deflective performance (flirtation, humor, accent, motion) in inverse proportion to felt safety.**
7. **Approach the moment of mutual disclosure and either swerve, sabotage, or arrange for accidental exposure.**
8. **Accept whatever consequence follows as just.**
9. **Withdraw without protest.**
10. **Return when summoned; resume utility; do not reopen the disclosure question.**

The single deviation in his entire documented life is the Rogue marriage in the *Mr. and Mrs. X* era and after, which represents the first sustained instance of him remaining present *through* steps 7–10 rather than withdrawing — and even there, the file should note, the structural prop of the touch-barrier had previously done much of the disclosure work for him. The marriage's continued health depends on him doing, voluntarily and repeatedly, the disclosure work the barrier used to do involuntarily. This is achievable. It is not automatic. It is the developmental task of the rest of his life.

The longitudinal verdict is that the subject is a man whose attachment system was built to solve an impossible problem — *how to be both used and loved* — and who solved it with an elegant, costly, lifelong workaround that allowed him to remain in proximity to love without ever having to test whether he could survive being fully known. The achievement of the late canon is not that he resolved the problem. It is that he found one person willing to stay in the room while he, slowly, learns to stop solving it.


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# DOSSIER SECTION VII: DEFENSES & COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

## The Full Defensive Architecture of Remy Etienne LeBeau

---

## VII.0 Orienting Premise

The subject's defensive system is **unusually well-developed, internally coherent, and consciously curated** — to a degree rare in clinical populations and rarer still in trauma populations. This is because his defenses were not improvised in the aftermath of trauma; they were **professionally trained into him from infancy** by the Thieves Guild as occupational equipment, *and then weaponized after the Morlock Massacre as psychic equipment*. He is, in effect, a man whose vocational toolkit and whose trauma-coping toolkit are the same toolkit. A Guild-trained pickpocket and a man hiding a perpetration secret both need: the ability to be looked at without being seen, the ability to redirect attention with one hand while the other hand works, the ability to leave a room without leaving a memory, and the ability to be liked on first contact.

This makes him **abnormally functional for his trauma load** — and abnormally hard to read. Most C-PTSD patients leak. Subject does not leak. He **performs**. The performance is the leak, but only to a viewer who knows what unleaked material would look like.

What follows is the full inventory, ranked from most mature/sublimatory to most primitive/regressive, with operational observables for each.

---

## VII.1 The Mature Tier (Sublimation Stratum)

### VII.1.1 Sublimation Proper — Criminality Re-Channeled Into Heroism

The clearest and structurally most important defense in the file. The subject's Guild-trained skill set — infiltration, lock work, social engineering, theft, the use of charm as a weapon, the use of cards and small objects as weapons — is, in adulthood, **deployed against the exact category of victim he once helped create**. He steals for the team, infiltrates for the team, talks his way through doors for the team, and now, as captain of the rescue vessel called the Marauders, **literally inverts the name of the unit he assembled for Sinister**. The semantic inversion is too neat to be coincidence; on a behavioral level, it is the defense made architectural. The job description hasn't changed (lead a small crew of operators called Marauders into dangerous spaces); the moral vector has been rotated 180 degrees.

Observable in: every X-Men heist arc; the Morlock-rescue subroutines that recur across his career; his preference, when offered any tactical role, for the *infiltration* slot over the *strike* slot — he chooses, repeatedly, the role that allows him to thieve a life back rather than take one.

### VII.1.2 Reaction Formation — Protectiveness In Excess of Warrant

Distinct from sublimation: reaction formation is the **emotional inversion** of the original impulse, not its skill-level re-channeling. The man who *led* a slaughter of defenseless mutants now exhibits an almost automatic, often tactically inadvisable, protective response toward defenseless mutants — specifically the disfigured, the marginal, the cast-out-by-their-own-community. The Marrow rescue at the moment of the crime is the prototype: under maximum stress, with the original crime in progress, he reflexively saves a child. This is not a calculated atonement; it is a **counter-impulse with its own velocity**, fast enough to register before deliberation.

Predictable behavior: he will be the first X-Man to interpose his body between a non-combatant and a threat, will do so without team coordination, and will downplay it afterward with humor. Anyone wishing to predict his battlefield position should look for the most vulnerable civilian on the field; he is within three meters.

### VII.1.3 Humor — Anticipatory Defusal

Subject's humor is **structural**, not decorative. Three distinct functions, deployed contextually:

- *Defusal humor* — he uses a joke to dilate a tense room, particularly when conflict between teammates threatens. Pattern across the Lobdell/Mackie era especially: he interrupts vertical confrontations (Cyclops vs. Wolverine, Rogue vs. Carol-residue) with a lateral, often self-mocking, aside.
- *Disclosure-bait humor* — he tells a true story about himself that sounds like a confession but is actually a decoy; the listener leaves with a sense of intimacy, having received nothing load-bearing.
- *Pre-emptive self-mockery* — he insults himself first, in registers ranging from his accent to his Cajun-rube affect to his thief past, **specifically when an interlocutor is about to**. This denies the other person the move and converts an attack into a shared joke. Observable in nearly every Wolverine interaction across the corpus.

### VII.1.4 Altruism (Pathological Subvariety)

Genuine, costly, repeated, but **organized around a guilt-economic**: he gives not because giving feels good but because giving is the only currency in which he believes he can pay rent on his place in the moral community. Distinguishable from healthy altruism by the **affect signature**: healthy altruism is followed by satisfaction; subject's altruism is followed by a brief flatness, sometimes a cigarette taken alone, occasionally a self-deprecating remark. He gives and receives no internal credit.

### VII.1.5 Anticipation — The Operational Planner

Trained capacity, leveraged defensively: he runs forward simulations of social and tactical encounters at high frequency. This is normal Guild tradecraft turned into a generalized cognitive style. Defensively, it means he is rarely *surprised* — and being-surprised is the state in which his other defenses are most likely to fail. He spends down emotional volatility in advance, in private, before encounters that might trigger it.

---

## VII.2 The Neurotic Tier (Identity-Management Stratum)

### VII.2.1 Splitting of Self — "Remy" vs. "Gambit"

Not Kleinian object-splitting (he does not bifurcate others into all-good / all-bad — his read of people is, in fact, unusually nuanced). Rather, **self-splitting**: he maintains two functional identities, with the codename functioning as a **clean container** for the post-Sinister self. "Gambit" is the X-Man, the operator, the team asset; "Remy" is the thief, the Cajun, the Guild son, the carrier of the Morlock secret. He uses the names with discipline. Teammates calling him "Remy" generally indicate intimacy or recruitment to vulnerability; teammates calling him "Gambit" indicate operational tempo. Rogue's oscillation between the two is itself a relational signal he tracks.

The bifurcation is **adaptive but costly**: it allows him to function in two domains without contamination, but at the price of never being a single integrated person in any room.

### VII.2.2 Intellectualization (Limited Variant)

Less developed than in higher-functioning intellectual defenders because the subject does not lead with cognition — he leads with read-of-the-room. But when forced to discuss the Massacre, he reliably **shifts to procedural language**: who was where, what the contractual terms were, what he did and did not know at what time. The affect drops out. This is observable across multiple confession scenes (to Rogue, to Storm, in the Antarctica trial). The procedural register is a defense; it allows him to give the data without giving the feeling.

### VII.2.3 Displacement — Onto Cards and Small Objects

A genuinely interesting case. Subject's signature behavior — the constant handling, riffling, flipping of a deck of cards — is **kinetic displacement** of multiple drives at once: hand-tension regulation (the energy of his power literally has somewhere to go), nicotine-substitute oral-replacement (when not smoking, the hands take over), and, most importantly, **affective displacement**. Watch the cards across any extended sequence: they accelerate when he is anxious, slow when he is calculating, stop entirely when he is genuinely caught off-guard. The deck is a tell *to readers of the deck* and a regulator *to him*. Bo staff handling serves the same function under combat conditions; cigarette manipulation served it before editorial environments curtailed depicted smoking.

### VII.2.4 Concealment / Lying by Omission

Default operating mode in intimate domains. Critical to characterize correctly: the lies are **protective rather than predatory**, and the subject experiences them as costs paid, not as triumphs. He does not enjoy deceiving Rogue; he believes, with conviction sufficient to override better counsel, that the truth will cost him the love. This is the **avoidant-attachment defense made verbal**.

Operational features: he does not fabricate, he omits. Direct questions receive deflections or partial truths, never invented falsehoods. This is Guild discipline — a fabrication can be checked, an omission cannot — but it is also a moral residue: he will not author an active lie to a loved one, only withhold. He preserves a thin line of personal honor inside the larger dishonesty, and the line matters to him.

### VII.2.5 Reaction-Formation Against Vanity — The Deliberately Thickened Accent

Granular observable. The accent is real — he is genuinely from southern Louisiana — but its *intensity is dialed*. Subject's interior-monologue captions across the Nicieza solo and the Layman run are markedly less accented than his dialogue. The Cajun affect is **performance turned up around non-Louisianans** as a self-effacing class-presentation, a method of inviting underestimation, and a way of converting cosmopolitan beauty into folksy nonthreat. Underestimation is a Guild asset; folksy is a charm asset; non-threat is a confession-evasion asset. One behavior, three defensive functions.

### VII.2.6 Suppression (Active, Conscious)

He has **trained conscious capacity** to set aside affect in operational windows — Guild discipline, reinforced by demonstrated ability to resist telepathic intrusion through controlled compartmentalization. This is mature suppression, not repression: he knows where the material is, he chooses not to access it now, he can retrieve it later. This capacity is what makes him one of the few X-Men who routinely defeats telepaths in close work; it is also what makes him hard to therapize, because the material is sealed behind a door he can open but will not.

---

## VII.3 The Compromise-Formation Tier (Relational Engineering Stratum)

### VII.3.1 Object-Choice as Defense — The Structural-Impossibility Selection

The signature defense, and the file's single most important behavioral datum. The Rogue selection is **not romantic accident**; it is, on inspection, the **avoidant defense made flesh, then ennobled by years of public yearning**. To select as life-object the one available partner with whom physical consummation is impossible is to engineer a relationship that **cannot collapse under the weight of full disclosure**, because it cannot reach full closure of any kind. He gets to remain a good lover *in the yearning register*, where his skills are best (charm, patience, romantic theater, the long courtship) and never has to become a lover in the *known* register, where the secret would have to surface.

This is the most expensive defense in the kit. It cost him almost two decades of publication-time in deferred intimacy. He paid willingly. When Rogue's powers were eventually moderated such that touch became possible (and after *Mr. and Mrs. X* made the marriage canonical), the defense had to be retired — and the file shows him entering marriage **with measurable difficulty**, requiring the integration he had structurally evaded for twenty years.

### VII.3.2 Disclosure-by-Violation Rather Than Confession

Tightly coupled to VII.3.1. Subject does not confess; he **engineers conditions in which the truth surfaces by accident** (Rogue's absorption of his memories; the Trial's evidentiary intervention; the Apocalypse-Death residues that surface despite his concealment). The defensive logic: a voluntary confession can be punished without mitigation; a truth surfaced by violation places the listener in the dual role of judge *and* of someone who has wronged him by intruding. It softens the verdict slightly. It also relieves him of the act he cannot perform — the act of speaking the words out loud, of his own will, to a face he loves.

This pattern repeats across the canon with such regularity it must be coded as defense, not as accident.

### VII.3.3 Anticipatory Self-Disclosure-as-Charm

He **performs** vulnerability constantly — the rakish confession of being a thief, the cheerful admission of being trouble, the self-deprecating account of his own romantic failures — precisely to **discharge the social demand for actual vulnerability**. The interlocutor walks away thinking they were given access. They were given decoy access. This is a refinement of humor (VII.1.3) into a higher-order interpersonal defense, and it is **the single most effective concealment technique in his repertoire**, because it does not look like concealment.

### VII.3.4 Charm as Pre-Emptive Tribute

He charms early and reliably, particularly the people who would, if they knew, condemn him. The charm functions as **pre-paid social currency** — he is depositing relational equity in advance against the day the secret comes out. Observable directionality: charm intensity correlates with how moral the target appears to be. He charms Storm differently than he charms Logan; he is gentler, more deferential, more eager-to-be-liked with the figures whose judgment he would most fear.

---

## VII.4 The Immature Tier (Repetition Stratum)

### VII.4.1 Identification with the Aggressor / Repetition Compulsion

The catastrophic-failure-mode defense. Under conditions of acute power dysregulation paired with a credible offer of *control over the power* from a powerful father-figure, subject has accepted the bargain **twice** — Sinister (the originating instance) and Apocalypse (Horseman of Death). Each time the bargain involves accepting the role of monster in exchange for relief of the dysregulation. Each time, the relief is real; the cost is the repetition of the original crime in a higher key.

This is the file's most predictive datum. **He is structurally susceptible to this bargain a third time.** Any operational planning involving the subject must price this in. The conditions that produce vulnerability are: (a) acute power instability, (b) loss or threat-of-loss of Rogue, (c) a credible figure of patriarchal authority offering control. Two of three is borderline; three of three is historically determinative.

### VII.4.2 Denial-of-Deserving / Acceptance of Disproportionate Punishment

The Antarctica acceptance is the prototype: subject *agrees* with the verdict that exceeds proportion. He does not defend himself, does not invoke mitigation, does not argue context. This is not masochism in the sexual or characterological sense; it is **a moral submission that has been calcified into reflex**. He has decided, internally, that he is owed punishment, and any punishment offered that falls under that ceiling is accepted as partial payment.

Behavioral observable: when he stops arguing, when the wit drops out, when he goes still — that is acceptance of judgment. It is the body language of a man receiving a bill he was already expecting.

### VII.4.3 Self-Sabotage at Threshold of Intimacy

A recurrent pattern: relationships stabilize, intimacy approaches the threshold of full disclosure, and subject **manufactures a rupture** — usually via a withheld truth surfacing, occasionally via an absence (a mission taken alone, a disappearance from the team). The mechanism is defensive: full disclosure is intolerable, so the disclosure is replaced by the rupture, which serves the same function (ending the proximity) at a lower psychic cost.

### VII.4.4 Hypervigilance Somatized

Sleep impairment, taking unbidden watch shifts, never being the last to wake. This is **trauma-driven hyperarousal repurposed as team utility**. It looks like reliability; it is also a sleep disorder. The disorder is fed because its symptoms are socially rewarded — the team values the man who always takes the late watch. He is paid for his insomnia in the only currency he accepts: continued membership.

### VII.4.5 Substance-Regulatory Use

Tobacco (in the Claremont/Nicieza eras), alcohol (consistent throughout). Use pattern: **social-recreational with regulatory function**, most pronounced when alone or post-loss. Not addiction; not absent of significance. The cigarette is a defense — an oral self-soothing, a hand-occupier, a permission-to-pause inside a social interaction (the smoke break as a reset). The bourbon is a defense — a slow disinhibitor that lowers the cost of the charm performance when fatigue raises it.

---

## VII.5 The Primitive Tier (Rarely-Observed, Acute-Stress Only)

### VII.5.1 Dissociative Numbing Under Threat

Observable only under acute stress (Antarctica, Apocalypse conversion sequence, X-Cutioner's Song memory-extraction). Subject **goes flat**, affect drops out, action becomes minimal or compliant. This is not his baseline; it is the failure mode that appears when the higher-tier defenses have been overwhelmed. It is the state in which the bad bargains have historically been accepted.

### VII.5.2 Splitting of Caregivers (Subclinical)

Rare and transient. Under acute father-figure pressure he can, briefly, idealize the figure offering him relief (Sinister at the bargain, Apocalypse at the conversion). The idealization collapses post-event. This is the *only* instance of object-splitting in his repertoire, and it is precisely co-located with the catastrophic failure mode (VII.4.1).

### VII.5.3 Acting-In (Self-Directed)

The Antarctica acceptance is the closest the file comes to a passively self-harming act. There is no documented active self-harm, no suicidality. But the willingness to walk into harm, to accept disproportionate consequence, to volunteer for the lethal infiltration, sits at the edge of the diagnostic territory of self-directed aggression. Coded as **passive acting-in via mission selection**. Risk-of-self is paid in operational currency; this provides moral cover and renders the self-harm illegible as such.

---

## VII.6 Positive Compensatory Mechanisms (Net Assets)

Distinct from defenses: these are stable capacities that compensate, in domains adjacent to deficit, by **converting wound-energy into competence**.

- **Outsized loyalty to chosen individuals**, once chosen — because he knows the cost of betrayal from the inside, he has set himself an internal floor against ever causing it again to someone he loves.
- **Capacity to absorb shame without externalizing blame** — almost unique on the X-roster. Most members in shame-states externalize (Cyclops withdraws into duty; Wolverine rages; Logan-types displace into combat). Subject internalizes cleanly. This makes him **stable to work with under shared blame conditions** and unusually safe to confide failures in.
- **Willingness to be the morally compromised operator the team needs**, and to bear the social cost. The team's wet-work, ambiguous-ethics, infiltrate-the-villain assignments default to him not because he is best (often he is) but because he will accept the residue. He absorbs the team's moral overflow.
- **High-resolution interpersonal perception** — Guild-trained, trauma-sharpened. He reads micro-expressions, status hierarchies, alliance fractures faster than anyone in his cohort. This is **hypervigilance converted into social intelligence**.
- **Stable identity-floor for the marginal-of-the-marginal** — children, the disfigured, the cast-out, those whose own community has rejected them. He functions toward this population as a reliable safe figure, almost without fail, because they are the category he secretly believes he belongs to and toward whom his protectiveness is non-negotiable.

---

## VII.7 Negative Compensatory Mechanisms (Net Liabilities)

- **Lying to loved ones "for their protection"** — costs him the relationships he is trying to protect, recursively.
- **Pursuing relationships structured to fail** — paid two decades for one such selection, and would, absent specific intervention, do so again.
- **Accepting punishment in excess of warrant** — saves the institution moral effort; costs him the integration that genuine proportional accountability would produce.
- **Gravitating, under acute stress, toward exploitative father-figures who offer control of his power** — the file's catastrophic vulnerability. See VII.4.1.
- **Performing wellness when not well** — the charm machine runs through his own crises; his teammates frequently learn he is in trouble only after the trouble has resolved or escalated past concealment. He is a **late presenter** for help, and his late presentation is reinforced by the social reward his concealed wellness produces.

---

## VII.8 Integrative Summary

The defensive architecture is **a single coherent system** in which Guild tradecraft (lower-tier operational deceptions, anticipatory planning, charm-as-tool, displacement onto small objects) provides the bottom rails, sublimation and reaction formation provide the upper rails, and the entire structure is **load-bearing on a single concealed perpetration-secret**. Remove the secret — give him a context in which it is known, witnessed, integrated, and survived — and large portions of the defensive system would, in clinical theory, become unnecessary.

The *Mr. and Mrs. X* marriage represents the closest the canon has come to that condition: Rogue has seen the secret (via memory absorption), survived knowing it, returned anyway, and made the choice voluntarily. The defenses do not vanish in this period — they are too over-learned for that — but they **soften**, and the bifurcation between Remy and Gambit narrows toward a single, livable, integrated person.

The defenses remain, however, **available for instantaneous redeployment** under stress. They are not gone; they are **stood down**. This is the correct disposition for them; full retirement would be neither realistic nor, given his line of work, advisable. The man needs his armor. He has just, for the first time in his documented life, been permitted to set it on the floor inside one room.

That room is the marriage. Everywhere else, the armor is on, and a viewer who does not know what to look for will not see it, because **it is shaped like charm**.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE

## Subject: LeBeau, Remy Etienne

*Decade-by-decade evolution of affect regulation, cognitive style, and self-concept. Formulations are derived from published behavior and validated against contemporary clinical frameworks (ICD-11 C-PTSD; Litz moral-injury model; Bowlby/Main attachment taxonomy; Linehan affect-regulation schema; Vaillant defense hierarchy). Where the canon is silent, inference is marked.*

---

## DECADE I — Infancy through Latency (approx. age 0–10)

### Affect regulation

In the earliest documented period the subject's regulatory environment was structurally pathogenic in a specific way: not abusive in the high-arousal sense (Jean-Luc is consistently depicted as a *warm* foster-father), but **conditional**. Affection arrived bundled with utility — the child was praised for competence at the lift, the pick, the read. The regulatory consequence is that the subject learned, in the period when interoceptive labeling is being installed, to **read others' affect with surgical precision and his own affect as background noise**. The Guild trained outward perception at the explicit cost of inward perception. Tante Mattie sequences (the *Gambit* Vol. 3 flashbacks, Nicieza, 1999) depict a child who soothes adults rather than being soothed by them — early-onset *parentification* in a thieves' household.

By latency, behavioral signs consistent with an **externally-oriented co-regulator** are visible: he calibrates his charm to the room before he registers his own state. The "smile that arrives before the feeling" pattern that defines the adult is already grooved in by age eight or nine.

### Cognitive style

Precocious convergent-and-divergent both — Guild pedagogy demanded simultaneous plan-execution (convergent) and improvisation under contingency (divergent). The child learns probabilistic, Bayesian-flavored reasoning before he learns to read fluently: every door, lock, mark, and patrol pattern is a prior to be updated. He is also being trained in **theory-of-mind exploitation** — not just inferring others' mental states but engineering them. By the end of latency he is an unusually skilled social manipulator with a value-neutral moral frame: the act is judged by its execution, not its content.

### Self-concept

Inchoate but already bifurcated. Two competing labels are present in the environment: *le diable blanc* (the visible mark of the eyes, the supernatural-other category imposed by superstitious adults) and *fils* (the Guild son, the chosen heir of Jean-Luc). The child cannot reconcile these and does not try; he simply *uses each in its appropriate context*. This is the embryo of the lifelong **context-switching identity architecture** that later allows him to be Remy-the-thief in New Orleans and Gambit-the-X-Man in Westchester without experiencing the contradiction as crisis.

---

## DECADE II — Adolescence through Early Adulthood (approx. age 10–20)

### Affect regulation

This is the decade of the **power-onset catastrophe**. Pre-Sinister, the bio-kinetic charge is uncontrollable and escalating; the documented experience is one of a body that betrays its owner with potentially homicidal consequences whenever arousal rises. Clinically, this produces a phenomenology indistinguishable from severe panic-spectrum interoceptive dread: every elevation of heart rate, every flush of desire or anger, becomes a possible prelude to detonation. The regulatory adaptation is **massive parasympathetic-leaning suppression** — the cool affect, the slow drawl, the smile-under-fire — drilled in adolescence under literal survival pressure. He learns to be *calmest when threatened* because the alternative is to kill the people around him.

The Bella Donna engagement and the duel with Julien sit in this period. The killing of Julien — an *affectively flooded* event he survives only by retreating into trained competence — establishes the lifelong template: **when emotion threatens to overwhelm, switch to operational mode and feel later, badly, alone.** He does not grieve the duel in any depicted way. He is exiled and moves.

### Cognitive style

The Sinister surgery falls in this window. Post-procedure, cognition is observably *cleaner* (he can plan complex sequences without the constant interoceptive interference of the unstable power) but also subtly *flatter*. The pre-Sinister Remy of the flashbacks is hotter, more reactive; the post-Sinister Remy is the cool tactician we know. Whether this is neurological sequela of the resection, learned discipline post-traumatic, or both, is impossible to disentangle from the canon — but the timing of the cognitive style shift is contemporaneous with the surgical intervention and the framework of *iatrogenic personality change post-frontal/limbic resection* is the most parsimonious read.

He acquires, in this same window, the assembly of the Marauders — i.e., a sustained, weeks-to-months executive-function project requiring sophisticated personnel evaluation, logistics, and operational security, executed by a man in his late teens. This is a cognitive datum: the subject was capable of complex strategic agency *and chose not to interrogate the strategic goal*. The defense here is **moral compartmentalization rationalized by debt** — Sinister fixed my hands, I owe him a team, what he does with the team is his moral problem. This rationalization survives until the tunnels, where it is detonated.

### Self-concept

Enters the decade as *le fils de Jean-Luc, le diable blanc, le voleur*. Exits the decade as something for which he has, at first, no name: **author of the unforgivable**. The Massacre re-codes every prior self-label retroactively. The eyes are no longer cosmetic strangeness — they are now legibly devil's eyes. The thievery is no longer a craft — it is now the gateway crime. The exile from New Orleans, previously an injustice, is now revealed to him (privately) as warranted, simply for the wrong reason.

The decade closes with the subject homeless in a moral sense: no community knows what he is, and the one that *would* condemn him for it doesn't exist yet (he hasn't met the X-Men). This interstitial period — between the Massacre and the recruitment — is the incubator of the adult personality. He spends it inventing **Gambit** as a wearable container.

---

## DECADE III — Young Adulthood / X-Men Entry (approx. age 20–30)

### Affect regulation

The Storm-recruitment arc inaugurates the long, stable phase of **dramaturgical affect management**. The presenting affect — light, flirtatious, mobile, ironically distant — is now reliably available on demand. Crucially, the Nicieza and Layman interior-monologue passages disclose that this is *not* dissociation in the impaired sense; the subject knows what he is doing, knows that he is performing, and can articulate the gap to himself. This is closer to a clinically sophisticated **emotional labor** strategy (Hochschild) than to alexithymia or detachment. He *feels* the underlying affect; he simply does not let it surface into the room.

The cost shows in the **isolation behavior post-mission**: the cigarette on the roof, the long walks, the unprompted watch shifts. He discharges the suppressed affect privately, in regulated doses, away from witnesses. This is functional but expensive — there is no co-regulator in his life in this period because the only candidate, Rogue, is structurally barred by skin from the form of co-regulation (proximate physical contact) that his nervous system most needs.

Acute dysregulation episodes in this decade cluster around two triggers: (a) accidental Rogue-disclosure events (the memory-absorption flashes in *X-Men* Vol. 2 #7), where the secret threatens to surface without his control; and (b) field encounters with surviving Morlocks, where the subject's depicted reactions — a fractional hesitation, an over-protective reflex, a refusal to make eye contact — are micro-tells of the still-unmetabolized perpetration trauma.

### Cognitive style

Reaches mature form. **Tactical improvisation atop strategic discipline**, with an extremely well-developed Bayesian read of human behavior and unusually low cognitive load when lying (the Guild training pays its largest dividend in operational deception). He is one of the only X-Men in this period who routinely defeats telepaths in close engagement, via trained compartmentalization — the same architecture that lets him hold the Massacre in a sealed room of his mind also lets him hold a decoy thought-package at the front of consciousness while Psylocke or Jean reads him.

Notably, his strategic cognition has a characteristic *negative space*: he plans against worst-case betrayal scenarios with paranoid thoroughness in operations involving institutions, and almost never in operations involving individuals he has personally chosen. The asymmetry encodes his ethical posture (loyalty to persons over systems) directly into his planning style.

### Self-concept

Now stably bifurcated. **Conscious self-concept: "a thief who is trying."** This is the load-bearing self-statement, the one he uses to get out of bed. **Unconscious self-concept: irredeemable.** The two are kept in different rooms by the same compartmentalization that defeats the telepaths. The penance economy is fully online: every Marauder lifted from rubble, every child shielded with his own body, every mission he takes that a less compromised X-Man could take instead — all are entries in a ledger he does not believe will ever balance, but which it would be intolerable to stop keeping.

The Rogue object choice is consolidated in this decade. The decision to pursue, with extraordinary patience, a woman whose powers preclude the intimacy that would force disclosure, is — re-emphasizing — **the avoidant defense rendered as a love story he can tell himself is romantic rather than defensive**. Both readings are true; he is genuinely in love, *and* the choice is structured by what he cannot risk.

---

## DECADE IV — Antarctica, Death, and the Long Reckoning (approx. age 30–40)

### Affect regulation

The Antarctica trial is the **affective hinge of the published life**. The behavioral datum to attend to is not that he is exposed (he had to be eventually) but that **he does not defend himself**. He does not produce mitigation, contextualization, or appeal. He accepts. The Rogue-as-judge sequence in *Uncanny X-Men* #350 documents a man whose superego, when finally given the public verdict it has been privately rehearsing for a decade, simply nods.

What follows — months stranded, the survival arc, the slow return — is depicted with an affective quality that clinical readers should flag as **morally-injured resignation**, not depressive collapse. The distinction matters. A depressively collapsed subject would not have survived Antarctica; the will to live would have failed. The subject's behavior is closer to penance pilgrimage — he believes the suffering is *owed* and therefore endurable. Discriminating moral-injury presentation from depressive episode by this exact criterion (suffering experienced as *fitting* rather than as meaningless) is core to the Litz framework and the subject is a textbook case.

The Horseman of Death conversion that follows in the Carey years detonates whatever stabilization he had reconstructed. The clinical signature here is a **dissociative-spectrum identity intrusion** — Apocalypse's conditioning installs an alter-functional Death-self that the subject experiences as both himself and not himself. The genuinely terrifying datum, recoverable from the post-conversion narrative beats, is that **he experienced relief inside the conversion**. Permission to be the monster he privately believed he was is, for a subject organized around suppressed self-condemnation, *symptomatically relieving*. This is the same mechanism that explains the Sinister bargain twenty years earlier: a powerful figure says *you are what I say you are, and I will manage you*, and the chronic interior pressure of self-management briefly lifts.

Post-Death, affect regulation is observably more fragile for a sustained period — sleep further disrupted, isolation behavior intensified, alcohol use slightly elevated (per panel evidence in Carey's run). He recovers, but does not return to pre-Death baseline. There is residue.

### Cognitive style

Decade IV introduces the first sustained **cognitive distortion** visible in the canon: catastrophizing about Rogue, future-foreshortening about his own life ("Remy don' got much of a future, chere"), and an emerging tendency to *interpret ambiguous interpersonal feedback as confirmation of unworthiness*. These are classic depressive-cognitive triad intrusions but they appear in a non-depressed substrate — they are the **cognitive overflow of moral injury** rather than primary mood-disorder cognitions.

His strategic cognition, by contrast, remains sharp and arguably sharpens further. The decade includes his most operationally complex independent work (the *Gambit* solo runs depict elaborate multi-party schemes executed largely without team support). The split between deteriorating intrapersonal cognition and intact-or-improving operational cognition is itself diagnostic: **his thinking works fine on every problem except himself.**

### Self-concept

Achieves its lowest published point in this window. The Antarctica acceptance and the Death conversion are sequential confirmations of the unconscious self-concept; the conscious self-concept ("a thief who is trying") thins to near-transparency. What sustains him through this decade is, by the evidence, **not self-regard but external relational anchoring** — specifically, the slow re-admission by Rogue, by Storm, by the team. He is, in this period, a man kept alive by *others' refusal to give up on him*, and he knows it, and his behavior reflects an exquisite, almost painful gratitude that he never voices directly.

---

## DECADE V — Integration, Marriage, Marauders Captaincy (approx. age 40+)

### Affect regulation

The *Mr. and Mrs. X* (Thompson, 2018) marriage and the contemporaneous developments around Rogue's control of her powers produce, for the first time in the subject's adult life, the conditions for **co-regulated intimacy with full physical contact and full mutual knowledge**. This is, from a developmental-trauma standpoint, the missing piece of his entire prior architecture. Skin contact with a securely attached partner downregulates the autonomic substrate that has been hypervigilant since the power onset; sustained, witnessed, accepted disclosure (Rogue has by now seen the worst of him and stayed) discharges the chronic shame loop that drove the dramaturgical management strategy.

The behavioral consequence is observable across the Krakoa and Marauders runs: the affect is *less performed*, the charm is still present but no longer load-bearing, the silences are easier, the isolation behaviors decrease in frequency. He is, for the first time, depicted **laughing in a manner that does not also function as deflection**.

This is not full recovery. The Marauders captaincy itself is best read as ongoing, sublimated symptom-management — the man who once led murderers called Marauders now leads rescuers called Marauders, performing the inverse of the founding crime in literal terms. This is the highest-order Vaillantian mature defense (sublimation in service of reparation) and it is doing real, lifelong work. He cannot stop performing penance; he has merely found a form of penance that is also love.

### Cognitive style

The strategic-operational cognition is now in full leadership application — captaining a ship and a team requires the planning architecture he developed in the Guild applied at organizational scale, and he is observably competent at it. The intrapersonal cognition shows the first sustained improvement of the published life: fewer catastrophizing intrusions about Rogue, more future-oriented planning that includes his own continued existence, more capacity to **accept good outcomes without immediately bracing for their withdrawal**. The clinical name for this is *positive-affect tolerance*, and its acquisition late in a C-PTSD presentation is a marker of genuine remission-trajectory, not symptomatic suppression.

### Self-concept

The bifurcation persists but the partition has become permeable. The conscious self-concept now reads closer to **"a thief who is trying, and who is loved anyway"** — the *anyway* is new and is doing enormous psychic work. The unconscious self-concept of irredeemability has not vanished; it has been *outvoted*, daily, by the lived experience of being chosen by someone who knows. The penance economy continues but its character has changed — it is no longer paying rent on a place he believes he has not earned, but contributing to a place he has begun, tentatively, to believe is also his home.

The pressure points listed in the synthesis remain live. He is in remission, not cured. The Sinister-Apocalypse susceptibility — the structural attraction to powerful father-figures offering control in exchange for compliance — is dormant rather than resolved. Should the conditions recur (power dysregulation + loss of Rogue + credible offer), the historical evidence suggests the bargain would still tempt him. Forewarned.

---

## CROSS-DECADAL SYNTHESIS

The five-decade arc shows a remarkably coherent developmental trajectory of a single underlying organization: **instrumentally-attached child → surgically-modified, perpetration-traumatized young adult → dramaturgically-managed mid-career operator → publicly-exposed and morally-resigned penitent → co-regulated, sublimating, late-life integrator.** The throughline is *moral injury managed by relational engineering*, and the late-life integration is the first phase in which the relational engineering finally produces the conditions for the injury to begin to metabolize rather than merely be carried.

The clinical prognosis, derived from the trajectory rather than from any one snapshot, is **guardedly positive within the marriage and team structure, fragile outside it**. The subject's psychological health is not a property of the subject in isolation; it is a property of the subject embedded in the specific relational ecology he has — finally, in middle age, after forty years of patient courtship of an impossible woman who became possible — earned the right to inhabit.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL

## Subject: LeBeau, Remy Etienne ("Gambit")
### Section 4 of the Intelligence Dossier — Clinical Formulation

---

## 4.1 Framing Note and Methodological Caveats

Before any diagnostic claim is made, three caveats must be entered onto the record, because they constrain everything that follows.

**First**, the subject has, to the file's knowledge, never sat for formal psychiatric assessment. The X-Men's medical apparatus (the Muir Island workups under MacTaggert, the post-Krakoa medical infrastructure, the various telepathic interventions by Xavier, Jean Grey, and Emma Frost) has had access to him for decades, and none of the longitudinal record contains anything resembling a structured clinical interview, an SCID-5, a CAPS-5, or any validated trauma instrument administered to him. What exists instead is a thirty-five-year accumulation of *behavioral observation under operational conditions*, supplemented by interior monologue (the solo runs) and by the partial telepathic readouts that necessarily accompanied his decades of close work with mind-readers. The file is rich in behavior and impoverished in self-report. Diagnostic formulations downstream of this should be held with appropriate humility.

**Second**, the subject is, by any functional metric, *not in active clinical crisis at the indexing date*. He is gainfully occupied, married, capable of love and work in the Freudian sense, has not exhibited frank psychotic features, is not actively suicidal, and is rated by team handlers as among the most reliable field operators on the roster. **We are diagnosing chronic character-level pathology in a high-functioning patient, not a presenting acute syndrome.** This matters because virtually every label in DSM-5-TR and ICD-11 was calibrated against treatment-seeking populations, and the subject would never voluntarily seek treatment. He is the kind of patient psychiatry catches only obliquely, through his marriage, through his work, or through forensic occasions.

**Third**, the subject is a mutant with documented neurosurgical alteration to the cerebral substrate that governs his power. Any diagnosis that turns on impulse control, affect regulation, or dissociative phenomena must explicitly bracket the question of whether the iatrogenic lesion contributes. We are working without imaging, without baseline neuropsych, without anything resembling a competent post-operative follow-up. The Sinister procedure is, to a clinician, malpractice of cosmic proportions left unmonitored for thirty years. Some of what we call "psychology" in this subject may be partial neurology we cannot see.

With those caveats, the formulation.

---

## 4.2 Primary Diagnosis

### Complex Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder (ICD-11, 6B41), Chronic, Perpetration-Subtype, Moderate Severity, Partially Compensated

The ICD-11 frame is preferred to DSM-5-TR's "PTSD with dissociative features" because CPTSD as defined by the WHO captures the three additional Disturbances in Self-Organization (DSO) clusters that DSM elides and that the subject demonstrates floridly: (a) affective dysregulation, (b) negative self-concept, (c) disturbances in relationships. The subject would not, in my judgment, cleanly meet DSM-5-TR PTSD criteria on the intrusion/avoidance/arousal triad alone — his intrusion symptoms are episodic and well-masked, his avoidance is selectively cognitive rather than behavioral, his hyperarousal is occupationally indistinguishable from professional competence. He *does* meet ICD-11 CPTSD because the DSO cluster is the dominant clinical territory.

**Criterion A — Trauma exposure.** Satisfied in multiple registers, but the load-bearing exposure is the **Morlock Massacre** — perpetration-trauma, with elements of betrayal-trauma (discovering after the fact what Sinister had used him for), with secondary witnessing-trauma (the bodies of an underclass of his own kind), with attached moral-injury character (violation of his own values, however nascent at the time). This is precisely the polytraumatic, perpetration-laced exposure that the moral-injury literature (Litz et al., 2009; Shay's earlier *Achilles in Vietnam* work on combatant guilt) identifies as producing the most refractory clinical course. The trauma is repeated within the subject's history (Apocalypse / Death conversion is a structurally identical event in higher key) and is interpersonal in origin, both of which are ICD-11 CPTSD qualifiers.

**Re-experiencing.** Present but heavily managed. The file documents (a) recurrent dream content involving the tunnels, alluded to in interior captions across the Nicieza solo and Mike Carey's run; (b) somatic recoil at specific cues — confined-tunnel environments, the smell of certain industrial spaces, presence of disfigured outcast children; (c) episodic flashback-equivalents during high telepathic load, when the compartmentalization shielding partially fails. He does not freely report any of this. It is inferable only from behavioral micro-data and from what telepathic colleagues have, on occasion, accidentally surfaced.

**Avoidance.** Conspicuously selective. He does not avoid Morlocks — he overcorrects toward them, which is reaction formation, not avoidance. He *does* avoid voluntary disclosure of the event, avoids returning to the original tunnel geography when operationally possible, avoids speaking Sinister's name when alternatives exist, and avoids being alone in the immediate aftermath of any operation that re-evokes the schema (post-mission, he seeks Rogue's physical proximity if available; failing that, he disappears to bourbon and solitude, which is also avoidance, just self-medicated).

**Hyperarousal.** Chronic, ego-syntonic, and professionally rebadged. He is a poor sleeper. He takes unprompted watch shifts. He startles, but converts the startle into smooth motion fast enough that observers code it as reflex, not as vigilance. His situational awareness in any new space is documentable — eyes to exits, hands to potential weapons-of-opportunity, read of every body in the room within the first ten seconds — and is *training-consistent* (Guild) but *trauma-amplified* beyond the training baseline.

**DSO Cluster 1 — Affective dysregulation.** Present and masked. The mask is the relevant clinical feature: he runs a wide gap between presentation and interior, and the gap itself is the dysregulation. Externally, hyperthymic, light, mobile. Internally (per solo interiority), ruminative, guilt-saturated, periodically self-loathing. The energy required to maintain the gap is itself dysregulatory and shows up as fatigue, somatic complaint substitutes (the smoking, the late nights), and occasional irritability bursts in low-stakes contexts that are displacement from the high-stakes interior.

**DSO Cluster 2 — Negative self-concept.** The most clinically prominent feature and the one that most strongly supports CPTSD over either uncomplicated PTSD or a Cluster-B personality diagnosis. He believes he is **structurally defective**, not merely that he has *done* bad things. The Antarctica acceptance is the cleanest single behavioral datum in the file: when offered the choice to defend himself before tribunal and surviving partner, he declined, accepted the verdict, accepted the abandonment, and did not protest the disproportionate sentence. This is not depressive nihilism (he was not, at that moment, depressed); it is a **stable, ego-syntonic self-appraisal as deserving of punishment**. CPTSD literature describes this exact phenomenon as the "permanently damaged" cognitive schema.

**DSO Cluster 3 — Disturbances in relationships.** The systematic object-choice that prohibits consummation; the lying-by-omission default; the disclosure-by-violation pattern; the cyclical confess-flee-return sequence with Rogue across two decades. This is not avoidant personality structure — those patients avoid relationships altogether. This is *traumatic disturbance* in the conduct of an intensely sought relationship.

**Severity rating: Moderate.** He is not severe — he works, loves, protects, recovers from setback. He is not mild — the impairment is durable, decades-long, and has demonstrably constrained his life choices. He is **partially compensated** because the X-Men context functions, accidentally, as something close to ideal trauma rehabilitation: structured belonging, repeated opportunities for restitutional behavior, a partner whose own trauma history allows her to tolerate his, and a leadership role (the *Marauders* ship) that operates as inadvertent narrative therapy by allowing him to literally invert the founding crime in symbolic form.

---

## 4.3 Co-Primary Diagnosis / Reframe

### Moral Injury (Litz/Shay framework; non-DSM, clinically validated)

The clinician with the Litz framework in hand will, on reading this file, argue that moral injury is the *more precise* primary frame than CPTSD, and that argument has merit. Moral injury organizes its symptomatology around **guilt and shame** rather than around **fear and threat**, which is the discriminating axis. The subject's interior is organized around guilt. His re-experiencing is guilt-tinged, not fear-tinged. His avoidance is shame-driven, not phobic. His arousal is hypervigilant in a *protective-of-others* register, not in a *threat-to-self* register.

Moral injury also predicts, more precisely than PTSD, the *specific* symptom cluster the subject exhibits: spiritual/existential brokenness, self-handicapping in relationships, anomic anhedonia, asymmetric reparative behavior (working off a debt that can never be paid down to zero), and the characteristic "demand for punishment" pattern that we see in the Antarctica acceptance and in his pattern of walking into harm during operations that re-evoke the schema.

The cleanest formulation, for the file, is therefore: **CPTSD with prominent moral injury features, in which the moral injury is the dominant clinical territory and the PTSD architecture is the substrate.** This is not a fence-sit; it is the correct clinical picture. Both frames are needed because each captures something the other misses.

---

## 4.4 Comorbidities, Subclinical Features, and Conditions for Monitoring

### Persistent Depressive Disorder (DSM-5-TR 300.4) — Subthreshold

Low-grade chronic dysphoria is detectable in the interior monologue across multiple eras. It does not meet duration *plus* symptom-count threshold at any documented point because the hyperthymic presentation and the genuine pleasures (Rogue, motorcycle, the Quarter, cooking) provide enough functional positive affect to disqualify the diagnosis. However, the *dysthymic substrate* is real and exacerbates under loss conditions. Best read as **trait-level negative affectivity within the CPTSD picture**, not a separate Axis I disorder.

### Substance Use — Subclinical, but on the monitoring list

Alcohol use is moderate, regulatory rather than compulsive, with no documented tolerance escalation, no withdrawal pattern, no failed cessation attempts, no functional impairment, no legal/occupational consequence. Tobacco use is more clearly habitual and self-soothing, classically increased under stress and during isolation. Neither rises to a use disorder.

The clinically interesting fact is the *function* of the use, not the volume: the bourbon comes out **after loss, alone**, and the cigarettes intensify **post-mission, on watch, when the interior is loud**. This is regulatory self-medication of CPTSD symptomatology, and the risk profile is for *escalation under loss of Rogue* or *acute power dysregulation event*, not for spontaneous addiction. Monitor; do not currently diagnose.

### Insomnia (Chronic, Trauma-Associated)

Present and durable. Sleep onset and sleep maintenance both affected. He works around it by taking watch shifts, which converts a symptom into a contribution and is characteristic of his entire defensive style — he metabolizes pathology as utility. Not separately diagnosed; subsumed within the CPTSD arousal cluster.

### Dissociative Phenomena — Subclinical

Episodic depersonalization is detectable under acute stress (the Antarctica survival period; the post-Death-conversion period). He does not exhibit dissociative identity phenomena. The "Remy / Gambit" split is **structural identity bracketing**, not alter-personality dissociation — he is continuously aware of both, uses the codename instrumentally to bracket the post-Sinister identity, and does not experience amnesia between states. This is a *defensive splitting* in the Kleinian sense, operating in service of CPTSD self-concept management. Does not warrant a dissociative disorder diagnosis.

---

## 4.5 The Differential — What He Is Not, And Why

The differential matters here more than usual, because the subject's presentation is highly mimicry-prone. Several Cluster B personality disorders and several trauma-adjacent conditions will *look* like him at first pass. The clinician who stops at first pass will misdiagnose. Each rejection below is rigorous.

### Considered and Rejected: Antisocial Personality Disorder (DSM-5-TR 301.7)

The naïve read — career criminal, trained deceiver, comfortable with violence, willingness to operate outside law — generates an ASPD hypothesis. It is wrong, and the rejection is unambiguous on multiple criteria.

ASPD requires, at core, *failure of conscience* — a deficient or absent capacity for guilt, remorse, and other-regarding empathy. The subject's conscience is not deficient; it is **hypertrophied to the point of being clinically disabling**. He experiences guilt to a degree that organizes his entire adult life and constrains his happiness. The Antarctica behavior alone disqualifies ASPD: an antisocial patient does not accept punishment that exceeds the warrant; an antisocial patient does not internalize the verdict; an antisocial patient externalizes, rationalizes, and escapes.

His deceptions are **protective rather than predatory**. The discriminating clinical question for ASPD is *whom the deception serves*. His serve the loved one being shielded from the truth that would (he believes) destroy them — they are misguided, costly to the relationship, and arguably immature defenses, but they are not exploitative. He does not lie to extract value from the deceived; he lies to spare them and to retain proximity to them.

His empathy is operational and consistent. The Marrow rescue (saving a child mid-massacre, *at risk to himself*, in the moment of his deepest moral compromise) is the prototype. ASPD does not generate that behavior under that load. The criminal record is environmental (Guild upbringing; he was apprenticed in larceny before he could form moral concepts of his own) and is the wrong kind of crime — Guild work is property crime executed under elaborate honor code, not predatory interpersonal harm.

Final note: he scores high on the *behavioral* checklist items of ASPD (PCL-R Factor 2, antisocial lifestyle) and near-zero on the *affective-interpersonal* items (Factor 1, callous-unemotional core). This is the inverse pattern from a true antisocial patient. **Reject with confidence.**

### Considered and Rejected: Narcissistic Personality Disorder (DSM-5-TR 301.81)

The flirtation, the swagger, the visible enjoyment of his own competence, the cultivated stylized self-presentation — all generate NPD on first read.

Wrong, and the rejection turns on the function of the grandiose presentation. **NPD self-presentation defends grandiosity against shame**. The subject's self-presentation **defends intimacy against disclosure**. He is not protecting an inflated self-concept; he is protecting an inflated *charm-front* that conceals a deflated self-concept. The clinical question for NPD is what happens when the grandiose self is wounded — narcissistic injury produces rage, devaluation of the wounder, or collapse. The subject, on narcissistic injury, *agrees with the wounder*. Tell him he is a thief and a killer who does not deserve the woman he loves, and he will nod and walk into Antarctica. This is the inverse of the NPD wound response.

He routinely accepts subordinate roles. He defers to Storm, Cyclops, Xavier, and (in the Krakoa era) Kate Pryde without difficulty. He does not require admiration; he requires *tolerance*. He does not exploit; he subsidizes. He does not lack empathy; he is drowning in it.

The flirtation is a *defense*, and a clinically interesting one — it is **anticipatory disclosure of the false self in order to discharge the demand for disclosure of the true self**. You leave a conversation with him feeling you know him, and you have learned nothing load-bearing. This is sophisticated, but it is not narcissistic. It is avoidant-with-style. **Reject.**

### Considered and Partially Endorsed (Subclinical Traits): Borderline Personality Disorder (DSM-5-TR 301.83)

He scores on identity disturbance (the bifurcated self-concept), on intense unstable relationships (the Rogue cycle), on affective instability under stress, on abandonment sensitivity. He does **not** score on recurrent suicidality/self-harm (Antarctica is closer to passive moral submission than to suicidal behavior — he accepted death, he did not seek it), on chronic emptiness (his interior is full, often painfully so), on impulsive self-damaging behavior outside the relational domain (no spending sprees, no reckless driving outside the operationally justified, no risky sex, no binge eating), and on stress-related transient paranoid ideation.

He has BPD traits but does not have BPD. The traits are explicable as **downstream features of CPTSD with disorganized attachment**, which is the more parsimonious formulation. The clinical literature increasingly treats the BPD/CPTSD overlap as a single dimensional space with different center-of-mass for different patients; his center of mass is squarely CPTSD. **Reject as primary; note as traits.**

### Considered and Partially Endorsed: Avoidant Personality Disorder (DSM-5-TR 301.82)

Strong avoidance of intimate self-disclosure; durable expectation of rejection-on-being-known; reluctance to take interpersonal risks where the risk is *being seen*.

Rejected because the avoidance is **domain-specific to intimate disclosure**, and the AvPD diagnosis requires pervasive social avoidance across domains. The subject is the opposite of socially avoidant in non-intimate contexts. He walks into rooms full of strangers and works them with professional ease. He flirts with people he has no intention of pursuing. He recruits, runs informants, operates as the team's human-intelligence specialist, and is genuinely sustained by social contact. AvPD patients are not sustained by social contact; they are exhausted by it.

The right formulation is **trauma-driven, domain-specific avoidance of intimate self-disclosure**, which is CPTSD-cluster behavior. **Reject AvPD; affirm the specific avoidance pattern within CPTSD.**

### Considered and Rejected: Dependent Personality Disorder

Considered only because of the consistent pattern of attachment to dominant father-figures (Jean-Luc, Sinister, Apocalypse, even Xavier in muted form). Rejected because the attachment is **trauma-reenactment**, not dependent personality structure. DPD patients seek others to assume responsibility for their lives and fear separation as inability to function. The subject is hyper-functional alone, has spent extended periods in voluntary solitude, and resents the bargains with the father-figures even as he accepts them. The dynamic is **identification-with-the-aggressor under power crisis**, not dependency. **Reject.**

### Considered and Rejected: Histrionic Personality Disorder

The charm, the theatricality, the seductive interpersonal style raise HPD as a hypothesis. Rejected because HPD requires **shallow rapidly-shifting emotionality** and **discomfort when not the center of attention**. The subject's emotionality is, if anything, *deeper* than baseline and concealed under theatricality; he is comfortable not being the center of attention and frequently engineers situations in which he is *not* (the watch shifts, the solitary operations, the willingness to be the deniable asset). The theatricality is a defense, not a personality structure. **Reject.**

### Considered and Rejected: Major Depressive Disorder, Recurrent

He has had episodes that approximate MDE criteria (post-Antarctica; post-Death conversion; post-various Rogue ruptures). None of the documented episodes clearly satisfy the two-week sustained criterion with the full symptom cluster *as a standalone episode*, in my read. The depressive symptomatology is better understood as **CPTSD-driven shame depression**, episodic and reactive to schema-activation, rather than as primary recurrent MDD. If a future episode meets full criteria, the diagnosis should be added. For now: **do not add; monitor**.

### Considered and Rejected: Bipolar Spectrum

Considered only to rule out, because the hyperthymic baseline and the periodic withdrawal periods could superficially mimic Bipolar II. Rejected because (a) the hyperthymia is **stable trait-level presentation**, not episodic hypomania; (b) the withdrawal periods are situationally triggered (loss, schema activation), not endogenously episodic; (c) no documented sleep-need reduction, grandiosity inflation, pressured speech, or goal-directed activity escalation outside operational context. He is **hyperthymic in temperament**, not cyclothymic or bipolar in disorder. **Reject.**

### Considered and Rejected: Pseudologia Fantastica / Pathological Lying as Standalone Feature

His lying is **strategic, instrumental, and selective**. He lies to protect, to operate, and to maintain plausible deniability. He does not lie compulsively, does not lie for the experience of lying, does not construct elaborate fictional self-histories for non-instrumental reasons. The Guild training accounts for the technical facility; the trauma accounts for the protective deployment. **Not a standalone feature; subsumed within CPTSD avoidance pattern.**

### Considered and Rejected: Substance Use Disorder (Alcohol; Nicotine)

Addressed above. Subthreshold for both. Monitor. **Do not add.**

### Considered and Rejected: Cognitive Sequelae of the Sinister Procedure as Primary

A neurologist's differential would, properly, raise the possibility that some of what we are calling CPTSD-driven affect dysregulation and impulse control is in fact post-surgical sequelae from the brain tissue Sinister excised. Without imaging and without baseline neuropsych, we cannot exclude this. The honest formulation is that **iatrogenic neurological contribution is plausible but unquantifiable**, and should be priced into any treatment plan. If kinetic-charge dysregulation events were ever to recur, they would need both psychiatric and neurological workup, not one or the other.

---

## 4.6 Etiology — The Causal Stack

The etiological model has four superimposed layers.

**Layer one: Constitutional / genotypic.** Mutant genotype with structurally anomalous ocular presentation, producing **infant visual


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS: REMY ETIENNE LeBEAU

*An exhaustive catalog of observable behavior, decision habits, somatic tells, and micro-patterns across every documented state. Compiled longitudinally from the entire published record (Claremont, Nicieza, Lobdell, Mackie, Layman, Carey, Austen, David, Thompson, Duggan, Percy, Ewing). Cross-indexed by condition.*

---

## I. BASELINE / CALM STATE

The "calm" baseline is itself a performance — this must be flagged at the front of every observation. The subject does not have a private resting state visible to others; what observers read as relaxation is a maintained presentation, the lowest-energy version of his social mask. True baseline appears only in solo-issue interior captions and in vanishingly few panels where he believes himself unobserved (the rooftop smoke after a mission; the pre-dawn kitchen scene; the long stare into middle distance before Rogue enters the room).

### Posture and Carriage

- **Standing weight on the back foot, hips slightly canted**, hands rarely fully visible — one in a coat pocket, one near belt-line where a card-deck or staff-collapsed lives. The posture is Guild-trained: weight loaded for either a back-step (escape) or a hip-pivot (drawn weapon), never planted square. He stands like a man whose primary career has been *exits*.
- **Habitual lean.** Against doorframes, kitchen counters, the Blackbird's bulkhead, walls at parties. He does not stand in the middle of rooms by choice. Center-of-room exposure happens only when he is performing — flirting at full output, addressing a team, demonstrating something. When he stops performing he migrates to a margin within four to six seconds.
- **Head angled, chin slightly down, gaze upward through the brow.** Both a flirtation tell (the look-up-from-under) and a tactical habit: the upward visual sweep keeps him reading faces while presenting as deferential.
- **Walks with the heel-light, ball-of-foot gait of a trained thief.** Audible footfall is suppressed even on hard floors. Teammates have noted across decades that they do not hear him arrive in a room.

### The Hands

The hands are the single richest behavioral channel he possesses and the one he himself most carefully manages, because his hands are also his weapon.

- **Card-handling at all idle moments.** A deck or partial deck appears in his hands whenever both are free — riffle shuffles, single-card cuts, fan-and-collapse, the slow tumble of a single card across the knuckles (the "card walk"). This is *constant* and observers stop noticing it within days, which is one of its functions: he wants the hands to be assumed-busy so that their occasional emptiness is not read as significant.
- **No-deck substitutes:** a coin, a lighter (the Zippo specifically — the metallic *click-clack* of the lid is one of his auditory signatures), a chip of stone, a poker chip, a wedding band rotated on the finger (post-*Mr. and Mrs. X*).
- **Touch-discipline.** He does not casually brush against people. The man flirts continuously and touches *minimally* — a knuckle-graze to a cheek, fingertips to the small of a back, never an open palm in unguarded contact. This is post-Sinister-surgery vigilance grown into character: the open palm is the charged surface. Watch his hands at any team meal or gathering — they are almost never flat on a person or surface; they are *curled*, finger-pads inward, palm slightly cupped.
- **The exception that proves the rule:** with Rogue, particularly in the post-touch-restored period, he over-touches — palm-to-cheek, palm-to-palm, hand-on-her-hand-on-the-table — almost compulsively, *because he can*. This is one of the most reliable diagnostic behaviors in the file. With her, the discipline reverses.

### Voice and Speech

- **Pitch:** low baritone, soft-edged. Volume habitually low; he draws people in rather than projecting. Even in combat dialogue, his shouts are rare; he speaks across battlefields in the same conversational register he uses across a bar table.
- **The accent is a dial.** Baseline Cajun French-English admixture, but the depth is calibrated to audience. Around fellow Louisianans and intimates: lighter, more naturalistic, code-switched into actual Cajun French and Creole structures. Around outsiders and especially around the X-Men's Anglo-Eastern-Seaboard core: *thickened*. "Dis," "dat," "de," dropped subject pronouns, "p'tit," "mon ami," "chère." Verifiable by comparing his thought-captions (cleaner English, only occasional Cajun) to his dialogue in the same scene (full performance). The accent is **a costume he wears louder when he is more uncertain of the room**.
- **Third-person self-reference.** "Remy gon' handle it." "Remy don' need dat." Increases under stress, decreases in true intimacy. The grammatical distancing is a near-textbook dissociative move performed lightly enough to read as charm. He is most himself when he says "I."
- **The "chère" / "chèrie" / "p'tit" address.** Distributed broadly across women, children, and (rarely, ironically) men. With Rogue specifically, "chère" is downshifted in moments of true tenderness to a near-whispered "Anna" or "Anna-Marie" — the use of the real name is the tell that the performance has dropped.
- **Pet names and diminutives for everyone.** "Stormy" (Storm, who hates it, which is partly why he persists — affectionate provocation as bond-test). "Cyke." "Wolvie" occasionally. Naming is claiming; the diminutives map his social field.

### Eyes and Face

- **The eyes themselves are immutable** (black sclera, red iris) and cannot be controlled, which is significant: the most "tell" feature of his face is not actually under his management. He compensates by managing everything *around* the eyes — the brow lift, the eye-crinkle smile, the half-lidded look, the deliberate eye-closure when laughing. He has trained his face to direct attention toward the surrounding musculature so the eyes themselves are read as expressive rather than alien.
- **Smile is asymmetric**, higher on the right, with the eye-crinkle following half a beat behind the mouth — a "two-stroke" smile that observers experience as genuine because the delay reads as spontaneous; in fact it is the smile of a man whose mouth moves on social autopilot and whose eyes catch up when the brain decides whether to commit.
- **Tongue-in-cheek and slow blink** during conversational pauses — both buy thinking time and both code as flirtation.

### Sensory Habits

- **Scans every room on entry.** Exits first, then high vantage, then weapons-of-opportunity, then people. The whole sweep takes under three seconds and is invisible unless you know to look for the micro-head-turns. He cannot turn it off; he has done it entering his own kitchen.
- **Sits with back to wall, facing door.** Non-negotiable. He will move chairs at restaurants. If denied, he becomes mildly distracted for the rest of the meal.
- **Counts people in a space and re-counts every two to three minutes** in any environment he does not control. Tracked across his solo runs as a captioned habit.

---

## II. MILD STRESS

Mild stress is most of his waking life. The triggers are continuous: a teammate brings up the past, an unfamiliar face arrives, the news mentions New Orleans, Rogue is fifteen minutes late.

- **Accent thickens audibly.** Within a sentence or two of any mild stressor, the Cajun deepens. This is the earliest and most reliable tell. Anyone close to him for six months learns this; he knows they have learned it and does not stop, because the cost of suppressing it would be more expensive than the cost of being read.
- **Humor frequency increases, content sharpens.** Mild stress brings *more* jokes, faster, slightly more barbed — gentle teasing aimed sideways at the source of the stress rather than confronting it. He will joke about Sinister before he will mention him.
- **Card work accelerates.** Riffles get faster, the card-walk on the knuckles tightens, occasional small kinetic charge-and-discharge of a single card into an ashtray or empty cup as a controlled release. The charge-discharge is the somatic equivalent of an exhale.
- **Cigarette appears.** In the Claremont and Nicieza eras this is almost a guaranteed marker — mild stress, cigarette materializes within a minute. Later editorial environments suppress depiction but the oral fixation persists: toothpick, sucker, the chewing-on-the-inside-of-the-cheek tell, the slow chewing of ice from a drink.
- **Migrates to a margin.** Whatever conversation he was in the middle of, he will, within a minute or two of mild stress, be standing at the edge of the group — by a doorway, by a window, at the bar rather than at the table. He will continue the conversation from there. Others rarely notice the migration.
- **Flirtation becomes deflective rather than recreational.** Baseline flirtation is sociable, distributed, low-intensity. Stress-flirtation is *targeted* at whoever is closest to the threat-topic and is used to redirect the conversation. If you ask him about the Marauders and he flirts with you, you have hit something.

---

## III. MODERATE STRESS

Moderate stress is operational pressure — a mission going sideways, a teammate at risk, an old contact resurfacing, Bella Donna's name on a wire.

- **Goes quiet.** The chatter stops, the flirtation stops, the accent flattens slightly (the performance is too expensive to maintain). The voice drops further in pitch and volume. Teammates have learned across decades that **a quiet Gambit is a worried Gambit**; a Gambit talking through a fight is in his element.
- **Withdraws into operational competence.** He becomes more useful, not less. Plans tighten, movements economize, the body language goes from idle-lean to compact-efficient. He works alone when permitted, asks for solo recon assignments, volunteers for the dangerous adjunct.
- **Sleep degrades.** Already a poor sleeper, under moderate stress he simply does not sleep — takes unprompted watch shifts, stays up reading mission files he has already memorized, sits in the kitchen at three a.m. with a coffee or bourbon and the deck of cards. Rogue's documented complaint across multiple writers: she wakes alone.
- **Smoking, drinking, both increase.** Pattern: alone, late, methodical. Never to intoxication; the alcohol is a metronome for the rumination, not an escape from it.
- **Touches Rogue more, talks to her less.** Counterintuitive but consistent. When stressed, he reaches for her physically (hand on her back, fingers laced through hers, forehead briefly to her temple) but volunteers less verbally. He wants the proof of her presence; he does not want to be asked what is wrong, because the truthful answer is usually unspeakable to him.
- **Lock-picking, knot-tying, small mechanical fidgets** appear in addition to the card work. He will disassemble and reassemble a small device he carries — historically a thieves'-pick set, latterly a ring or a small folded knife — in the way other men click pens.

---

## IV. THREAT / COMBAT

Threat conditions produce the subject's *highest* observable functioning. He is, by every metric, more comfortable in a firefight than in a domestic conversation about feelings. The Atlas notes this without irony: combat is a domain in which the rules are legible, the consequences are immediate, and the demand is for competence rather than disclosure.

### Initial Threat Recognition

- **Posture compresses by perhaps an inch and a half.** Shoulders drop, weight settles forward onto the balls of both feet, hands come out of pockets in a single fluid motion — one to the bo staff at the small of the back or thigh, the other already producing a card from the deck or the inner coat.
- **Eyes go from social-soft to operational-flat.** The eye-crinkle disappears. The face goes still in a way that is more unsettling to civilians than any threatened violence — the *cessation* of the charm is itself a signal.
- **Verbal continues but pivots in content.** He keeps talking — *through* the threat assessment, through the engagement, sometimes through the entire fight. The talk is now tactical-and-distracting rather than social: drawing attention, baiting tempers, projecting confidence to allies, deniable threats to enemies. Combat patter is a Guild-trained instrument. He fights at the same conversational volume he flirts.

### Combat Movement

- **Mobile, lateral, oblique.** Almost never charges straight. The Guild template is the en garde of a fencer overlaid on the footwork of a street thief: in-and-out, around-and-behind, never planted, always with a clear exit lane.
- **Uses the environment compulsively.** Vaults, slides, rolls, parkour ascents to rooftops and rafters. He cannot resist *up* — the high vantage is the Guild reflex. He will spend an extra two seconds gaining a meter of elevation he did not strictly need.
- **Throws cards in flights of three to five,** rarely singly except for precision shots; uses the staff in the off-hand as both bludgeon and reach-extender.
