Switches dominant hand fluidly — ambidextrous by training, with a slight right-hand preference for the staff and a slight left-hand preference for card-throw release. This ambidexterity is itself a tell: he was *trained out of laterality*, which civilians never are.
- **Charges objects of opportunity** rather than relying solely on prepared decks: pebbles, coins, broken glass, his own coat buttons in extremis. The improvisational charging is a stress-graded behavior — the more dire the fight, the more inventive and the larger the charged object. Charging a large object is metabolically and neurologically expensive (and historically, the path back toward the pre-Sinister dysregulation), so its appearance is itself diagnostic of severity.

### Decision Habits in Combat

- **Will not kill if avoidable.** This is a *bright-line behavioral rule* and a remarkable one given his Guild training, in which lethality is an available tool. Post-Morlocks, he has organized his combat ethic around incapacitation, evasion, and the saving of bystanders. He will accept tactical losses to preserve this rule. Observers should note: when he *does* kill, it is information. He has chosen.
- **Triages toward the most vulnerable target on the field.** If there is a child, a civilian, a wounded teammate, his movement bends toward them within the first ten seconds of engagement, often before any team callout. He is one of the most reliable *unprompted* rescuers on the roster. This is reaction formation in its purest tactical expression — the man who once led killers into a tunnel of the defenseless now positions himself, every fight, between killers and the defenseless.
- **Accepts disproportionate personal risk** to extract teammates. Will draw fire, will play decoy, will stay behind to cover withdrawal. The "I'll catch up, chère, go" is a recurring beat across decades. Sometimes he does catch up. Sometimes he is captured or stranded. Both outcomes are acceptable to his operating system.
- **Beats telepaths in close work** because the Guild-trained mind-shielding is *layered* — false fronts, decoy memories, an inner room behind an inner room. Telepaths who breach his outer mind hit a constructed second self ("the thief") before they reach anything load-bearing. He has used this against Jean, against Emma, against hostile telepaths; the technique is consistent and remarkable. Behaviorally observable: when a telepath attempts him, his face goes blank-pleasant rather than tense — he is engaging the shield, which feels to him like *settling into a chair*.

### Post-Combat

- **Adrenal crash, well-managed.** Twenty to forty minutes after action ends, he goes quiet, finds a margin, lights up if circumstances allow, drinks water deliberately, and runs a body-check (palpates ribs, rolls shoulders, flexes hands) under the cover of casual stretching.
- **Will not debrief in detail immediately.** Asks for "a minute, chère" and takes ten. The deferred debrief is consistent; he needs to *file* before he can narrate.
- **Reaches out to confirm teammate status before reporting his own.** Will say "Rogue all right?" before "I caught a piece of shrapnel." Underreports own injuries by a factor that medical has learned to multiply.

---

## V. INTIMACY

The condition under which the subject is *least* competent and most observable. The defenses that perform flawlessly in combat misfire here, which is precisely diagnostic.

### Approach and Courtship Pattern

- **Closes distance by inches, never by leaps.** A courtship with him is measured in weeks of progressive proximity at the same dinner table, at the same kitchen counter, on the same training mat. The actual moment of physical escalation, when it comes, is preceded by an extraordinary amount of looking.
- **Asks questions, volunteers little.** A first hour with him at a bar yields the partner's entire life story and almost nothing of his. He is an exceptional listener; the listening is partly genuine interest, partly intelligence work, partly the avoidant strategy of running out the clock on the disclosure economy.
- **Self-deprecating disclosure as substitute.** He will tell you he is a thief. He will tell you he was thrown out of his city. He will tell you he has done bad things. He will say all of this in a tone that absolves you of having to take it seriously. The *load-bearing* truths — the Massacre, the Sinister bargain, the Death conversion — he does not voluntarily say. **What he discloses is calibrated to feel like intimacy without being it.**

### With Rogue Specifically

The entire relational arc is its own atlas. The key behaviors:

- **The years of yearning gap.** Touch impossibility weaponized as relational architecture. He courts in the register of the impossible, which is the only register in which he can court without risking the secret-discovery he fears. Hand-near-hand-not-touching is one of the most-drawn images in the X-Men canon and one of the most accurate to his actual preference: the *almost* is more comfortable for him than the *yes*.
- **Physical creativity within the constraint.** Gloves, scarves, sheets between palms, the trick of breath-on-neck rather than lips-on-neck. He treats the touch-prohibition as a puzzle to be solved partially, not as a barrier to be lamented continuously. This is one of his more attractive traits and one of his more revealing ones — he is *good at* incomplete intimacy, in a way that suggests practice predating Rogue.
- **The over-touch when touch becomes possible.** Already noted under baseline. Worth repeating because it is so consistent: he will not let go of her hand at the breakfast table. He will keep a palm on her back through whole conversations. The behavior reads as romantic and is partly that, but is also the body confirming, again and again, *I am allowed*.
- **He proposes, courts, marries — and gets quieter during.** The deepening of the relationship corresponds, observably, to a flattening of the performance. He uses fewer "chères" and more "Anna-Marie"s; the accent lightens; the third-person drops away. The marriage is the slow disassembly of the costume, and it visibly costs him to disassemble it, and it visibly relieves him.
- **The self-sabotage pulse.** Every two to three story-years, on average, he creates a rupture — a withheld truth surfaces, an old contact resurfaces, he disappears on a "case" without explanation. The pulse is consistent across decades and writers because it is rooted in the structural fact that *he does not believe the relationship is stable and tests it periodically to confirm*. Each surviving test produces a several-month period of unusual openness, which then decays back to baseline.

### With Children and the Marginal

- **Crouches to their eye level immediately.** Without thinking. This is the most consistent automatic kindness in his behavioral repertoire.
- **Softer voice, lighter accent, more direct gaze.** The performance reduces; he is more *himself* with children than with most adults.
- **Will not lie to a child** about anything load-bearing. Will deflect, will redirect, will say "Remy can' tell you dat right now, p'tit," but will not fabricate. A near-universal observation across the Marrow, Lil' Ro (de-aged Storm relationships), and various rescued-civilian arcs.
- **Hovers protectively without performing it.** Stations himself between child and door, between child and unknown adult, with a casualness that conceals the constancy.

---

## VI. GRIEF

Grief in this subject does not present loud. It presents as *organization* and *withdrawal*.

- **Becomes useful.** The bereaved Remy cleans, fixes, runs errands, takes patrols, organizes the funeral logistics nobody asked him to organize. Activity is the container.
- **Eats less, drinks slightly more, sleeps not at all.** The three-a.m. kitchen scene is the iconic grief tableau in his record. Bourbon neat, one finger, sipped slowly. The deck on the table, not in his hands. The deck *on the table* is itself the tell — he has stopped fidgeting, which means the internal pressure is high enough that the small motor outlet is insufficient.
- **Visits places, not people.** Goes back to physical sites associated with the lost — a New Orleans corner, a Westchester clearing, a Krakoan gate. The grief is geographically anchored.
- **Does not cry in company.** The record contains very few panels of him weeping, and almost all of them are private — alone on a rooftop, alone in the Antarctic snow, alone in the dark of a bedroom with Rogue asleep. When grief surfaces in company, it surfaces as a single hard exhale, a turning away, a "Remy need a minute," and a walk out of the room.
- **Returns to the Cajun deeper.** Speaks Cajun French to himself in private. The language of the people who first did not choose him is the language he returns to when chosen company is gone.
- **Increased physical risk-acceptance for several weeks following.** Grief Remy is the most likely to volunteer for the bad mission. The Antarctica-acceptance template is partly a grief response — grief at himself, but the mechanism generalizes.

---

## VII. VICTORY

Victory is the condition he handles worst after intimacy. He does not know what to do with unalloyed wins.

- **Deflects credit instantly and reflexively** to teammates, often with self-deprecating humor. "Stormy did de hard part. Remy just t'rew some cards." This is partly grace, partly the genuine team ethic, and partly the *refusal to accept positive valence* that pairs with his refusal-of-absolution. To accept full credit for a win would imply he is the kind of person who earns wins.
- **Migrates to the margin of the celebration** within ten minutes of arriving. Will buy the round, will toast, will then be found outside smoking or on a balcony alone, ostensibly "givin' de young ones some room." The pattern is consistent across team-victory celebrations in the Claremont, Nicieza, and Krakoa eras.
- **Becomes mildly melancholic some hours after the win.** Captioned across multiple solo runs: the win triggers the rumination that he does not deserve to be among the winning. This is the most counterintuitive behavioral pattern in his file and one of the most diagnostic: *he is sadder after victories than after defeats*.


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 6
## DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS
### *What a Week of Surveillance Would Record*

---

## 6.0 Preliminary Note on Method

The subject is the single most surveillance-resistant member of his cohort, not because he lives in hiding — he does not — but because his daily life is constructed of *small habits of misdirection* baked into otherwise ordinary motion. He does not break pattern when watched; he never had a clean pattern to break. The Guild training is visible in the geometry of his day: he walks the same route twice in a week with two different gaits; he sits in the same café and orders differently; he leaves a hotel room "lived in" within forty minutes of check-in so any later observer cannot date his arrival from the room. What follows is the underlying schedule the observer would, with patient longitudinal work, eventually extract from the noise.

---

## 6.1 The Diurnal Cycle

### Wake

Subject wakes early but not regularly — between 04:40 and 06:30 depending on which time-zone-of-the-mind he went to bed in. He does not use alarms. He surfaces in stages: a stillness of perhaps ninety seconds in which the only movement is the eyes opening and the head not turning, during which he inventories the room by sound (HVAC, refrigeration cycle, footfall above, traffic) before any visible motion. Anyone sharing the bed learns this is not coldness but a tic; he resumes contact as soon as the inventory completes.

He is *bad* at sleep. The chronic sleep deficit is the somatic backbone of the dossier. Across the entire published record he is shown taking night watch unprompted, working in the dark, reading at small lamps, walking the perimeter of whatever structure houses him at unsociable hours. Even in stable periods (the *Mr. and Mrs. X* domestic phase, the Krakoa years), the pattern of waking once around 02:00–02:30, moving through the residence for ten to twenty minutes, then returning to bed, is consistent and decades-old. He calls this "checking the doors." There are not always doors.

### First Hour

The first hour after rising is the most ritualized hour of his day and the most diagnostically rich.

- **Cigarette or, in periods of reduction, an unlit one held in the fingers.** The oral fixation is regulatory. In editorial environments where smoking has been reduced or excised he is observed with toothpicks, matches, drinking straws, a thin reed of cut sugarcane (a New Orleans tell), or — telling — a playing card turned end-over-end across the knuckles.
- **Coffee.** Strong, dark, made by him personally even when others are awake. He does not trust coffee made by other people. This is a small Guild residue: prepared food and drink are points of compromise; you make your own or you watch it being made.
- **Window check.** Subject visits each window of his current residence within the first fifteen minutes of waking. He does not pull the curtain — he looks *through* it from oblique angle. This is sub-conscious; he is unaware he does it; he has done it in every documented residence from Salem Center to the Marauders bridge.
- **Hand work.** Within the first thirty minutes he has handled a deck of cards. Riffle, cut, fan, spring, cascade — short movements, no audience. The cards function as a quiet hand-warmup for the kinetic governor; he is verifying that the charge sits where it should and does not bleed into the cardstock. The day he forgets to do this is the day his power-control is in trouble.

### Grooming & Self-Presentation

- **Shaves rarely; trims regularly.** The visible stubble across the canon is curated, not neglected. There is a difference, observable across panels, between his three-day stubble (curated) and his post-mission seven-day growth (decompression).
- **Hair.** Auburn, kept at jaw-to-shoulder length, never short. The length is operational as well as aesthetic — it breaks the silhouette and the face, which matters for a man whose eyes mark him at fifty yards. He runs both hands through it once on rising and once before leaving any room. The second pass is the tell of imminent departure.
- **Eye coverage.** When civilian, sunglasses. He owns more pairs of sunglasses than any other item of clothing — observed across decades. The amber-lensed aviators are most frequent. Indoors he prefers low ambient light, and will adjust lamps downward on entry to a room without comment.
- **Wardrobe.** Layered. Always layered. Even in heat he wears at minimum two layers, because the trench coat / duster is identity-bearing and the inner layer is operational (concealment). The coat is functionally a tool-roll — interior pockets carry decks of cards (between two and five at any time, in varying conditions of preparation), the collapsible bo staff in a custom inner sleeve along the spine, lockpicks (tension wrenches in the cuff, picks behind the lapel), a small folding knife, occasionally tobacco, a folded bandana, and a single photograph he will not let you see.

### Movement Through the Day

The subject does not commute in any straight line he can avoid. Observed pattern: he leaves a residence, walks one block in the wrong direction, doubles back through an adjacent block, and only then takes his actual route. He calls no attention to this; if asked, he says he likes the air. Surveillance teams over a week will record this as fact: **he never takes the same route twice in succession to any location he visits more than twice in a week.**

He prefers walking to driving; driving to flying. He drives well, fast, and with a peculiar attentiveness to the rearview that is not paranoia per se but trained habit. When he does drive he prefers motorcycles or low-slung vintage muscle — not for image but because the seating posture suits a man who is always slightly leaning forward, ready to be elsewhere.

Public transit he uses gladly. He reads other passengers compulsively and silently — observe his eye-pattern across a subway car and you can extract his threat-ranking of every person in it within ninety seconds. He gives up his seat to elderly and pregnant passengers reliably and quickly. He does not engage in conversation with strangers on transit; this is one of the few public domains in which he is not "on."

---

## 6.2 The Weekly Skeleton

A week of close surveillance, after the noise is averaged out, would resolve into the following:

**Daily, every day, without fail:**
- Hand-warmup with cards (multiple times — on rising, mid-morning, before any operational engagement, before bed).
- Window/perimeter check on rising and before sleep.
- A minimum of one solo walk of forty-five minutes to two hours, no destination, often at dusk or after dark. This is his thinking-time. He will fight to preserve it. Interrupted, he is short.
- Contact with Rogue. Even when apart on mission, daily — call, signal, message, or the equivalent in whatever communications medium the era affords. The longest documented voluntary gap between contacts is roughly seventy-two hours and is associated with arcs of acute relational rupture. The pattern is otherwise unbroken.
- Personal weapons & tools check. Cards inspected and rotated through the coat pockets (worn cards retired; he does not throw a card he does not trust the edge of); staff checked for the joint mechanism; picks oiled lightly with a single drop from a small vial kept in the coat.

**Several times per week:**
- Physical training. Solo, early, light by superhero standards but technically dense — emphasis on agility, joint-lock work, blade defense, staff forms with a recognizably bo-jutsu and Savate hybrid. He spars willingly but does not initiate. He prefers training alone.
- Cooking. He cooks for himself or for company a minimum of three nights a week when domestic conditions allow. Cooking is the second-most-ritualized activity in his life after the hand-warmup. He cooks Louisianan — gumbo, étouffée, jambalaya, red beans on Mondays (this last is the deepest Cajun-Creole calendar habit and is observed even on bases and ships where the ingredients must be requisitioned). The roux is made personally and at length; he does not delegate the roux. He cooks while drinking a single beer, never two.
- A long bath or a long shower, depending on mood. He does not rush water.
- Music. Zydeco, blues, jazz, occasionally older French chanson. He plays it low. He does not sing in front of others; he hums while cooking.

**Approximately weekly:**
- A bar or café visit, solo, for two to four hours. He sits with his back to a wall, with sight lines to all exits, with a drink he nurses, and he reads the room. This is not work; it is rest *as he understands rest*. The cognitive load of reading the room is the load he is comfortable carrying; the absence of that load is what makes ordinary downtime difficult for him.
- A card session. Either solo (practicing manipulations on a felt surface for hours) or in low-stakes social play. He does not gamble seriously for money among friends; he does gamble seriously among strangers, and wins, and tips heavily, and leaves.
- A long letter, message, or call to someone in the Louisiana network — Tante Mattie if she is in continuity, Mercy LeBeau, Henri's family, a Guild contact. The maintenance of the New Orleans line is non-negotiable even across decades of exile.

**Monthly or near-monthly:**
- A trip, if possible, to or toward New Orleans. The pull is gravitational and irrespective of welcome.
- A solo night in which he drinks more than is usual for him. This night is predictably timed to anniversaries (the Massacre, the wedding-day duel, the death of Belladonna's brother, the day of his Antarctica abandonment). He does not announce these. Rogue knows them. Storm knows two of them. No one else is told.

---

## 6.3 Habits of Place

### The Residence

Whatever space he lives in is arranged in the same way regardless of architecture:

- **One chair faces the door, with a sightline to at least one window.** This is his chair. Guests offered it will, if observant, notice his discomfort when they take it; he will not ask them to move.
- **Light is low and warm.** Overhead fluorescents are turned off and replaced with lamp light wherever possible. He travels with a small lamp in his luggage when residency is temporary.
- **No clutter on horizontal surfaces near doors and windows.** A surface near an egress must be available for the placement and retrieval of an object at speed. He does not articulate this rule; he enforces it by quietly relocating any object that violates it.
- **A deck of cards within arm's reach of any seat he uses regularly.** Multiple decks across the residence. Worn, half-worn, fresh — staged at different conditions.
- **One drawer or box, locked or hidden, containing the photograph(s) and a small set of items from New Orleans.** The contents vary by era; the existence of the drawer does not. He visits it rarely; he checks that it is intact often.
- **Kitchen well-stocked with the specific items required for the Louisianan repertoire** — file powder, andouille if obtainable, holy trinity vegetables, hot sauce in quantities other residents would find alarming, a cast-iron skillet that travels with him.
- **Bedroom curtains heavy and full-coverage.** He cannot sleep in a room with any external light source. This is non-negotiable and observed across the entire residential record.

### Public Space

In any public interior he enters, he performs within ninety seconds:

1. Identify all exits.
2. Identify the most defensible seat (back to wall, sightline to primary entrance, secondary sightline to secondary exit).
3. Rank the threat-relevant persons present (armed; trained; intoxicated; agitated; concealed).
4. Locate at least two improvised exits beyond the obvious ones (kitchen door, window with manageable drop, service corridor).

He is unaware he does any of this until questioned, at which point he can produce the inventory perfectly. The Guild trained the procedure below the level of conscious effort by repetition before age twelve.

### Outdoor Space

He prefers water. Rivers, harbors, swamps, the open ocean. Bridges are favored walking destinations. He will, given a choice, route any solo walk to cross water at least once. The captaincy of the Marauders' ship in later eras is, by his own private accounting, the easiest billet of his career partly for this reason: the water is constant and below him.

He dislikes deserts and high-altitude cold. The Antarctica residue is permanent; he is observed, decades after, to layer aggressively in any cold environment and to become unusually quiet in snow.

---

## 6.4 Habits of Time

The subject's relationship to clocks is functional, not affective. He is reliably *on time* for operations and reliably *late* for social occasions — by ten to twenty minutes, never more, and always with an entrance that converts the lateness into a gift. This is performance. He arrived on time and waited around the corner.

Anniversaries dominate his calendar privately. The Massacre date he treats as a fast day — observable to anyone tracking his intake: he eats very little, drinks water and coffee, smokes more, sleeps less, takes a longer walk than usual, and is absent from social gatherings without elaborate excuse. He will accept company on this day from Rogue and from no one else.

Mardi Gras and the deep Catholic calendar still organize him whether he professes belief or not. Lent is observable — a small abstention, usually from one specific pleasure, undertaken without announcement. Christmas Eve is observed; Christmas Day he treats as a working day. All Saints' / All Souls' he marks by visiting a cemetery if one is reachable; he leaves no flowers; he stands for a while and leaves.

---

## 6.5 Communication & Speech Patterns Across the Day

His accent thickens and thins by audience and stress, and this is *measurable* across the canon by comparing dialogue caption to thought caption. Alone, in interior monologue, the accent is mild — recognizable but light, the Cajun-Creole syntax present but the orthographic markers (the dropped *th*, the *dis/dat*, the *chere*) reduced. In dialogue with non-Louisianans the markers double. The thickening is not unconscious; it is *deployed*. It serves three functions: (a) it sets him as Other and exotic, which front-loads charm into the first thirty seconds of any encounter; (b) it gives interlocutors a frame of reference that organizes their expectations of him along folksy lines, which he then exploits or subverts at will; (c) it produces a small acoustic and rhythmic distance between the speaking-Remy and the thinking-Remy, which is its own form of compartmentalization.

He refers to himself in the third person under specific conditions: when flirting (deflection), when distressed (dissociation-adjacent), and when discussing past actions for which he holds himself responsible (the grammatical distancing of an accountant of guilt). "Gambit, he done that" is, in his mouth, a *confession* dressed as a verbal tic.

He uses pet names ("chere," "p'tit," "mon ami") with great precision. "Chere" is for Rogue, principally and almost exclusively in the load-bearing sense; deployed to others it is theater. "P'tit" is for those he is protecting and reads as smaller-than-him in either age or vulnerability. "Mon ami" is for peers whose loyalty he is acknowledging. The vocabulary is intimate currency carefully spent.

He laughs easily and falsely in public and rarely and quietly in private. The real laugh is observable in domestic Rogue scenes and in the small handful of canon moments with Storm and Logan in which he is genuinely at ease — it is shorter, lower, and more startled than the public laugh.

---

## 6.6 Eating, Drinking, Smoking

**Eating.** Two large meals a day, breakfast often skipped or reduced to coffee and toast. Lunch frequently missed when working. Dinner is sacred and usually late. He eats *slowly* — Guild training; a fast eater is an unaware eater — and he finishes his plate. He does not eat sweet things often; when he does, it is beignet, pralines, bread pudding, things rooted in place. He drinks water constantly throughout the day, a small but consistent tell of the Antarctica/dehydration residue.

**Drinking.** Bourbon is the default; beer is the social lubricant; wine he tolerates with food; cocktails he can mix competently and will order rarely. He nurses drinks. He has been depicted intoxicated perhaps a handful of times across thirty-five years of canon, and each instance is correlated with acute loss (Rogue rupture, exposure of the Massacre, Antarctica aftermath, the death of certain New Orleans figures). He does not become hostile drunk; he becomes quiet, then truthful, then sad, then absent.

**Smoking.** When permitted by the editorial environment, cigarettes — never more than half a pack a day, often less, but with peaks under stress that approach a full pack. He smokes outside or by an open window; he is fastidious about not smoking near food or near children. He extinguishes carefully and pockets the butt as often as he discards it (Guild residue: leave no trace). In environments where he has cut back, the substitutions are visible: toothpicks, matches turned in the mouth, sugarcane reeds, the cards.

---

## 6.7 The Domestic Register (with Rogue)

The *Mr. and Mrs. X* / Krakoa-era and later domesticity records what a stabilized version of the subject looks like. The patterns shift but do not disappear:

- He still rises at irregular early hours; he is quieter about it, leaving the bed without waking her, returning before she stirs.
- He makes the morning coffee for two now and brings hers to her side of the bed. This is one of the most consistent observable rituals of the marriage.
- He cooks more, not less. The cooking is now partly performance of provision — he is *feeding her*, which carries weight he does not articulate.
- The window check persists.
- The perimeter walk persists.
- The night walks shorten and become *with her* when she is awake and willing, *alone* when she sleeps; he no longer takes the long solo walks of the bachelor years.
- The cards remain. They sit by every chair. She has learned to riffle them, badly, and he watches her practice with an expression his teammates rarely see.
- Physical contact, freed by the resolution of the touch problem, is *constant and small* — a hand at the small of her back, a brush of fingers at the wrist, a touch to her hair in passing. He is making up, daily, for the years of structurally prohibited contact, and he does not seem to know he is doing it. To Rogue this is the most legible love language he has.

He still does not tell her the new versions of the old secrets quickly. He still tries. He is, by his own private accounting, better at it than he was, and the gap between intention and execution is the gap inside which the marriage does its real work.

---

## 6.8 The Operational Register (On Mission)

On mission he becomes a different organism — or rather, a more concentrated version of the same one. The flirtation drops by perhaps eighty percent. The accent thins. The body quiets. He moves with the spare, low-amplitude economy of a man who was taught before he was old enough to remember being taught.

- He volunteers for reconnaissance and infiltration roles and accepts them readily.
- He works best in pairs or alone; in larger group ops he tends to drift to the perimeter, which is operationally useful and personally preferred.
- He carries a smaller load on mission than at rest — fewer cards (the ones carried are battle-prepared and lightly pre-charged at the edge of his control), the staff, the picks, the knife, a sidearm only when the mission requires it (he has no love of guns).
- He is *first* to volunteer for the morally compromised job. Always. This is observable across his entire team-affiliated history. The penance is operationalized.
- He sleeps even less on mission. He takes more watches than his share. He does not complain about this and resents being relieved.
- Post-mission, he requires twelve to thirty-six hours of solo decompression. He will be physically present and conversationally light, but the long walk, the long bath, the long cigarette, the longer silence, are non-negotiable. Interrupted, he tolerates it; granted, he integrates faster.

---

## 6.9 What the Week Would Look Like, Compressed

A surveillance team running a full seven days on the subject in a stable domestic period would record, in aggregate:

- Approximately 38–42 hours of sleep across seven nights, fragmented, with at least four nights interrupted by a 02:00 perimeter walk.
- Approximately 50 cigarettes (in eras permitting) or 200+ instances of substitute oral fixation behavior.
- Between 6 and 9 solo walks of 45+ minutes, most beginning at dusk or after dark, most routing across water.
- 4–5 home-cooked meals of identifiable Louisianan derivation; one of which is red beans, on Monday.
- 5–7 instances of contact with Rogue when separated; near-constant low-level contact when not.
- 1–2 long café/bar sits, solo, back-to-wall.
- 1 card-practice session of an hour or more, solo, felt surface, no audience.
- 1 contact maintained with the New Orleans network.
- 1 visit to the hidden drawer / box, brief, unobserved by housemates.
- At least 14 window/perimeter checks (twice daily, never missed).
- Zero instances of his preferred route to any location being walked twice.
- One quiet refusal of an order or request he reads as wrong, executed by non-performance rather than by argument.
- One small kindness to a child or marginal person, unprompted, unreported, undocumented by him.

This is the shape of his life: the criminal's discipline reorganized into the penitent's calendar, the charm carried like a tool through a day whose underlying geometry is built to keep him useful, keep him watching the doors, keep him within reach of the woman who knows, and keep him — at every hour and in every small habit — one cigarette and one card-cut and one perimeter walk further away from the man who once led the Marauders into the tunnels.

He is, in the end, a man living a *very orderly life* on top of a wound he does not expect to close, and the order is the dressing.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# UATU DOSSIER — REMY ETIENNE LeBEAU ("GAMBIT")
## Section IV-A — Relationships I: Family & Origin Bonds

> *Preface.* The subject's family map is unusual in that it contains no biological members the subject acknowledges, almost no relationships untouched by transactional logic, and a startling number of caregiver-coded figures who at various points have tried to kill him, sell him, recruit him, or convert him into a weapon. The pattern across all of them — without exception — is that affection in this subject's life has always arrived bundled with use. The dossier below maps each origin bond on the dimensions of (a) documented history, (b) operational dynamic, (c) longitudinal evolution, (d) trust/safety register, (e) characteristic failure mode, and (f) exploitable leverage. The map is dense because the subject's interior is dense; he is a man who carries every one of these people, alive or dead, in his ribcage at all times.

---

### IV-A.1 — The Biological Parents (Unknown / Absent)

**History.** No name, no record, no face. The published canon is consistent on this: the subject was abandoned at or proximate to birth, his unusual ocular phenotype the operative cause as reconstructed via Tante Mattie's later commentary (he was, in the local idiom, marked *le diable blanc* — the white devil child — and discarded accordingly). The subject has, across thirty-plus years of publication, asked after them exactly zero times on panel in any sustained way. He has never undertaken a search. He has refused, on multiple occasions, opportunities to investigate (Sinister, who almost certainly knows or could know, has never been asked).

**Dynamic.** This is the *negative space* relationship — the one defined by the subject's refusal to make it real. The absence is so total that it has become a load-bearing wall in his architecture: he does not have to mourn parents he never claims to have had. The biological parents exist for him as an abstract verdict (*I was given up because of what I am*) rather than as people. The verdict is what he carries; the people are kept successfully unreal.

**Evolution.** Static. The single most notable longitudinal fact about this relationship is that it does not evolve. Across pubescent confession, adult crisis, marriage, near-death, conversion-to-Horseman, and rehabilitation — the subject does not turn toward this question. This is itself diagnostically loud. A man who turns toward every other wound does not turn toward this one. The inference is that the abandonment-verdict is so structurally foundational to his self-concept (*I was correctly identified at birth as something to throw away*) that to investigate would risk either confirming the verdict in unbearable specificity or — worse — discovering it was contingent, banal, or reversible, which would obligate a reorganization of the whole interior the file maps below.

**Trust / Safety.** Not applicable; no relational object exists. This is the most psychologically dangerous category of "absent figure" — a phantom limb that the subject has learned to keep numb.

**Failure mode.** Not failure of the relationship; failure of the subject's relation to the *category*. He has organized his life around the assumption that primary caregivers will use him; he has never tested the counterfactual of what it would mean to have had primary caregivers who simply loved him. He cannot test it without disturbing the foundation.

**Leverage.** Significant but volatile. Any operator presenting credible information about the biological parents would produce a behavioral effect difficult to model in advance — he could collapse, could refuse, could go violent. Sinister has historically refrained from playing this card, which is itself instructive: Sinister, who understands him better than anyone, judges this leverage too unpredictable to risk degrading the asset. Recommend the same restraint.

---

### IV-A.2 — Jean-Luc LeBeau (Adoptive Father; Patriarch, Thieves Guild)

**History.** The man who took the infant from the hands of the street-network and brought him into the LeBeau household — the patron, the patriarch, the king-of-thieves of New Orleans, and the only figure in the subject's life who can be described, without major qualification, as *father*. Per *Gambit* Vol. 1 (Nicieza, 1993), Vol. 3 (Nicieza, 1999), and the Layman 2004 run, Jean-Luc trained Remy from earliest childhood in the full Guild curriculum: lock work, sleight, knife, three-card monte, social engineering, the Cant, the Code, and the political theology of the Guild's relationship with the Assassins. He arranged the marriage to Bella Donna. He exiled the subject after the Julien duel, in accordance with Guild law. He has, across the published years, received the subject back into the family on multiple occasions, often grudgingly, always conditionally.

**Dynamic.** Love mediated through institution. Jean-Luc loves the subject — the evidence is consistent and the affect, when it appears, is unfeigned — but the love is structurally inseparable from Guild logic. He raised Remy to be the prophesied bridge between Guilds (per the *Tithe* / *Prophecy* arcs); he raised him as son *and* as instrument, and never resolved the contradiction in the boy's favor. Jean-Luc is the figure who taught the subject the foundational and devastating lesson: *the same hand that strokes your hair tonight will frisk you tomorrow.* The subject's adult conviction that to be valued is to be used originates here, with a man who genuinely valued him and who genuinely used him, both at full intensity, simultaneously.

**Evolution.**
- *Childhood:* idealization, mimicry, eagerness to please, demonstration of skill for paternal approval. The subject's craftsmanship as a thief is, on close reading of the flashbacks, a continuous performance of *look what I can do, Papa.*
- *Adolescence:* introduction of the bargain economy — affection contingent on Guild service. The subject begins, here, to develop the dual-track self (performed self / withheld self) he will carry forever.
- *The Marriage / Exile:* Jean-Luc enforces Guild law over fatherly partiality. The subject *accepts* this. Not because he agrees the law is right, but because he has been pre-conditioned to accept punishment as the price of belonging anywhere.
- *Reconciliations (mid-90s through Krakoa era):* a slow, partial, never-complete restoration. The two men work together; they speak in the Cant; they perform sons-and-fathers theater for the Guild; but the subject does not, ever, fully give Jean-Luc the interior. There is a permanent thickness of glass.
- *Latest era:* mutual respect, distance maintained by the subject. Jean-Luc has aged; the subject visits; affection is real and limited.

**Trust / Safety.** Moderate trust on operational matters within Guild domain; near-zero trust on matters of the subject's interior. Jean-Luc has never been told about Sinister, the Massacre, the Horseman conversion in any depth, or the full content of the Antarctica period. The subject protects Jean-Luc from this information *and* protects himself from Jean-Luc's reaction to it. Safety register: physically safe in Jean-Luc's presence; emotionally guarded at full clamp.

**Failure mode.** Whenever Guild interest and personal interest diverge, Jean-Luc will choose the Guild. The subject knows this and has built his expectations around it. The failure mode is not betrayal — it is *predictable subordination of him to the institution*, which the subject treats as a feature of reality rather than as a wound to be addressed.

**Leverage.** Operationally significant. A credible threat to Jean-Luc would produce rapid mobilization. A credible request *from* Jean-Luc, framed in the Cant and in Guild-honor terms, has a much higher probability of compliance from the subject than the same request framed any other way. The Guild-honor channel is the most reliable nontelepathic route to behavior modification in this subject and the most underestimated by non-Louisianan adversaries.

---

### IV-A.3 — Henri LeBeau (Adoptive Older Brother)

**History.** Jean-Luc's biological son; the subject's older brother by adoption; the brother who, by every available indicator across the Nicieza solo era, *welcomed* the foundling without reservation. Henri taught Remy the practical thieving curriculum at street level (the formal curriculum came from Jean-Luc; the *real* curriculum — how to run from cops, how to fence, how to lie to a girl — came from Henri). He stood up for Remy in Guild politics. He died — murder, in the early 1990s in the Tithe arc, hands of the Assassins Guild in the cyclic Guild war Remy's exile failed to prevent.

**Dynamic.** This is the subject's only documented experience of *uncomplicated* familial love. Henri did not use him. Henri was not measuring him for a destiny. Henri was, in the strict sense, *family without bargain*. The subject knows this and has held it as the lone interior referent for what an unconditioned love between persons could look like.

**Evolution.** Living era: collaborative, warm, mutually protective, mutually amused. Death: catastrophic loss, partially metabolized through Guild ritual, never psychologically resolved. The subject's later protectiveness toward team-younger-brothers (varying X-roster members across runs; arguably echoed in his Krakoa-era mentorship modes) is in part the Henri-shaped slot being filled by replacements who never know they are replacements.

**Trust / Safety.** Total, retrospectively. Henri is the *only* figure in the family map about whom the subject's interior shows zero defensive structure. He is also the only figure who is not available to confirm or disconfirm the subject's idealization, which makes the idealization stable.

**Failure mode.** Henri's death is the failure mode. The subject privately holds the conviction — never voiced and not fully formed — that had he not killed Julien Boudreaux and triggered the exile, the Guild war could have been contained and Henri would have lived. This is a small private moral debt running alongside the larger Morlock debt, and the two reinforce each other.

**Leverage.** Posthumous. Invocation of Henri's name or memory by a credible party produces immediate and unguarded affective response — one of the very few stimuli that pierces the subject's charm-layer in real time. Use is high-yield and high-cost: he will not forgive cynical instrumentalization, and Henri's name is sacred ground.

---

### IV-A.4 — Mercy LeBeau (Adoptive Sister-in-Law; Henri's Widow)

**History.** Henri's wife, the subject's sister-in-law, a senior Guild operator in her own right; surviving member of the inner LeBeau household after Henri's murder. Her relationship with Remy across the canon is depicted as warm, loyal, and protective — the surviving co-keeper of Henri's memory.

**Dynamic.** Mercy is one of two adult women in the subject's life (the other being Tante Mattie) toward whom he expresses tenderness with no flirtation overlay. The absence of flirtation is diagnostically loud — flirtation is his default social register, and its absence indicates a register of *family proper*, the small sealed category where charm is not deployed because it is not needed and would be insulting.

**Evolution.** Stable across decades. Mercy is among the few constants in the subject's life. She has carried Henri's authority into the post-Henri era; she is, in some Guild dynamics, the senior LeBeau-by-marriage when Jean-Luc is absent. The subject defers to her in matters of family memory.

**Trust / Safety.** High trust on personal matters within the family frame; the subject is more likely to admit fatigue, fear, or doubt to Mercy than to any other Louisianan in his life. This is not the same as full disclosure — Mercy, too, does not know the Morlock truth — but the range of admissible affect is wider with her than with Jean-Luc.

**Failure mode.** Their bond is, fundamentally, *mediated by the dead.* If the Henri-shaped center were ever displaced (e.g., by Mercy remarrying, by a Guild realignment that pitted her interests against the subject's), the bond's resilience is untested. The published record suggests it would hold, but the prediction is extrapolation, not data.

**Leverage.** Mid-range. Threat to Mercy invokes the Henri-protection circuit; request from Mercy carries family-honor weight comparable to but distinct from Jean-Luc's. Mercy can ask the subject to come home in a way no one else can.

---

### IV-A.5 — Theoren, Etienne, and the Wider LeBeau / Guild Cousinry

**History.** A diffuse cousin/uncle/elder network appearing intermittently across the Nicieza solo runs and the Tithe arc. Theoren Marceaux and others operate as Guild middle management; Etienne Marceaux (the cousin) appears in younger flashbacks. Etienne's death — in the *Externals* / X-Cutioner's Song-adjacent flashbacks, killed during an early job that went catastrophic — is one of the subject's chronologically earliest documented exposures to peer-loss-by-his-own-association.

**Dynamic.** Functional kin-network ties, ranging from warm (cousin level) to coolly professional (Guild middle management). The Etienne death is the operative item: it pre-dates the Morlock Massacre and rehearses the same structural lesson in miniature — *people I love die when they come close to my work.*

**Evolution.** Largely off-panel maintenance; the subject sustains these ties with the same reliability he sustains all chosen family bonds. The Etienne grief is not a continuous live wound but a low-grade chronic ache, integrated into the broader self-blame substrate.

**Trust / Safety.** Variable; calibrated person-by-person; default Guild-trust (which is conditional and Cant-mediated, not interior-disclosure).

**Failure mode.** Standard Guild-politics failure: any of them could, under sufficient pressure, sell him out. The subject prices this in.

**Leverage.** Low individual, moderate collective. The Guild as a whole is leverage. Individuals within it are not.

---

### IV-A.6 — Tante Mattie

**History.** The street-mystic / healer / Guild-adjacent matriarch figure who, in multiple tellings, was either present at the subject's earliest infancy or entered his life shortly thereafter, providing the spiritual / folk-Catholic / hoodoo-syncretic framework that constitutes the subject's actual functioning religious cosmology. She named him *le diable blanc* in a sense that, in her usage, was protective rather than condemnatory — she identified the marking and chose to mother through it rather than discard because of it.

**Dynamic.** Tante is the *closest thing in his life to an unconditioned maternal figure*, and her place in the file is correspondingly load-bearing. She is the one origin-period adult who appears to have valued him for his existence rather than his utility. Critically, she did not raise him as her own — she ceded him to the LeBeau household — and so the relationship operates as *blessing-figure* more than *parent*: the woman who sees him clearly and does not look away, but who is not the one who feeds and houses.

**Evolution.** Periodic returns across the canon, particularly during Louisiana-arc storylines. Each return functions as a brief reset — the subject visits Tante and receives, without asking, some form of frank assessment and folk-spiritual maintenance. He leaves quieter than he arrived. The relationship has not evolved so much as it has *persisted* in a register the subject has not allowed any other relationship to occupy.

**Trust / Safety.** The highest in the file, qualitatively. Tante is the one person to whom he has, in the published record, come closest to voluntary disclosure of interior material. He does not unburden completely even to her — the full Sinister-Marauders content remains compartmented — but in her presence the charm layer drops to its lowest baseline observable in any setting.

**Failure mode.** Tante's eventual death (anticipated, not yet definitively in canon at all points) would remove the only living person in the family map who functions as a no-bargain mother. The clinical prediction is that her loss would precipitate either a depressive episode of significant depth or a regression toward exploitative-mentor susceptibility (see Section 4, Risk Profile).

**Leverage.** Asymmetric. Tante cannot be used *against* him by adversaries without provoking lethal-grade response; Tante can ask of him almost anything and receive it. She is among the very few human routes into him that bypass the charm-layer entirely.

---

### IV-A.7 — Fabian / Sinister as Surrogate "Father" (cross-referenced; full treatment in Section IV-C: Antagonists & Captors)

**Brief, with redirect.** Nathaniel Essex / Mr. Sinister enters this file under *family* with explicit caveat: he is not family, he is the parodic mockery of family, but he *functions* in the subject's interior as a surrogate-father figure whose hold is structurally identical to the original-paternal hold (offers control, demands service, withholds disclosure of true cost). The subject, in the surgical-debt period, related to Sinister as one relates to a powerful father one cannot escape and whose approval one has been conditioned to seek even when one knows him to be monstrous. This is the most dangerous relationship in the subject's history and is treated at full length in the Antagonists section. It is noted here because *the subject himself, in moments of unguarded interiority across the Carey run, has coded Sinister in paternal grammar* — and this is the single most clinically alarming datum in the file.

---

### IV-A.8 — Bella Donna Boudreaux (First Wife — Annulled / Disputed; cross-referenced with IV-B: Intimate Bonds)

**Brief here, because the bond originates in *family-of-origin* logic before it becomes a romantic relationship.** The arranged marriage was a Guild-political act, not a courtship — Bella Donna entered Remy's life as *betrothed-since-childhood*, a fixture of his family map before she was a fixture of his romantic one. Their childhood bond was real and mutually affectionate; the marriage itself, on the day, dissolved into the duel with Julien and the exile. Bella Donna's later trajectory — Assassins Guild matriarch, recurrent antagonist, intermittent ally, perpetual ex-wife — keeps her in the family-bordering category throughout the canon. Full romantic treatment is held for Section IV-B; here, note only that she is the figure through whom *family and lethality first fused* for the adult subject, and that this fusion is the template every subsequent intimate relationship is fitted against.

---

### IV-A.9 — Julien Boudreaux (Brother-in-Law; Killed by Subject)

**History.** Bella Donna's brother. The duel on the wedding day. Killed by the subject's hand, in lawful Guild combat per the Code, at age (approximately) seventeen-to-nineteen depending on the timeline used.

**Dynamic.** This is the subject's first kill of someone *named, known, and family-adjacent*. The pre-Morlock perpetration. The published record treats it briefly; the interior, when occasionally surfaced, treats it as a lasting weight — not as guilt, exactly (the duel was Code-legal and Julien drew first by all accounts), but as the *introduction of the category* of killed-people-the-subject-knew-by-name. Julien is the first; Morlocks are the multitude; the moral arithmetic is continuous, not discrete.

**Trust / Safety / Failure mode / Leverage.** Not applicable except as memory. Julien's name in the subject's interior triggers the Guild-exile circuit, the Bella Donna circuit, and the *I am the kind of man who kills people I have eaten meals with* circuit. Adversarial invocation of Julien is rare in the canon, which is itself notable — the Assassins Guild has chosen, generationally, *not* to weaponize this name beyond a certain ritual threshold, because doing so would invoke counter-obligations in the Code. The Code, as so often in this file, is doing more work than charm.

---

### IV-A.10 — Olivier (Adopted / Found Son, *X-Men Forever* and adjacent continuities; partial-canon)

**History.** In the *X-Men Forever* alternate continuity (Claremont, 2009) and tangentially across alternate-Earth materials, a child Olivier is introduced as the subject's son. The status across main-616 canon is uncertain; the dossier flags this as a *partial-canon* relationship that nevertheless illuminates a tendency in the subject's interior worth noting even where the strict continuity is suspended.

**Dynamic.** Whenever a child appears in proximity to the subject across any continuity — Sarah/Marrow at the moment of the Massacre, Olivier in alternate continuities, the various rescued children across team operations — the subject's behavior bends sharply toward protective. The protective bend overrides standard threat-assessment, mission priority, and self-preservation in that order.

**Evolution.** Not applicable to a stable timeline; the pattern is more important than the instance.

**Trust / Safety.** With children — including hypothetical or adopted children — the subject is at his most reliably tender and least defended. Among the family map, the *category* of "child entrusted to me" is the only one where his behavior is fully congruent with his stated values and his interior simultaneously.

**Failure mode.** Loss of a child under his protection would be the single likely-catastrophic destabilizer in the subject's emotional system, exceeding even Rogue-loss in destructive potential. He has not yet been tested at this exact threshold; the file flags it as an unmodeled extreme.

**Leverage.** Extreme and brittle. Threat to any child under his protection produces maximum tactical irrationality. Any operator playing this card had better intend the consequences.

---

### IV-A.11 — Sarah / Marrow (Rescued from the Massacre; quasi-daughter / surviving witness)

**History.** The child Remy carried out of the Morlock tunnels at the moment of the Massacre, against orders, in the only act of resistance he managed while the slaughter he had assembled played out around him. She survives, grows into the Morlock-leader-then-X-Man known as Marrow, and at various points across the canon (Lobdell, Carey) confronts him with what he did.

**Dynamic.** The most overdetermined relationship in his file outside Rogue. Sarah is at once: (a) the *one life he saved*, his single piece of moral evidence in his own defense, (b) the living witness who could expose him at any time, (c) a quasi-daughter-figure he protected at infancy of the relationship, and (d) the human face of the multitude he killed. The subject cannot meet her gaze without all four registers active simultaneously.

**Evolution.** Began with him as her rescuer (she did not know, then, that he was also her near-killer). Mid-period: she learned, she raged, she did not kill him though she could have. Later periods: an uneasy détente, in which they coexist on shared rosters with the prior history suspended-but-never-resolved. He has never asked her forgiveness — clinically consistent with his self-concept (he does not believe he deserves to receive it and will not insult her by requesting it).

**Trust / Safety.** Mutual high-stakes wariness, threaded with a real and unspoken bond. She knows. He knows she knows. Neither of them weaponizes the knowing. This is, in its way, one of the most morally adult relationships in the subject's file — both parties are carrying the whole thing without flinching.

**Failure mode.** If Marrow were ever to choose to act on the prior debt


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# UATU INTELLIGENCE FILE — REMY ETIENNE LeBEAU

## SECTION 7: RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

> *Preface.* The subject does not form relationships the way most operators in the X-roster form them. He does not bond on shared ideology, shared origin trauma, or shared species-fate. He bonds, almost exclusively, on **read-of-character at close range** — a Guild-trained, near-instantaneous assessment of whether the other party is decent, exploitative, dangerous, or salvageable — followed by a slow accumulation of small kept promises. This produces a relational map with unusual properties: shallow with the X-Men's ideologues (Cyclops, Xavier, Hank in his moralist mode), deep with operators (Logan, Storm, Bishop in his quieter periods), almost familial with the outcast-among-outcasts (Marrow, Mercy, the Morlock survivors), and structurally weird with figures who occupy intermediate categories he cannot resolve (Jean-Luc, Tante Mattie, Henri).
>
> The taxonomy that follows is organized by **functional category**, not chronology. For each subject the file maps: shared history, observed dynamics, trust topology, characteristic failure mode of the bond, and standard leverage assessment.

---

### 7.1 JEAN-LUC LeBEAU — Adoptive Father / Guild Patron / *Père putatif*

**History.** Patriarch of the New Orleans Thieves Guild; took the infant or toddler Remy into his household after the child had passed through several hands within the Guild's adjacency network. Trained subject from earliest cognition in the Guild's curriculum: pick-pocket craft, climbing, lock work, evasion, the formal hand-signs and oaths of the Guild liturgy, and the Code (a feudal-honor code that prizes loyalty to the Guild above all). Arranged the Boudreaux marriage as an instrument of Guild statecraft. After the Julien duel, formally exiled Remy from New Orleans — a Guild verdict that Jean-Luc, as patriarch, was institutionally obligated to render and personally pained to render. Has reappeared across the canon as ailing father, as captured hostage, as ceremonial elder, as a man Remy returns to bury and re-bury.

**Dynamics.** This is the relationship in which the subject's foundational ambivalence is most legible. Jean-Luc is the closest thing to a real father he has, and the man who chose him as *asset before son*. Subject's behavior around Jean-Luc shifts visibly: the Cajun accent thickens to near-parody, the rakish surface tightens into something more formal — there is a posture of *the boy reporting to the father* that does not appear in any other relationship in the file. He defers, he code-switches into the Guild's argot, and he becomes, briefly, smaller.

**Trust topology.** *Operational trust: high.* He believes Jean-Luc will not deliberately betray him on small things. *Existential trust: low.* He believes Jean-Luc will, when forced to choose between Remy and the Guild, choose the Guild — and he believes this is correct, because he has been raised inside the same code and would do the same in reverse. The relationship is therefore conducted with the mutual understanding that both parties love each other inside a structure that will, if pressed, eat them.

**Failure mode.** Jean-Luc is the source of subject's primary *non-Sinister* relational template: love expressed through instrumentalization. When Jean-Luc dies or is endangered, the subject does not respond with clean grief — he responds with the doubled grief of someone mourning both the father and the version of himself the father failed to free him from being. Operational decision-making degrades sharply when Jean-Luc is in play.

**Leverage.** Threat to Jean-Luc produces compliance, but not full irrationality (cf. Rogue, where the irrationality is total). Disclosure of subject's continuing affection for Jean-Luc to enemies of the Guild can be weaponized.

---

### 7.2 HENRI LeBEAU — Adoptive Brother

**History.** Jean-Luc's biological son. The brother who was *chosen by blood* against the brother *chosen by acquisition*. Trained alongside Remy in the Guild curriculum; was, by all internal Guild assessments, the lesser thief — slower hands, less talent for the read, no mutant edge. Killed during the Guild War arc (*Gambit* Vol. 1, 1993), in part as collateral consequence of Remy's exile and the destabilization of the Thieves/Assassins peace that the Boudreaux marriage was meant to seal.

**Dynamics.** Henri loved Remy without reservation. This is the single cleanest emotional bond in the subject's pre-X-Men life — the only person who chose him without an angle, possibly because Henri lacked the strategic sophistication to have an angle. Subject responded to this with an unusual softness; in the limited flashback record, his behavior around Henri lacks the deflective charm-armor that characterizes him everywhere else. He could be quiet with Henri. He could be unfunny.

**Failure mode.** Henri's death is one of the secret structuring losses of the subject's interior life — secret because he rarely speaks of it. It functions as a private confirmation that *people who love him without a defensive ledger die for it*. The lesson is filed alongside the Morlock lesson and has been generative of the same protective overcompensation he extends to civilians and children: he will throw himself between an innocent and harm because Henri is, in some part of him, always the innocent.

**Leverage.** Posthumous. Invoking Henri's name to the subject — particularly invoking it in any framing that suggests Henri's death was Remy's fault — produces an immediate shame-flood and a willingness to absorb cost.

---

### 7.3 MERCY LeBEAU — Adoptive Sister-in-Law / Surviving Family

**History.** Henri's widow. Remained in the New Orleans Guild orbit after Henri's death. Has the unusual position of being *family* to subject without being *chosen by the same broken machinery that broke him* — she married into the family rather than being raised inside it, which gives her a clearer view of the LeBeau pathologies than the LeBeaus possess.

**Dynamics.** Subject's relationship with Mercy is gentle, formal, and protective in a way that does not require performance. He brings her news. He sits with her. He does not flirt — one of the very few women in the canon with whom he does not, which is itself a tell of how seriously he categorizes her.

**Trust topology.** *High in both registers.* One of the few people who can correct him about himself and have it land.

**Failure mode.** Distance. The relationship maintains its purity because they do not see each other often. Sustained co-habitation would expose more of him than he can comfortably show even to Mercy.

**Leverage.** Negligible; she is a non-combatant in his moral universe and threatening her would simply close him.

---

### 7.4 TANTE MATTIE — Childhood Healer / *Traiteuse* / Witness-Figure

**History.** The Cajun *traiteuse* (folk-healer) of the LeBeau household and Guild adjacency, present from earliest childhood. Healer of his earliest power-related injuries. The one adult in his childhood who appears to have *known* what was wrong with him — both the powers and the loneliness — and did not respond by sharpening him for use.

**Dynamics.** Subject treats Tante Mattie as a *moral compass external to the Guild's code*. She is the figure he returns to when the Guild framework fails him. The accent he uses with her is the most natural — closer to his unperformed cadence than any other documented register, which is diagnostically useful: comparing his Mattie-voice to his X-Mansion voice gives a baseline measure of the performance overhead in his daily presentation.

**Trust topology.** *Existential trust: among the highest in the file.* He believes she would not abandon him even if she knew the worst. He has nonetheless not told her the worst — which is consistent with the file's central pattern: he protects his sanctuaries from the truth, because he needs the sanctuary more than he needs the disclosure.

**Failure mode.** None observable in the bond itself; the relationship's limitation is the limitation he imposes on it by withholding.

**Leverage.** Threat to Tante Mattie would produce protective response. Direct manipulation of Mattie *against* him — convincing her of his guilt — would be devastating, possibly more so than any other single intervention available to a hostile actor, because she occupies the role of *unconditional witness* in his psychology and her withdrawal would collapse a load-bearing internal structure.

---

### 7.5 ORORO MUNROE ("STORM") — Sister, Co-Thief, Broker of Return

**History.** First encountered as the de-aged, amnesiac, feral child-Storm in the streets of Cairo, Illinois (*Uncanny X-Men* #266, 1990). Subject — at that time a free agent, post-exile, post-Sinister, post-Massacre — chose to protect her, then accompanied her back toward identity and toward the X-Men. She is, functionally, his *broker* into the moral community he believed himself excluded from. They share a thief's pedigree (Storm's Cairo childhood as a pickpocket); they speak a craft-language no one else on the team speaks.

**Dynamics.** The deepest non-romantic bond in the file. Their interactions are characterized by an ease that does not appear elsewhere in his social life — they can be silent together, they can run an op together with minimal coordination, they can read each other's micro-cues across a room. He calls her *Stormy*, a nickname she tolerates from no one else; she allows it because she understands that the nickname is the *register-marker* by which he signals safety. When he uses it, he is unguarded.

**Trust topology.** *Operational trust: total.* He will follow her into anything. *Existential trust: nearly total* — and this is the only platonic relationship in the file for which the qualifier "nearly" applies. He has come closer to telling Storm about the Massacre than telling anyone else, and has not done so, but the bond can sustain the not-yet-disclosure better than any other.

**Failure mode.** When Storm is required to function in her *queen / leader / institutional-authority* register, the bond compresses; he reverts to the deferent-operative posture and the intimacy goes underground until she is private again. He cannot fully be his sibling-self with Storm-as-monarch.

**Leverage.** Threat to Storm produces tactical irrationality second only to Rogue. Conversely, Storm's *disapproval* is one of the few social signals that can actually course-correct him in real time — she occupies the role of the sister whose verdict he respects without needing to fight.

---

### 7.6 LOGAN ("WOLVERINE") — Brother-in-Arms / Co-Operator / Mirror

**History.** Ally, sparring partner, drinking companion, and operational peer across nearly the entire X-Men tenure. Their bond stabilized early and has survived multiple ruptures (Antarctica fallout, Apocalypse arc, various team realignments).

**Dynamics.** Both men carry perpetration trauma. Both men have done things in service to powerful exploitative figures (Sinister, Weapon X, etc.) that they cannot fully metabolize. Both men deal with this by being useful to a moral community that would not have them if it knew everything. Neither has had to *tell* the other this — they recognize each other by gait, the way two men who have walked the same road recognize the limp.

The relationship is conducted in remarkably few words. They share bourbon (subject's drink) and beer (Logan's), they share cigars in eras the editorial environment permits, they share a willingness to do the morally compromised work the team needs done without making the team watch. Subject defers to Logan in matters of close-quarters combat and tracking; Logan defers to subject in social engineering, theft, and infiltration. The division of labor is implicit and stable.

**Trust topology.** *Operational trust: total.* *Existential trust: high but unspoken.* Logan is one of the very few people the subject suspects could hear the Massacre confession without flinching — because Logan has his own Massacre — but the confession has not been made, perhaps because between them it does not need to be.

**Failure mode.** When Logan is in his berserker register or under Weapon X conditioning relapse, the bond suspends until Logan returns. Subject does not attempt to handle Logan in crisis; he waits him out. Conversely, when *subject* is in Death-conversion or Apocalypse-relapse register, Logan is one of the few people credibly capable of bringing him down, and both men understand this is part of the contract.

**Leverage.** Negligible from outside. Internally, Logan's good opinion is one of subject's few load-bearing external validators, alongside Rogue's and Storm's.

---

### 7.7 SARAH ("MARROW") — The Saved Child / Living Penance / Daughter-Figure

**History.** The Morlock child subject pulled out of the tunnels during the Massacre — the one life he saved while leading the operation that killed her community. She grew up in Mikhail Rasputin's pocket dimension under brutal conditions, returned to the X-Men as a violent, traumatized, physically deformed young woman with a deep rage at the surface world and an unresolved relationship to the figure who saved her by half.

**Dynamics.** This is the single most morally complex bond in the file, and the one in which the subject's reaction-formation defense is most visible. He is *unfailingly gentle* with her, *unfailingly patient* with her violence, *unfailingly available* when she will accept availability. He does not perform charm with her — there is no flirtation, no rakish wit; the register is quiet, careful, almost penitential. He treats her with the precise, attentive humility of a man who has appointed himself her permanent debtor.

She, for her part, oscillates between gratitude for the rescue, rage at the necessity of the rescue, and a more complicated emotion that does not have a name in standard relational vocabulary — the emotion of being the *one survivor* whom the destroyer kept. The dynamic is asymmetric and will remain so; he will not permit it to become anything else.

**Trust topology.** *He trusts her with his life.* *She trusts him operationally but not existentially*, and he has accepted this as the just shape of the bond.

**Failure mode.** If Marrow ever learns the full extent of subject's authorship of the Massacre — which depending on continuity she partly knows and partly does not — the rupture would be catastrophic, and subject would not defend himself. He would accept whatever verdict she rendered, up to and including his own death at her hands. This is operationally relevant: any actor who could deliver Marrow the documentation could effectively *neutralize* the subject without firing a shot.

**Leverage.** Marrow herself is a pressure point — threat to her produces protective response — but the deeper leverage is *Marrow's knowledge*. Custody of the truth about her past is custody of the subject.

---

### 7.8 THE MORLOCK SURVIVORS (Collective) — The Constituency of His Crime

**History.** The wider population of Massacre survivors — Caliban, Leech, Erg, the scattered remnants — who under various continuities have or have not known of subject's role.

**Dynamics.** Subject's behavior in any room containing a Morlock survivor is observably altered: he stands slightly farther back than his usual social distance, he speaks less, he watches more, and he positions himself between them and any visible threat without seeming to think about it. He has, across canon, repeatedly intervened on behalf of Morlock survivors at personal cost. The intervention is automatic and does not require deliberation, which marks it as a *standing internal commitment* rather than a case-by-case decision.

**Trust topology.** Asymmetric. He does not expect their trust; he has assigned himself a unilateral duty toward them that does not require reciprocity.

**Failure mode.** Mass disclosure of his role would end his place in the X-Men's moral community and he knows it. He has organized his life around the assumption that this disclosure will eventually happen and that he will accept its consequences when it does. This is not resignation in a passive sense — it is a *standing accepted verdict* that he carries in the background of every day.

**Leverage.** Total, for any actor with credible documentation. The Massacre file is the master key to the subject.

---

### 7.9 ROGUE — *See Section 6 (Relationships I — Primary Romantic).*

*Cross-referenced here only for completeness. Rogue is not catalogued in this section; she is the structural object around which this entire file orbits. See dedicated section.*

---

### 7.10 CHARLES XAVIER — Institutional Father / The Man Whose Pocket He Picked

**History.** Subject's first documented contact with Xavier predates the X-Men recruitment: as a child or adolescent thief, he picked Xavier's pocket on the street, an anecdote he later tells with calibrated rakish pride. The encounter functioned, in retrospect, as Xavier's early flagging of the subject as a future candidate. Recruitment proper came years later via Storm.

**Dynamics.** Subject's relationship with Xavier is *cordial, deferential on the surface, and quietly resistant in operation*. He addresses Xavier respectfully, follows orders within the band of orders he considers defensible, and bypasses orders he considers wrong without arguing about them. He distrusts telepaths on Guild-trained principle and distrusts Xavier specifically as a *charismatic father with a cause* — a category-match for Sinister and Apocalypse, against which his trauma history has hard-wired suspicion.

He has also, more than once, observed Xavier's compromises — the cover-ups, the moral expediencies, the secret-keeping — and these observations have *reduced his shame*, marginally, by demonstrating that the moral community he is paying rent on is itself ethically imperfect. This is not cynicism; it is a kind of relief.

**Trust topology.** *Operational trust: conditional.* *Existential trust: low.* He has never told Xavier anything that mattered, and never will.

**Failure mode.** Direct telepathic intrusion by Xavier would produce immediate, possibly violent, defensive response. Subject's Guild-trained mental shielding is among the strongest non-telepathic shielding in the X-roster, and this is not accident — it is a relational stance externalized as discipline.

**Leverage.** Xavier has very little leverage over the subject and the subject knows it. The relationship operates on mutual professional courtesy and very little else.

---

### 7.11 HANK McCOY ("BEAST") — Trusted Clinician, Distrusted Moralist

**History.** Long-term teammate. Subject's primary point of medical contact within the X-Men; in particular, Hank is the clinician who has examined the subject's neurological status post-Sinister and post-Apocalypse and is one of the few people with hard data on the surgical alteration.

**Dynamics.** Bifurcated. Subject trusts Hank *the doctor* — he is one of the very few people in the file the subject will allow to put hands on him in a medical context without visible tension — and is wary of Hank *the moralist*, particularly in Hank's later, darker editorial periods. The clinician-bond is durable; the friendship-bond is conditional on Hank remaining recognizably the Hank of the early years.

**Trust topology.** Domain-specific. *Medical: high.* *Personal disclosure: low.* He will tell Hank what hurts and not why.

**Failure mode.** Hank's possession of subject's medical record is a standing exposure. Were Hank ever to choose to disclose what he has clinically inferred about subject's neurological history, he could do real damage. Subject is aware of this and accepts it as a cost of being treated.

**Leverage.** Indirect, via Hank's records. Direct leverage on subject through Hank is minimal.

---

### 7.12 SCOTT SUMMERS ("CYCLOPS") — Respected Commander, Unloved Brother

**History.** Long-tenure teammate, frequent field commander, ideological counterpart-by-contrast.

**Dynamics.** Subject respects Cyclops's discipline and tactical mind and does not particularly like him. The dislike is not personal — it is structural. Cyclops embodies the *principled moralist* archetype that subject distrusts on temperament: a man who believes in causes and institutions and will sacrifice individuals to them. Subject is a relational moralist; the two operate on incompatible ethical operating systems.

Field cooperation is excellent. Personal warmth is low. Subject executes Cyclops's orders within the same band he executes Xavier's — accepting the defensible, quietly routing around the rest. Across the Utopia, Schism, and AvX eras, when Cyclops radicalized, subject's distrust deepened but did not break into open opposition; he characteristically *withdrew* rather than confronted.

**Trust topology.** *Operational: high.* *Personal: limited.* Cyclops is a colleague, not a brother.

**Failure mode.** If Cyclops were to demand from subject an action that violated his protective commitments to children, civilians, or the Morlock-survivor constituency, subject would refuse, lie about refusing, and accept the discipline. He has done versions of this multiple times.

**Leverage.** Cyclops cannot meaningfully leverage subject and does not particularly try. The relationship is stable precisely because both men have correctly assessed its limits.

---

### 7.13 BISHOP — The Hunter / The Reconciled Adversary

**History.** Originally a peer-teammate who, across the *Messiah Complex* and subsequent arcs, became convinced subject would commit a future betrayal and pursued him across timelines with intent to kill. They have, in subsequent continuity, partially reconciled.

**Dynamics.** Subject's response to Bishop's pursuit is one of the file's most diagnostically rich behavioral sequences. He did not respond with the fury of an innocent man falsely accused. He responded with *grim, sad recognition*, fled efficiently, and at multiple junctures expressed the view that Bishop might be right — that some version of himself, in some future, plausibly *would* do whatever Bishop believed. **This is not normal innocent-man behavior.** It is the behavior of a man whose self-concept includes a standing acknowledgment that he is capable of atrocity, because he has already authored one, and therefore cannot in good conscience deny that he might author another.

Post-reconciliation, subject extends to Bishop the unusual courtesy of *not holding the hunt against him*. He understands the hunt; he might, in Bishop's place, have done the same.

**Trust topology.** Cautious operational trust, mutual professional respect. No intimacy expected by either party.

**Failure mode.** If Bishop ever again becomes convinced of subject's future guilt, subject will not fight him hard. He will run, and if Bishop catches him, he will largely accept it. This is consistent with the Antarctica pattern.

**Leverage.** Bishop himself is a low-leverage figure with respect to subject. The *idea* that Bishop carries — that subject is *predictably* dangerous — is the leverage, and it is leverage that already operates internally without external prompting.

---

### 7.14 BELLA DONNA BOUDREAUX — *See Section 6 (Relationships I — Primary Romantic).*
