*Cross-referenced; catalogued in romantic-history section. Note here only that the Assassins Guild as an institution functions as a *permanent ambient hostile presence* in the subject's life, and Bella Donna's oscillating


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# UATU DOSSIER — REMY ETIENNE LeBEAU ("GAMBIT")
## Section: RELATIONSHIPS III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

A note on scope. This section maps the antagonists, intimates, and the small handful of figures who occupy the strange overlap zone where rival, enemy, and lover collapse into one another (a pattern that, in the subject's life, is not coincidence but structure). Each entry traces the relationship across the full longitudinal record: how it began, what it became, the operational dynamics between the two parties, the trust architecture, the failure mode, and the leverage either party can apply to the other. Where the canon is contradictory, the contradictions are themselves data.

The categorical ordering — rivals, enemies, lovers — is artificial in this subject's case. He has slept with a rival, been raised by a man who became an enemy, and loved a woman whose first organized response to him was a death warrant. The categories will be observed, but the bleed-through is itself the file.

---

## I. ENEMIES — THE STRUCTURING ADVERSARIES

### 1. NATHANIEL ESSEX ("MR. SINISTER")

The single most important figure in the subject's life. Not Rogue. Not Jean-Luc. Sinister.

**Origin of the relationship.** A pubertal Remy, in escalating bio-kinetic power crisis — convulsing, charging objects he could not discharge, on a trajectory toward death by his own neurology — was located, evaluated, and operated upon by Essex. The surgical intervention (excision of a portion of cortical / limbic-adjacent tissue identified as governing the charge capacity) saved his life and gave him voluntary command of his power. The price was the recruitment of the Marauders and the guiding of that team into the Morlock tunnels (per the disclosures of *Uncanny X-Men* #350, Lobdell, 1997, and elaborated across Carey's *X-Men*, 2007–08).

**Dynamic.** The relationship is the prototype of every subsequent dangerous-attachment in the subject's file. Essex offers what no parent gave: *competence with the body Remy was born into*. He does not love the boy; he calibrates him. The transaction is delivered in the register of medicine and bargain, not affection, which is the register Remy was conditioned by the Guild to accept as the *honest* one. He distrusts love; he trusts contract. Sinister knew this, or read it, or simply happened on the configuration of psyche that would respond. Either way, the result is a man who, decades later, can still be moved by the sentence *I can give you control* in a way no other sentence reaches.

**Trust / safety architecture.** Zero trust, total operational compliance — at the time. The subject understood Sinister to be monstrous and submitted anyway, because submission was the cost of staying alive in his own skin. The defining moral data point is that he submitted *before* knowing the full price. He learned what the Marauders were for during the act itself, in the tunnels, in the dark, with Sarah in his arms. Sinister's gift to him is therefore not power but *complicity with his own monstrousness, ratified by a man who already saw him as monstrous and was unbothered.* This is the structural wound.

**Evolution.** Across the canon the relationship shifts from creator-creation to one of mutual mythological gravity. Essex returns to the subject's life with regularity — sometimes as adversary, sometimes as offerer of further bargains (the Hickman/Krakoa-era Sinister machinations involve Gambit's genome, fittingly, as Essex's interest in his subject was never personal but always genomic-fascinational). The subject's response curve, over years, moves from compliance → guilt-stricken severance → confrontational hostility → calibrated wariness. He no longer takes the bargain. But he has not stopped *hearing* it.

**Failure mode.** Were Essex to appear under conditions of (a) renewed power dysregulation in Remy, (b) Rogue endangered, and (c) plausible offer of cure or control, the file's prediction is that subject would parley before refusing, and would refuse with effort rather than reflex. The reflex broke a long time ago, in a New Orleans operating theatre.

**Leverage (Sinister → Remy).** The Massacre, threatened or weaponized for disclosure. The genomic register — anything implicating Rogue's biology, or children, or future children, or surviving Morlocks. Above all, the offer of *neurological intervention*: Sinister knows what was taken and could, conceivably, take or restore more. Remy is, in his own bones, Essex's surgical patient. That is a tether that does not dissolve.

**Leverage (Remy → Sinister).** Remarkably, some. The subject knows where bodies are buried — literally, in the Morlock tunnels, and figuratively, in the lab records and recruitment protocols of the Marauders project. He is one of the few living witnesses to the project's interior workings. Essex's interest in *not* being known is itself a vulnerability Remy has, on occasion, leveraged.

---

### 2. EN SABAH NUR ("APOCALYPSE")

The second father-figure who offered the same bargain in different ritual dress, and to whom the subject said yes for the second time.

**Origin.** During the early 2000s (Austen) and elaborated under Carey's run (2007–08), Apocalypse selects Remy to become the Horseman of Death. The conversion is partly coercive, partly seductive: the subject is offered, again, *mastery of his own destructive capacity*, this time scaled up and rendered in mythic-eschatological register.

**Dynamic.** The subject's acquiescence — even partial, even resisted — replays the Sinister bargain. The defense Remy mounts (he claims, internally and to Rogue afterward, that he was infiltrating, gathering intelligence, playing the long con) is partially true and partially the Guild-trained rationalization that allows him to recategorize compliance as operation. The honest reading is that some part of him wanted the permission Apocalypse was giving: *be the monster you already are, but with purpose.*

**Trust / safety.** None on either side. Apocalypse regards Remy as raw material; Remy regards Apocalypse as a god to be poisoned slowly. But the relationship's deeper truth is that Apocalypse offered a *theology of the irredeemable* — a worldview in which Remy's self-condemnation is recategorized as fitness, as election. For a man whose private operating system is *I am irredeemable*, hearing a god say *yes, and that makes you mine* is not refused as easily as it should be.

**Evolution.** Subject extricates himself, with effort, and conceals the residual conditioning afterward. The Death conversion has lingering somatic and ocular effects he masks. He does not voluntarily discuss the period; when forced to, he minimizes. The pattern *repetition of the structuring crime in altered key, followed by concealment and a return to ostensible normalcy* is the Morlock template recapitulated. He has done this twice now. The file's predictive concern is that the third instance is not foreclosed.

**Failure mode.** Subject is structurally susceptible to any figure of sufficient power who frames itself as offering *control in exchange for service*. Apocalypse confirmed Sinister's lesson rather than disrupting it.

**Leverage.** Apocalypse-residual conditioning. Any operator who could credibly threaten reactivation of the Death state would hold him. He fears this — quietly, ambiently — more than he fears death.

---

### 3. JULIEN BOUDREAUX

The first man Remy killed for love.

**Origin.** Bella Donna's elder brother, scion of the Assassins Guild, opposed to the arranged-marriage peace from its inception. He challenges Remy on the wedding day. Remy kills him in fair duel (per *Gambit* mini, 1993, and the New Orleans war arcs).

**Dynamic.** Julien is dead in the file's first chapter, but he is structurally alive in the subject's psyche as the *first cost of intimacy*. Marriage to Bella Donna required killing her brother. This is, in raw symbol, what every subsequent intimate relationship will replay in muted form: *to be with this woman, something will have to die*. The subject did not invent this conviction. The Guild engineered it into the founding day of his adult life.

**Leverage.** Julien himself: none, being dead. But the *fact of Julien* — wielded by the Assassins Guild, by Bella Donna in her hostile phases, by anyone who knows the history — produces in the subject a particular kind of immobility, a willingness to pay debt. Threats to harm an Assassins Guild member in revenge for the subject would not stop him; demands that he accept an Assassins Guild punishment for Julien's death would, historically, be entertained.

---

### 4. CANDRA, THE EXTERNAL

The witch-queen sovereign of the Thieves and Assassins Guilds, ancient external mutant, recipient of tithes from both Guilds in exchange for longevity-conferring blessings. She is, for most of the subject's young life, the supernatural ceiling of his world.

**Dynamic.** A figure of uncanny seductive authority, partial maternal valence, partial sexual valence, fully predatory. Across the *Gambit* solo runs of the late 1990s she alternates between patron and adversary. The subject's response to her is a paradigm case of his behavior with powerful older women who frame themselves as benefactors: surface charm, ironized courtesy, no operational trust, constant reading for the catch.

**Trust / safety.** None. He treats her as the Guild taught him to treat sovereigns — with elaborate deference that costs nothing and conceals everything. She, for her part, regards him as a particularly fine instrument she did not personally craft.

**Failure mode.** Were Candra to credibly threaten the New Orleans Guild infrastructure or the surviving LeBeaus, the subject would deal. He has dealt with her before. He does not pretend, internally, that this makes him clean.

**Leverage.** Mutual and roughly balanced. He knows her rituals' weaknesses; she knows his obligations.

---

### 5. THE EXTERNAL ASSASSINS GUILD (POST-JULIEN)

Treated here as a collective enemy because the subject's relationship is institutional rather than individual after the duel.

**Dynamic.** A standing death-warrant operates against the subject from his exile onward, periodically suspended, periodically reactivated depending on Bella Donna's current standing within the Guild. The subject's relationship to the Guild is a permanent low-grade vigilance: any Cajun-accented voice in a crowd is registered, any New Orleans-connected stranger evaluated for tells. This is somatized into the file's general hypervigilance profile.

**Failure mode.** Subject will not flee from Assassins; he will negotiate, fight, or accept the consequence. He will not, however, allow them to use civilians or X-Men teammates as proxies — this triggers disproportionate response.

**Leverage.** A credible Assassins move against Rogue, Marrow, or any child under his protection would produce the only consistently lethal-without-hesitation behavior on the subject's record.

---

### 6. THE MARAUDERS (ORIGINAL, SINISTER-ERA)

His own team. His own crime. Treated here as an enemy because the subject's relationship to the men and women he assembled is one of permanent moral debt and intermittent personal hostility.

**Dynamic.** The original Marauders — Scalphunter, Arclight, Harpoon, Riptide, Vertigo, Sabretooth among them — are, to the subject, the embodied memory of his worst hours. He assembled them. He guided them. He cannot pretend he did not know what kind of men they were when he hired them; the rationalization that he did not know the *target* does not reach the rationalization that he knew the *tools*.

When elements of the original Marauders resurface, the subject's response is a peculiar composite: tactical professionalism, no negotiation, an absence of the usual flirtatious affect, and afterward a marked depressive interval. He does not kill them when not required to (a fact that itself is data — a colder operator would). He bears their continued existence as part of his sentence.

**Sabretooth specifically.** The relationship with Creed deserves its own micro-entry, because Creed delights in the subject's guilt and weaponizes it. Creed, perhaps uniquely, *enjoys* reminding Remy of the tunnels, of the children, of the blood. The subject's response is unusually disciplined hatred — he does not take Creed's bait into rage, which would honor Creed's framing; he answers with the cool of a man paying a bill. This is one of the few interpersonal arenas where the subject's affective control is total. It costs him.

**Leverage.** The Marauders, collectively, are the leverage. Their continued reality, their reappearances, their willingness to testify in any moral tribunal of the surviving Morlocks, are a permanent file-open against the subject.

---

### 7. BASTION / OPERATION: ZERO TOLERANCE-ERA TRIBUNAL APPARATUS

Less an enemy than a context — the apparatus through which the Antarctica trial was staged. Worth noting because the subject's behavior under tribunal is diagnostic: he did not contest, did not invoke counsel, did not argue mitigation, did not name Sinister's coercion as exculpation. He sat. He answered. He accepted. Any future tribunal of any kind that frames itself as legitimate will receive the same response. He believes he owes the verdict, whatever it is.

---

## II. RIVALS — THE OVERLAPPING ZONE

### 8. BELLA DONNA BOUDREAUX

The first wife, in the only sense that word can take in this subject's life — the marriage was contracted, sanctified, and never consummated; he killed her brother on the wedding day; she has alternately tried to murder him, save him, marry him again, and kill him again ever since. She is the proof-of-concept for every subsequent intimacy.

**Origin.** Childhood betrothal as Guild-peace instrument. They grew up adjacent, knowing they would marry. Whether the affection is genuine or trained-into-them by political necessity is a question neither has ever cleanly answered; the honest reading is that it is both, irreducibly. He loved her. He loves her, in the residual way one loves the first person whose face was promised to one's own. He also has tried, on occasion, to leave her for dead with operational coolness. Both are true.

**Dynamic.** Volatile. Predatory-affectionate. She is, of all his women, the one most like him in moral architecture — Guild-raised, trained in deception, comfortable with violence, willing to lie protectively, suspicious of institutions, loyal to chosen persons. She is also the one who most consistently *uses* him as the Guild taught them both to use one another. Sex with Bella Donna (when occurring, post-her-power-coma-recoveries and in various tangled later arcs) is depicted as performative-aggressive on both sides — a register Remy is fluent in and Rogue is not.

**Trust / safety.** Low operational trust; high *baseline* trust, paradoxically, because she is predictable in her unpredictability. He knows the *shape* of her betrayals. He does not have to wonder whether she is the kind of woman who could be murderous toward him; she is, and he is at peace with the fact.

**Evolution.** The relationship oscillates between attempted reconciliation, attempted murder, and operational alliance against larger threats (the Assassins Guild's worse factions, external enemies, Candra). After the marriage to Rogue, the Bella Donna relationship is rezoned into a kind of charged armistice. She still considers herself his wife by older law. He does not contest the claim; he simply does not act on it.

**Failure mode.** The relationship fails catastrophically when Bella Donna interprets a kindness from him as a renewal of betrothal; it also fails when she interprets an act of necessary distance as a fresh betrayal. The interpretive bandwidth is narrow, and the subject knows this and navigates it with the same Guild-trained micro-gesture vocabulary she uses.

**Leverage (Bella Donna → Remy).** She can summon him to New Orleans on Guild business, and he will go. She can claim Guild law and obligate him to honor it. She can endanger herself, and he will respond. She cannot, any longer, make him return to her in the spousal sense — that door is closed by Rogue, and Bella Donna knows it — but she can extract operational service.

**Leverage (Remy → Bella Donna).** Symmetrical. He retains Guild standing she values; he knows her organizational vulnerabilities; he can, with a word in the right ear, alter the Assassins Guild internal politics in her favor or against her. The relationship is, in this respect, the most adult one in his file — two former children of conspiratorial families who have stopped pretending the conspiracies are not the medium of their love.

---

### 9. THE THIEVES GUILD POLITICAL APPARATUS / RIVAL CLAIMANTS TO THE LeBEAU LINE

Various Guild figures across the canon position themselves as rivals to the subject's standing — particularly during his exile periods, when his absence creates opportunity. Names rotate (Singer, Bourbon Street factions, various cousins). The subject's general response: he does not contest succession claims while absent; he reasserts authority efficiently when present; he does not seek the Patriarch role and is visibly relieved when it goes elsewhere.

Diagnostic point: the subject *could* be Patriarch of the Thieves Guild. He has, multiple times, declined or sloughed off the role. The man who feels he does not deserve the X-Men also does not feel he deserves the inheritance the Guild was prepared to give him. He has consistently chosen the role of *captain* over the role of *king*. This is a stable preference and operationally important.

---

### 10. NORTHSTAR (JEAN-PAUL BEAUBIER)

A narrower entry, but worth mapping for the rivalry-rather-than-enemy register. The two have, across various team contexts, an uneasy mutual recognition: both Francophone-coded, both pretty, both performative, both proud, both with histories of being the team's morally complicated operator in different ways. Their interactions are competitive-flirtatious in tone, never sexual, characterized by a kind of arms-length professional respect. The subject responds to Northstar's directness with deflection; Northstar responds to the subject's charm with impatience. They function well on operations together because neither needs to be liked by the other.

**Leverage.** None either way. This is one of the genuinely *clean* relationships in the subject's life — devoid of debt in either direction.

---

### 11. WOLVERINE (LOGAN)

Not enemy, not rival, but does not belong in the friends section because the relationship operates in the rival register more than the friend register, especially in the early Claremont and Jim Lee eras. Logan smelled the wrong on Remy the day they met. He could not name it but he knew it was there, and he made the subject know that he knew.

**Dynamic.** Logan-as-truth-detector functioned, for years, as Remy's most uncomfortable mirror. The subject responded with a performance of offhand respect over a substrate of permanent wariness. He never lied to Logan more than necessary, because he knew the lies would not land, and he never tried to charm Logan, because he knew the charm would be smelled out. The relationship was therefore unusually honest *by negation* — a relationship in which the subject's usual tools did not work and so were not deployed.

After the Massacre disclosure, Logan's response was characteristic: minimal speech, no absolution, continued tactical reliance. This was, paradoxically, the most useful response any X-Man gave the subject — neither forgiveness (which would have rung false to Remy and triggered his denial-of-deserving) nor exile (which would have confirmed his self-condemnation and ended his utility). Logan offered him *continued usefulness without absolution*, which is the exact moral configuration the subject privately believes he should be living in.

**Leverage.** Logan retains the implicit threat of his own judgment, which the subject takes seriously. The subject retains nothing leverage-relevant in the other direction.

---

## III. INTIMATES & LOVERS

### 12. ANNA MARIE — "ROGUE"

The central object. The relationship around which two decades of the subject's interior life are organized. To map it fully is to map him.

**Origin.** Subject is introduced to the X-Men in *Uncanny X-Men* #266 (Claremont, 1990) via a regressed Storm, but it is the encounter with Rogue that catches and holds him. The catch is, behaviorally, immediate and intelligible: she is the woman who cannot be touched. The subject — whose touch is, at the kinetic level, the literal site of his lethality, and whose touch is, at the relational level, the literal site of his potential exposure (skin contact is when memory passes between them and she could read him) — has found the one available partner whose powers structurally guarantee he will never have to disclose himself voluntarily, and whose touch will never collapse the courtship register he is good at into the post-courtship register he is afraid of.

This is not cynicism on his part. He does not, at the conscious level, choose her *because* she cannot touch him. At the conscious level he is in love. At the operational-unconscious level — and the file is here to make the operational-unconscious legible — the constraint is exactly the constraint his attachment system required.

**The courtship era (1990–1997).** Years of yearning across enforced gap. The flirtation is constant, the longing is genuine, the consummation is impossible, and the *register of perpetual approach without arrival* is, behaviorally, where the subject is most at ease. He is excellent at this register. He has been training for it since the Guild taught him the language of seduction-without-delivery. Rogue, for her part, is responding to a man who treats her untouchability as a feature rather than a tragedy — every other interlocutor in her life has framed her power as her wound; the subject frames it as the shape of her, and the shape is what he loves. This is true, and it is also tactically perfect for his avoidance.

Disclosure-by-violation occurs in *X-Men* Vol. 2 #7 (Lee/Claremont): she absorbs him under duress, sees fragments of his Antarctica/Sinister history, and flees. The pattern — *the truth gets out by accident rather than confession* — is established. He does not pursue immediately. He waits to be summoned. He believes he has lost her and accepts the loss as just.

**The Antarctica rupture (1997).** *Uncanny X-Men* #350. The Massacre is publicly disclosed via Magneto's apparatus. Rogue, asked to render judgment, leaves him alive but stranded in the Antarctic. The subject *accepts the verdict* — this is the single cleanest behavioral data point in the file. He does not argue. He does not invoke Sinister's coercion. He does not name the mitigations any defense attorney would have named. He believes the punishment is just; he believes a heavier punishment would also be just; he is *grateful* to her, in some operational-unconscious register, for being the one to administer it, because the love object becoming the judge collapses two of his organizing wishes into one act.

He survives Antarctica. The subject's survival is itself diagnostic — he did not die, did not let himself die, because dying would have ended the penance rather than continued it, and the penance is the thing he is organized around.

**The return / reconciliation arcs.** Across the late Nineties and early 2000s, the relationship reconstitutes itself in modulated form. She is no longer his judge; he is no longer her uncomplicated suitor. They move through a series of approach-and-flinch cycles


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

## Pre-Synthesis Intelligence File — Section 5

---

## 1. THE PRIMARY MUTATION: BIO-KINETIC CHARGING

### 1.1 Mechanism (Operational Description)

The subject's primary mutation is the capacity to convert the *latent potential energy* of an inanimate object into *kinetic-explosive* output, mediated by sustained physical contact and an act of focused will. The technical literature on his power (Claremont, Nicieza, Carey, Layman across thirty years of canon) is inconsistent on whether the conversion draws on the object's own molecular potential, ambient ambient ergic substrate, or a bio-kinetic field generated by the subject's own metabolism. The behavioral evidence — caloric drain after large charges, exhaustion after sustained use, observable thinness after combat-heavy arcs — supports a **hybrid model**: the object provides the substrate, but the catalyst is generated metabolically by the subject. He is, in effect, an *enzyme* for transmuting stored matter into kinesis.

Charge time scales with object mass and desired yield: a playing card is ready in under a second; a metal coin in two to three; a Bo staff at maximum yield requires sustained handling over five-to-ten-second windows. The charged object glows on a roughly violet-to-magenta-to-white scale, with brightness functioning as honest signaling of yield. Detonation is triggered by release of contact plus subject's volition — both are required; he can hold a charged object indefinitely without discharge (a tell of how *good* the post-Sinister governor is), and he can recall a charge from an object he is still holding (the *uncharge*, a power rarely depicted but documented in the Nicieza solo run when he stops a charge mid-pulse to spare a bystander).

### 1.2 Range, Yield, and Scaling

- **Minimum yield:** the *paper-cut equivalent* — a playing card charged just enough to sting a hand or singe paper. Used as warning, as flirtation, as nonverbal punctuation.
- **Standard combat yield:** a thrown card delivering force roughly equivalent to a hand grenade in a one-to-two-meter radius. This is his operational baseline and the projectile most associated with him in field reports.
- **Heavy yield:** a charged Bo staff used as a melee detonator, capable of structural damage to vehicles, walls, and unenhanced exoskeletons.
- **Extreme yield (situational, dangerous to self):** charging a large object — a car door, a section of flooring, in one extreme case (Carey's *X-Men: Legacy*) charging his own clothing — for area denial or escape. Documented self-burn and concussive recoil at this yield.
- **Theoretical ceiling (pre-Sinister, uncontrolled):** unbounded; the in-character implication is that without surgical intervention his power would have escalated until he detonated his own body and a significant radius around it. This is the *original* clinical emergency.

Range is exclusively contact-mediated *for the charging*; once charged, the object can be thrown, dropped, kicked, or placed, and the discharge will occur at his volitional trigger. He is therefore not a "blaster" in the X-Men sense — he is a *delivery system*. The distinction matters: he does not project energy, he *invests* it, then transports it. **This is the defining shape of his combat doctrine and, by inference, of his cognitive style: place the charge, walk away, choose the moment.**

### 1.3 The Sinister Governor

The single most important fact about the power is that it is *post-surgical*. A portion of brain tissue — most plausibly a neural inhibitor that allows volitional gating of charge magnitude and duration — was excised by Mr. Sinister during the pre-Marauder period. Pre-surgery: power was binary, escalating, and lethal to the subject. Post-surgery: power is finely modulable, voluntary, and survivable.

The clinical and operational implications cannot be overstated:

- **His control is iatrogenic, not endogenous.** He did not learn his power; it was *carved into him*. Every act of fine modulation is, at the somatic level, a use of the gift purchased with the Massacre.
- **Stress destabilizes the governor.** Documented across *X-Cutioner's Song*, the Apocalypse conversion, and several arcs in the Nicieza solo: under acute emotional load, charges become harder to hold, shorter in latency, larger in yield than intended, and occasionally *involuntary*. The neural substrate that allows him to choose is the same substrate that grief, panic, and intimacy disrupt.
- **The "uncharge."** Demonstrated rarely but consistently in canon: he can pull a charge back into himself without discharge. This is the most psychologically diagnostic of all his power-uses, and we will return to it.

### 1.4 Apocalypse-Era Amplification ("Death")

During the Horseman conversion (Austen, then Carey), the subject's power is *expanded* by external augmentation: he can charge organic matter, can charge at range without contact (briefly), can charge himself without detonating (a body-as-bomb posture). The sclera deepens; the iris reddens further. Post-conversion, he conceals the persistence of some of these enhancements — most notably, the ability to charge organic targets — and *underuses* his power in the recovery arcs, presenting as if returned to baseline. The deception is consistent with the character profile (concealment as default) and the operational note is: **the post-Death subject is more dangerous than he reports.**

### 1.5 The Hypercognition / Probability Read (the under-discussed power)

A consistent but under-explored secondary effect, documented intermittently from Claremont forward and explicitly elevated in the Carey *Legacy* run: the subject perceives the *kinetic potential* of his environment with abnormal clarity. He reads angles, surfaces, trajectories, and the energy state of moving objects faster and more accurately than an unenhanced human. This is the substrate of his card-throw accuracy (consistent multi-target hits in dense combat, blind shots, ricochets), of his unusually high evasion rate against bullets and energy weapons, and of his card-game proficiency.

It is not precognition. It is a *running real-time kinematic model* of his surroundings, generated by a brain that has been re-wired by being a charge-vector. He sees the world as a field of stored potential energies and probable trajectories. Some writers have flirted with this as "probability manipulation" or "luck" (especially Nicieza). The cleaner reading: he is not lucky, he is **constantly computing**.

---

## 2. THE GUILD CRAFT (NON-MUTANT ABILITIES)

The mutant power is the headline. The Guild training is the spine.

### 2.1 Theft, Infiltration, Sleight

Trained from infancy by Jean-Luc LeBeau and the New Orleans Thieves Guild in:

- **Lock work.** Mechanical, electronic, and several pre-electronic exotic systems. Documented bypass of museum-grade and Hellfire-Club-grade security. He carries dedicated picks but prefers improvised tools — a habit drilled in by Guild pedagogy: the thief who *needs* his tools can be disarmed.
- **Sleight of hand and stage-grade misdirection.** The card flourishes that read as flirtation are professional muscle memory; the cards he palms during conversation are operational rehearsal. He cheats at cards reflexively and at near-undetectable levels. He has picked the pockets of telepaths, of trained operatives, and — in one early story — of Charles Xavier.
- **Social engineering.** Voice modulation, accent shift (he can suppress the Cajun affect entirely when needed; the persistence of the accent around the X-Men is therefore *a choice*, see §4), cold-reading of marks, pretext construction, the long con. Operationally indistinguishable from the trade-craft of a working intelligence officer.
- **Free-running, climbing, infiltration movement.** Roofline routes, low-light navigation, silent entry. The Guild's training is pre-modern parkour married to second-story-man tradecraft.
- **Forgery and document work.** Less depicted but referenced; passes through borders under multiple identities without difficulty.

### 2.2 Combat

- **Bo staff.** His signature melee weapon, telescoping for concealment, used at near-master level. The staff is selected for three reasons: (a) it is a charge-substrate of significant mass, (b) it permits a fighting style that *keeps distance* — i.e., keeps the lethality of his hands away from his opponent, a tell, (c) Guild tradition.
- **Throwing.** Cards, coins, knives, improvised projectiles. Distinguished accuracy at range; the cards are merely the most *charged* projectiles, but the throwing skill is independent of the mutation.
- **Hand-to-hand.** Competent at the X-roster median: trained in savate and Guild-house close-quarters, with a strong preference for *avoiding* H2H precisely because his bare hands are the most dangerous part of him. He fights *gloved*, almost always, in part for fine-control reasons, in part for psychological insulation from his own touch.
- **Knife work.** Trained, used reluctantly. The duel with Julien Boudreaux that ended his New Orleans life was a blade duel; he has not since used the knife as a primary, which the file reads as avoidance behavior.

### 2.3 Mental Discipline

The Guild trained mental shielding as a professional discipline — thieves do not survive in a world of telepaths without it. The subject possesses a layered, trained, and *unusually durable* psychic shielding for a non-telepath. Notable: he has resisted, partially or fully, intrusions by Jean Grey (in restraint), Emma Frost (in irritation), the Shadow King (in extremis), and Apocalypse (in conversion, until augmented force overcame him). His shields are compartmentalized — he can present false surface thoughts while concealing deeper layers, a structure mirroring his everyday relational defenses. **The same neural architecture that hides his trauma from a lover hides his plans from a telepath.** This is not metaphor; it is the same tool.

### 2.4 Languages and Cultural Fluency

Native Cajun French; standard French; English (with operationally controllable accent); functional working knowledge of Spanish, Italian, Japanese (variably depicted), and several criminal-trade dialects. Reads room culturally at a near-savant level — the social-engineering substrate.

---

## 3. SIGNATURE APPLICATIONS

### 3.1 The Card Throw

A charged playing card, thrown underhand or backhand, detonating on impact or proximity. The signature is so well-established it functions as a *brand* — and the canonical use of *playing cards*, when coins or pebbles would serve identically, is not accidental. The card is *theatrical*. It is the gambler's tool. It announces who is throwing it. The signature is at once a combat efficiency (light, dense, throwable in volume, easy to fan and multi-charge) and a *self-identification ritual*: every card thrown is a small declaration of *I am still the man you think I am*, even in moments when the interior states otherwise. The card is a defense.

### 3.2 The Charged Staff

A melee detonator and pressure tool. He uses the staff to *touch without touching* — to apply force, to redirect bodies, to detonate near targets without contacting his own hands. The staff is the displaced glove.

### 3.3 The Quiet Charge (Set-and-Walk)

His most professionally distinctive application. He charges an object — a doorframe, a section of floor, a vehicle panel, a chess piece on a mark's desk — and walks away. Detonation at his chosen moment, often hours later. This is *thief's combat*: do the work in advance, be elsewhere when it matters. It is the application most consistent with his temperament and the one most often used in solo work.

### 3.4 The Card Flourish (Non-Combat)

Hand-warming, conversation-occupying, mark-distracting. The cards in his hands at all times serve the operational function of *keeping the hands seen* — a gesture that disarms in social settings while simultaneously rehearsing the muscle memory of throw-readiness. He performs the flourish unconsciously when thinking, when bored, when waiting, when uncomfortable. **It is the most reliable behavioral tell in the file**: when the cards stop, something is wrong.

### 3.5 The Uncharge

Rare. Documented. He pulls back a charge mid-deployment. The cost is somatic — a flinch, sometimes a nosebleed, sometimes a brief loss of fine motor control in the contacting hand. The operational use is the saving of a bystander or a teammate. The diagnostic use is everything: **he is the only person on the X-roster who has demonstrated the capacity to retract lethal force already committed.** No one else can put the bullet back in the gun. He can. And he has — repeatedly, quietly, at cost. This is the power-use that argues most powerfully against the self-image of irredeemability.

---

## 4. GROWTH AND CHANGE OVER TIME

### Early Era (Claremont, 1990 – early Lobdell)

Power presented as moderate, contact-mediated, slightly mysterious. Yield depicted at the "card-grenade" register almost exclusively. Tradecraft foregrounded — the early Gambit is a *thief who throws cards*. Mental shielding established early (resists Psylocke, slips Xavier).

### Mid Era (Nicieza, Mackie, post-Massacre Reveal)

Yields expand, willingness to use heavy charges increases, the *uncharge* is established. Hypercognition / kinematic-read introduced as text rather than implication. The power becomes more clearly a *spectrum* under voluntary control rather than a single trick.

### Apocalypse / Death Era (Austen, Carey)

Augmentation. Organic-matter charging. Body-as-bomb posture. Post-conversion *concealed* persistence of enhancements. The subject becomes operationally more dangerous and, per his pattern, *under-reports*. His own self-monitoring of power increases — there are several panels in Carey's run of him testing himself in private, charging small objects to gauge yield, like a man checking a wound that is healing badly.

### Krakoa Era (Hickman, Duggan)

Power presented as fully matured, integrated, professional. The captaincy of the Marauders ship places him in operational command of a rescue infrastructure that uses his charge work for *liberation* rather than detonation — charged barriers blown to extract refugees, charged distractions for evacuation. The *application* of the same mechanism shifts from harm to rescue. This is the most important *qualitative* growth: the power did not change, the *grammar* did.

### Late / Married Era (Thompson, Mr. and Mrs. X; subsequent)

Fine control at peak. The power used playfully — small charges to light cigarettes, to spark candles, intimate-scale uses that signal the integration of the mutation into a *domestic* register. This is, in its own way, the most striking growth datum in the file: the man who once nearly detonated his own body now uses the same mutation to light a match for his wife.

---

## 5. LIMITS AND VULNERABILITIES

- **Contact requirement.** Cannot charge what he does not touch. Sealed in glass, gloved (heavily) in inert material, restrained at distance — neutralized.
- **Object mass / charge-time curve.** Cannot instantly charge a tank. Larger objects require longer hold. In dynamic combat this constrains him to the small-and-fast end of the projectile spectrum.
- **Metabolic drain.** Large or sustained charges cost calories, hydration, and energy. He eats heavily after combat-heavy days; he is depicted lean precisely because the power runs hot.
- **Governor instability under stress.** The Sinister-installed neural inhibitor is *finite* and *vulnerable*. Acute trauma, telepathic intrusion, exhaustion, and specific triggers (Sinister proximity, Massacre cues) degrade fine control.
- **Cannot charge living tissue (baseline).** Without Apocalypse augmentation, organic matter resists the charge. This is the merciful limit — without it, every touch would be a potential murder. The post-Death persistence of the organic-charge capacity is therefore *the* concealed risk in the current file.
- **Cannot uncharge at scale.** The uncharge works on objects he is still in contact with, of moderate yield. He cannot recall a thrown charged card.
- **Mental shielding is finite under sustained assault.** Augmented telepaths or layered psychic attack can breach. The shielding is *very good for a non-telepath* — it is not a substitute for actual psi-defense.
- **Optical signaling.** The charge glows. He cannot deliver a charged object covertly in low light without giving away its state. The Quiet Charge is therefore set in cover or at distance.
- **Hand injury.** Damage to his hands disproportionately disables him — both his mutation and his Guild craft route through them. He guards his hands consciously. He fights to *keep* his hands.

---

## 6. THE SYMPTOM-AS-SIGNATURE READING

Every element of the powerset, read clinically, returns the same sentence in different keys: *this is a man whose hands are the problem and whose life is the management of his hands.*

- **He charges by touch, and his lover cannot be touched.** The mutation and the central relational selection are the same fact stated twice. The power that makes him dangerous to those he contacts and the partner whose skin protects her from contact are not coincidence — they are the somatic and the relational expressions of a single organizing problem. **To be safely loved, he had to find someone whose skin was already a glove.**

- **He wears gloves continuously.** Long before the X-Men, in flashback, in the field, in domestic scenes. The glove is *power discipline* (he cannot accidentally charge through fabric), *Guild discipline* (no prints), and *psychological discipline* (the constant reminder: your hands are loaded). Three functions, one habit. When he removes the gloves — for combat, for intimacy, for surgery on a teammate — it is *always* a marked moment in the panel. The glove off is the safety off.

- **The card flourish keeps the hands *seen*.** A man who knows his hands are weapons does not want them to disappear from a room's attention. The flourish is hypervigilant self-surveillance externalized. He watches his own hands the way a sniper watches his own muzzle.

- **The Bo staff is the displaced touch.** A reach extension that lets him strike without making contact. He chose, of all the weapons available to a trained thief, the one that *most consistently mediates between his body and another body*. Behaviorally: the staff is a glove for the whole arm.

- **The Set-and-Walk doctrine mirrors his relational pattern.** Place the charge, leave the room, let the consequence detonate without you present. Confession-by-violation rather than confession; truth detonates *to* the partner after he has walked away. He fights the way he loves: charge, exit, detonation in absentia.

- **The uncharge is the buried hope.** Of all his power-uses, this one is — psychologically — the most precious datum in the file. It says: *force already committed can, at cost to the self, be withdrawn.* It is the somatic proof, in his own body, that the bargain he believes he made with the Massacre (irrevocable, paid forever, never recoverable) is *not* the only physics his body knows. The uncharge is the secret evidence that redemption is mechanically possible. **He has it in his hands and does not allow himself to see it.**

- **The hypercognitive kinematic read is the operational form of his vigilance.** He has been hyperaware of every potential energy in every room since adolescence because his own body taught him that potentials become kinetics in an instant, fatally. The world he perceives is a world where everything is about to become something else. This is, in nervous-system terms, *the trauma posture as a visual modality*. He sees what he has been forced to see.

- **The Sinister governor is the file in microcosm.** His control is real, it is fine, it is hard-won, and it was bought with an atrocity he authored. Every act of precision he performs is a use of the gift bought with the Morlocks' lives. He cannot use his power without using *that*. There is no clean use of his hands. The mutation is the moral injury in tissue.

- **The Apocalypse augmentation and its concealment.** The post-Death enhancement of his power — and his refusal to disclose its persistence — is the somatic expression of his characterological pattern: *more dangerous than he reports, concealing the residue of the bargain with the father-figure, performing wholeness over a contamination he is managing alone.* His mutation, his trauma, and his relational pattern share an architecture.

- **The shift in grammar from detonation to rescue (Krakoa-era).** The mutation did not change. The captaincy of the rescue *Marauders* is the inverse signature of the criminal *Marauders*. The power that once delivered the Massacre now delivers refugees. The reaction-formation visible in the personality is now visible in the work product. **The hands that opened the tunnels now open the cages.**

---

## 7. OPERATIONAL SUMMARY

The subject is, in pure capability terms, a top-quartile X-roster asset: a mutant of moderate raw output but exceptional fine control, augmented by elite-tier tradecraft, weaponcraft, social engineering, and mental discipline, deployable across the full spectrum from black-bag infiltration through team combat to humanitarian extraction. He is the X-Men's most professionally complete *operator* — distinguished not by raw firepower (he is outclassed there by most of the roster) but by the breadth, integration, and precision of his toolkit.

The single most important operational note for any file using him: **his power is governed by surgically installed neural tissue, is degraded under emotional load, and is — secretly, post-Death — broader than he admits.** Any planning that does not price in (a) governor failure under acute stress and (b) concealed organic-charge residual is planning against the version of the asset he presents, not the version that exists.

The single most important *clinical* note: **every signature of the powerset — the glove, the staff, the card flourish, the set-and-walk, the choice of an untouchable partner, the secret uncharge — is the moral injury speaking through the mutation.** He cannot use his hands without using his history. The file is therefore not separable: the powers section and the psychiatric section describe the same man from two sides of the same skin.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT
## Subject: LeBeau, Remy Etienne — File Section 6 of 14

---

## 6.1 Foundational Framework: How the Subject Thinks Before He Acts

Subject's operational doctrine is **Guild-derived, X-Men-modified, and trauma-stabilized**. The Thieves Guild of New Orleans imparted, before adolescence, a complete tradecraft curriculum (reconnaissance, sleight-of-hand, lock work, social engineering, urban infiltration, escape-and-evasion, the *fence economy*, the etiquette of made-thieves vs. freelancers, the *honor brief* — what a Guild contract requires you not to do regardless of payment). Joining the X-Men did not overwrite this layer; it *contextualized* it inside a moral mission whose ethics he does not entirely share but whose people he loves. Operationally, this means **the subject runs Guild tradecraft on X-Men objectives**, which is why his operations look stylistically different from anyone else on the roster.

His decision-making sequence under operational load, derivable from the longitudinal record (Claremont's tactical scenes, the Nicieza solo's interior captions, Carey's *X-Men* infiltration arcs, Duggan's *Marauders* command sequences), proceeds approximately:

1. **Read the room before reading the brief.** Subject habitually arrives early to any operational space — a meeting, a target site, a rendezvous — and stations himself with sightlines to the exits and the principals. He has determined the social hierarchy of the room before anyone has stated it.
2. **Identify the *un-said* objective.** Decades of Guild contracting train him to assume the stated objective conceals a real one. He will execute the stated mission while quietly auditing whether it serves the real one. This makes him a poor follower of *literal* orders and an excellent follower of *intended* ones.
3. **Construct two plans, the second of which assumes the first is compromised.** Almost never visible in dialogue; visible in his persistent pre-positioning of caches, contacts, and fallback transport.
4. **Reserve a personal exit independent of team plan.** Not because he intends to abandon the team — historical record shows he does not — but because the Guild-trained operator does not enter a structure without his own egress.
5. **Decide late.** Subject is famous within-roster for committing to a course of action at the *last* tactically viable moment. Cyclops plans; subject improvises against a pre-built lattice of contingencies. This is not impulsivity. It is delayed commitment as a tradecraft principle: the longer one's posture remains ambiguous, the longer the opposition cannot orient.

---

## 6.2 Tradecraft — Larcenous Core Skillset

**Lock work.** Master class on physical locks of effectively any era and origin. The Guild curriculum, per Nicieza's flashback material, includes Old World tumbler systems, modern pin-tumbler, wafer, disc-detainer, lever locks, and the various electronic systems he has had to update against across the publication record. Subject carries a slim pick set on his person at all times — typically integrated into the lining of the coat or in a flat case the size of a playing-card deck — and supplements with improvised picks (paper clips, the spine of a card, hairpins) when stripped of kit. He has been depicted picking restraints from behind his back inside thirty seconds.

**Sleight-of-hand and palm work.** Trained to professional-stage-magician level and beyond. The card-charging signature is partly weapon, partly *stagecraft*: he handles cards constantly because the constant handling builds and maintains the manual dexterity on which all his other tradecraft depends. The deck is a *practice instrument disguised as a habit disguised as a weapon*. Documented capabilities: pickpocket on contact, plant items as readily as remove them (a tradecraft inversion most thieves never master), palm objects up to roughly the size of a small phone, perform the standard repertoire of false cuts, shuffles, forces, and reveals.

**Social engineering.** The most undervalued of his skillsets and arguably his most lethal. Subject can establish a credible cover identity inside a single conversation, will tailor accent and register downward or upward by class as the target requires (the Cajun is sometimes performance — see Section 6.10 on tells), and will *seed plausible alibis* in incidental conversation hours before a job, so that when a witness later reconstructs the evening they reconstruct his cover. He routinely conducts *pretextual* reconnaissance — entering target premises in a uniform, a delivery role, or as a guest of a guest — well in advance of any operation.

**Infiltration / E&E.** Comfortable on rooftops, in storm drains, in service corridors, in any liminal architecture. Subject reads buildings *as floor plans extended in time* — he is computing the patrol schedule of the security as he walks. Verified preference for vertical infiltration (in via roof, out via stairwell or service shaft) over horizontal. Will use vehicles for staging but tends to make the actual breach on foot.

**Fence economy.** Subject maintains, across decades, a working knowledge of who moves what at what discount in which port cities — New Orleans first, then New York, Madripoor, Hong Kong, Marseille, certain quiet rooms in London. He does not need to use this network for income (see Section 6.7) but uses it for *information*, which is the actual currency of the fence world.

---

## 6.3 Tradecraft — Combat & Power Application

The subject's combat doctrine is **mobility-first, distance-flexible, asymmetric**. He is not a brawler; he will not stand toe-to-toe with the heavy hitters of the roster and does not pretend to. His method:

**Bo staff.** Collapsible / telescoping, carried at the small of the back or down the line of the coat. The staff is preferred because (a) it extends his reach without committing him to a strike line, (b) it can be charged kinetically in a pinch, (c) it functions as climbing aid, lever, brace, and (d) it is non-lethal at default settings, which matters to his post-Massacre operating ethic. Trained in *bâton français* / *canne de combat* traditions visible in his stance work, blended with Guild close-quarters.

**Kinetic-charge cards.** The signature weapon is doctrinally specific: subject charges the card on the *throw*, not before, so the projectile is live for the minimum window. Throws are *flat*, with backspin, from the hip or across the body — almost never the overhand stage-throw the silhouette suggests. Range is variable by charge level, accuracy is professional-grade out to roughly twenty meters. He uses cards rather than coins because cards are *deniable*, *plentiful*, *aerodynamically tunable*, and — diagnostically — because they are the instrument of his identity. He will throw whatever is to hand if cards are not: pens, bolts, bottle caps. The card is signature, not requirement.

**Kinetic charge in melee.** Will charge an opponent's belt buckle, sidearm grip, watch, or jewelry on contact, with timed detonation. This is unusual and underestimated. Most opponents prepare for the *thrown* card; very few prepare for the fact that he has, in the clinch, charged something they are wearing.

**Restraint of lethality.** Power output is *titrated*. He almost never charges to maximum yield; he charges to the minimum required to achieve the tactical effect. This restraint is *post-Sinister, post-Massacre* and is enforced as a discipline. When he does loose maximum yield (rare; documented in extremis), it is psychologically costly and visible in subsequent withdrawal behavior.

**Power-immunity to his own kinetic field.** Subject can hold a charged object indefinitely without self-harm. This is exploited tactically: he will charge an object and *carry it* into position, releasing only at the moment of contact.

**Hypnotic charm.** Latent / occasional power, inconsistent across writers but canonical — a low-grade empathic / persuasive field. Subject *does not rely on it* and is on record (Nicieza solo) as actively distrusting it, because it produces compliance he cannot distinguish from genuine warmth and he does not want to be the kind of man whose love is induced.

**Telepathic resistance.** Guild-trained mental discipline plus the residual Sinister neural alteration produce one of the better non-telepath shielding profiles on the roster. He has resisted, evaded, or partially deceived telepaths including Jean Grey, the Stepford Cuckoos, and Emma Frost in close work. This makes him a uniquely valuable asset for operations *against* psionic adversaries and a uniquely difficult subject for *friendly* psychic medical intervention — a fact that has complicated every attempt to help him therapeutically.

---

## 6.4 Decision-Making Under Specific Operational Pressures

**When the team plan is sound:** Subject executes flawlessly, contributes incremental improvements at the margin, and does not draw attention to his contributions.

**When the team plan is flawed:** Subject will not argue in briefing. He will execute the plan up to the point of flaw, then *quietly substitute his own solution*, then accept whatever after-action criticism follows. This is a known and durable frustration to commanders (Cyclops in particular). It is not insubordination in the affective sense; it is the Guild operator's belief that the field, not the briefing room, is the venue of truth.

**When the mission requires moral compromise:** Subject will take the morally compromised role *off his teammates' shoulders*. The pattern is consistent: he volunteers for the interrogation, the deception, the kill, the deal with the unsavory broker, because (a) he believes himself already compromised and (b) he is protecting the moral self-conception of teammates he believes are *not* compromised. This is operationally invaluable and psychologically corrosive. See Section 3.

**When the mission requires harming a non-combatant:** Hard stop. Subject will abort, sabotage, or defect. The Morlocks are the bright line beneath which he will not be pushed. Any handler who has read this file should not test it.

**When his own power destabilizes mid-operation:** Documented behavior is to *withdraw from the team's immediate proximity*, work alone, and rejoin only when the charge is controllable. He will not put teammates at kinetic risk to remain in formation.

**When a credible father-figure offers control of his power:** See Section 4 risk profile. This is the catastrophic failure mode. Operational planning must price it in.

---

## 6.5 Infrastructure — Safehouses, Caches, Routes

Subject maintains a *distributed personal infrastructure* independent of X-Men/institutional resources. This is Guild reflex and is not a sign of disloyalty; every Guild operator maintains private infrastructure, and to do otherwise would be amateur. Documented or inferable elements:

- **New Orleans:** Multiple safe locations in the Quarter and the Garden District, some Guild-owned and accessible by family standing, some private. At least one rooftop apartment used as personal retreat. Knowledge of the Guild's tunnel and rooftop routes across the old city — *complete*, end-to-end, including routes that predate the modern street grid.
- **New York:** Safehouse(s) outside the Westchester compound, almost certainly in Manhattan and at least one in Brooklyn or Queens, used during periods of separation from the team. Routes to and from the mansion practiced obsessively (rail, road, river).
- **Madripoor:** Working contacts in Lowtown, fence relationships, at least one room he can take on short notice. Substantiated by *Wolverine*-era crossover material.
- **Europe:** Working knowledge of Marseille (Guild diaspora), Paris, London. Has operated in Westminster and the City; knows at least one cleared route through the Channel.
- **Caches:** Subject habitually pre-positions small kits — cards, picks, cash in mixed currencies, a clean shirt, a burner phone, a knife, sometimes a charged item left in a state of arrested charge — in locations across territories he frequents. *Estimated* number of active caches at any time: low double digits.

**Vehicles.** Comfortable across motorcycles (preferred for solo travel; a recurring depiction across decades), small fast cars, boats (Guild trained on Mississippi/Gulf craft; later qualified on ocean-going vessels per Marauders captaincy), small aircraft to passable pilot level. The Marauders captaincy in Duggan's run formalized blue-water seamanship at command level — a competence the file should note as having appreciated significantly in the last canonical era.

**Communications.** Burner-phone discipline. Will not carry a single phone for longer than an operation requires. Encrypted comms when issued by team; default-distrustful of any comm channel he has not personally vetted. Uses *non-electronic* dead-drops and brush-passes by preference for sensitive material — a Guild habit retained into the digital era and one of the reasons the subject is unusually hard to surveil by signals means alone.

---

## 6.6 Information Tradecraft

Subject is a **human-intelligence operator first, signals-intelligence consumer second.** He builds and maintains personal networks of barkeeps, dock workers, fence intermediaries, ex-Guild contacts, sex workers, low-level uniformed police, hotel concierges, and the diaspora of people who owe him favors from previous decades. He pays his sources in cash, in occasional protective intervention, and in *discretion* — he never burns a source, ever, and his retention rate is therefore unusually high.

He cultivates targets via **slow build**: he will spend weeks establishing a casual presence at a target's regular bar before ever speaking to them on operational terms. Subject is comfortable with the long game in a way that distinguishes him from teammates who default to direct approach.

He treats his *own* operational history as a network asset: people who remember him from prior operations are catalogued and re-approached when geographically convenient. He maintains a near-complete mental map of every meaningful operational encounter of his life, names and locations included. He keeps almost nothing in writing. The Guild-trained memory is the file system.

---

## 6.7 Finances

Subject's finances are **opaque, distributed, and probably comfortable**. He does not draw conspicuous compensation from any institution. The evidentiary base for inference:

- Decades of high-end Guild operations performed at minimum profit-share rates would have produced substantial capital.
- Subject's consumption is modest-to-moderate: good coats, good boots, good liquor, motorcycles, the occasional well-cut suit. He does not collect. He does not display.
- Subject demonstrates the habits of someone with *liquidity in mixed currencies and instruments* across multiple jurisdictions — he has never, in the record, been functionally stranded by lack of funds.
- He likely maintains accounts under multiple identities, holdings in gold or comparable instruments in at least one Guild-secured location, and small property holdings via shell arrangements in New Orleans and possibly Marseille.

He is not motivated by money. He is *liberated* by it. The accumulated capital removes the need ever to take a job on financial pressure, which preserves his ability to refuse work that violates his ethics. This is, again, Guild doctrine: the master thief does not steal *for* money, he steals *because he chose to* — and the way you preserve that distinction is by ensuring you never have to steal for money.

---

## 6.8 Operational Resources — People

- **The Thieves Guild (New Orleans, and diaspora).** Subject's standing is complicated and time-variable but durable. Even during periods of personal estrangement from Jean-Luc, Guild *etiquette* protects him in most jurisdictions where the Guild has standing.
- **Rogue.** Operational partner of last resort and first preference. Their tactical compatibility is unusually high — see Section 8 on dyad.
- **Storm.** Long-standing trusted handler-equivalent; subject will accept orders from her he will not accept from others.
- **Wolverine.** Functional working relationship despite mutual wariness; Wolverine has read him from the start, which subject simultaneously resents and respects.
- **Marauders crew (later era).** Subject's first sustained command. Behavior in command is *protective, low-ego, decision-decisive, willing to absorb blame upward and distribute credit downward* — textbook Guild captaincy reapplied.
- **Bella Donna Boudreaux.** Volatile asset. Sometimes operationally cooperative, sometimes adversarial; subject will not target her and she has, at intervals, returned the courtesy.
- **Mercy LeBeau, Theoren Marceaux, and the wider LeBeau / Guild family.** Long-tail familial obligations, periodically activated.

---

## 6.9 Operational Resources — Materiel (Carried)

Standard EDC, consistent across decades with minor era-drift:

- A deck of playing cards (working deck; he is rarely depicted with fewer than one in reach, and frequently more — coat pockets, inner lining, sometimes a deck box).
- Collapsible bo staff.
- Slim pick set.
- Folding knife, modest size, used more often as tool than weapon.
- Cigarettes / lighter (era-variable; the lighter is also a small flame source for utility use).
- A second lighter or matches kept separately. He does not run out of fire.
- Cash, mixed currencies, distributed across pockets so a single loss does not strand him.
- One or two burner-grade communications devices when on operations.
- Identification documents in working name plus at least one alternate.
- The coat itself — see 6.10.

---

## 6.10 Signature Operational Tells

This is the section a hostile analyst would dwell on. It is the section the subject would most regret being written.

**The coat.** The long coat is functionally a *kit*. It conceals the staff, the cards, the picks, the cash, the documents. It also breaks his silhouette, making him harder to ID at distance and harder to grapple at close. Operationally: when the coat comes off, he is preparing for sustained close combat. When the coat stays on, he is planning to leave soon.

**The deck in hand.** Constant card-handling is real practice but also a *baseline tell*. When the handling *stops* — when the cards go still or disappear into a pocket — he has shifted from social mode to operational mode. Anyone trained to watch him learns this quickly. He knows they learn it and sometimes *fakes the cessation* to spoof the read. Counter-counter-signal.

**Accent thickening under stress.** Documented and verifiable by comparing his interior captions (standard register) to his spoken dialogue under pressure (deepened Cajun). This is partly involuntary regression to mother tongue under load and partly *performance* — the thicker he leans on the Cajun affect, the more he is *managing* the room and the less spontaneous his behavior is. A handler reading the file should note: *very thick accent = he is in control and performing*; *flattened accent = he is genuinely shaken*. This is counter-intuitive but durable in the record.

**Cigarette as instrument.** When he smokes, he smokes for a reason: to mark time, to occupy his hands, to create a plausible reason to be stationary in a sightline, to offer one (a classic social-engineering opener), to time an exit by burn rate. He has been depicted *not lighting* a cigarette he has placed in his mouth — the cigarette as prop without combustion. A lit cigarette is a clock. An unlit cigarette is a prop.

**Eye contact.** Holds eye contact longer than social baseline. With targets, this is a deliberate control technique (the unusual sclera-iris combination is unnerving, and he weaponizes that). With intimates, it is genuine. The two modes are distinguishable: with targets, his eye contact is *steady and unblinking*; with intimates, it is *steady and blinks normally*.

**Hand position at rest.** Hands almost always *visible and occupied* — on the cards, on a glass, on a cigarette, on the staff. Hands going *out of sight* (into the coat, behind the back) is operational preparation. A handler watching him learns this. He knows that, too.

**Approach geometry.** Will not enter a room through the door an opponent expects. Will not sit with his back to a door. Will, in a long social engagement, *rotate his position* approximately every twenty to forty minutes — a Guild habit to refresh sightlines and disrupt anyone setting a long pattern on him.

**The flirtation pulse.** Flirtation intensifies in inverse proportion to actual romantic interest in the target — because the flirtation is *social lubricant*, not pursuit. With the actual chosen object (Rogue), the verbal flirtation is comparatively *less* performative and more direct. Anyone receiving florid charm from him should understand they are receiving stagecraft; anyone receiving quiet, plain affection should understand they are receiving the real signal.

**Time on target.** Subject is *fast in and fast out* on operations of his own design and *patient to the point of stillness* when surveilling. The pattern is bimodal; he does not linger in the active phase and does not rush the observational phase. A site he hits is rarely a site he scouted that day.

**Pre-action stillness.** In the seconds before committing to an action, subject becomes briefly, conspicuously *still*. The cards stop. The patter stops. The eyes settle. This is the most reliable indicator across the whole record that something is about to happen, and it is the one tell he cannot eliminate — though he has reduced its window over the years.

---

## 6.11 Operational Strengths and Failure Modes — Synthesis

**Strengths.** Distributed and durable infrastructure; deep human network; first-class infiltration and exfiltration; one of the few operators on the roster who can run an operation start-to-finish *without team support*; psionic-resistance superior to almost all non-telepaths; willingness to take morally costly roles; calibrated power use; loyalty to chosen individuals; protective default toward non-combatants.

**Failure modes.** Will not argue with bad orders, will simply not follow them — produces command friction. Will take on more moral cost than the operation warrants, producing post-operational psychological withdrawal that degrades availability. Will compromise mission to protect Rogue, children, or visibly outcast non-combatants — non-negotiable, must be planned around rather than against. Catastrophic failure mode: the bad-bargain reflex with a powerful figure offering power-control. Has happened twice. Will happen a third time if the conditions reassemble. **The single most important predictive line in this file.**

**Net operational assessment.** A first-tier covert operator whose technical tradecraft is at the ceiling of his cohort and whose deployment value to any moral community he has chosen is unusually high — *provided* the community understands that what they are receiving is a man paying rent on a place he does not believe he has earned, and that the rent is being paid in operational excellence that is, in the subject's private accounting, **inadequate to the debt and will remain so until he dies**.

— END SECTION 6 —
*Next section (7): Relational Mapping & Dyad Analysis.*


## Worldview & Operational Code

# WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE

## Remy Etienne LeBeau — Section 5 of the Working Dossier

---

## I. FIRST PRINCIPLES — THE METAPHYSICS OF A MAN BORN ALREADY-COMPROMISED

The subject does not hold what a philosopher would call a *system*. He holds something older and more durable: a set of rules-of-thumb hammered into him before he was old enough to argue with them, refined against thirty years of evidence, and now sitting in him at the level of reflex. Pressing him on the system produces shrug-and-charm; watching him operate produces the system in clear outline. The dossier therefore derives the code from behavior and from the rare moments of unguarded interiority (the captioned monologues across the Nicieza solo, the post-Antarctica recollections in Carey's run, the marriage-eve internal address in Thompson's *Mr. & Mrs. X* #1), rather than from any stated creed.

**The foundational axiom**, around which everything else organizes, is this: *the world is a place where someone was already using you before you knew there was a you to use.* He was bargained for in infancy; he was raised toward a function; he was loved conditional on utility; he was surgically modified by a man who needed a tool. By the time the subject was capable of holding an ethical opinion, he had already been the instrument of three competing agendas. From this he derives the operational corollary that **innocence is not a default state, it is a privilege of the well-parented**, and he does not extend himself the courtesy of pretending he ever possessed it. Other people may have been good before they were tested; he was tested before he was good.

This is not nihilism. The subject is, in his own peculiar register, a deeply moral man. But his morality begins from a *post-fall* premise: the question is never "how does one live an unblemished life?" because that question was answered no for him in the cradle. The question is always **"how does someone already implicated live in a way that adds rather than subtracts?"** Everything in his operational code is a partial answer to that single question.

---

## II. THE WORLD AS HE READS IT

### A. Institutions

The subject distrusts institutions as a category, and this distrust is finely calibrated rather than ideological. He has been used by four kinds of institution — a criminal Guild, a scientific-eugenic project, an apocalyptic religious-prophetic apparatus, and a humanitarian mutant-rights team — and notes, correctly, that *the form of the bargain is identical in each case*. The institution offers belonging, training, identity, and protection. In return the institution requires service whose full nature is never disclosed at the point of signing. The X-Men are, in the subject's private accounting, the most honest of these institutions and the one whose service-bill he is happiest to pay, but he does not lie to himself about its category. Xavier picked his pocket too, in another sense.

Consequently he treats every institutional command as a *proposal*, never an order. He nods, he assents, he goes through the door — and then, once out of the room, he operates by his own read. He will not be told to do something he believes wrong; he will not argue about it; he will simply not do it, and he will accept the social cost when discovered. This is not insubordination in the ordinary sense, which is defiance for the pleasure of defiance. This is the disposition of a man who learned early that *he* is the only audit on his own conduct, because every institution that ever held him misused him, and he is not about to outsource his conscience to one more.

### B. Power

Power in the subject's worldview is morally neutral, materially decisive, and **almost always misused by those who hold structural quantities of it**. He has watched powerful men (Sinister, Apocalypse, Magneto in his Acolyte phase, the Guild patriarchs, the X-Tribunal that judged him at the Trial) shape lives at scale, and he has not seen any of them shape lives well. His preferred level of operation is therefore *small*: one operator, one room, one outcome, no witnesses. He distrusts plans that require many people to do the right thing at once. He trusts plans that route around the question of trust entirely.

His own power he treats with a specific kind of horror. The kinetic charge is not, for him, an ability — it is a *liability under temporary management*, and the management is medical (the Sinister excision) rather than virtuous. He does not feel he has earned the control he has; he feels he was given it by a monster, in payment for a worse thing he then did. The hand that can charge a card can also detonate a child, and the only thing standing between those two outcomes is a piece of brain tissue that was removed from him without consent and replaced with conditioning. From this he derives the rule that **one's own power is the first thing one must distrust**, which makes him an unusually steady combatant — he has already done the existential work most operators only do after their first accidental kill.

### C. Conflict

Conflict, to him, is a *negotiation conducted by other means*, almost never an event with a moral structure. He does not believe in fair fights; the concept strikes him as a category error, like a fair theft. A fight is something you arrange so that you have already won by the time the other party realizes it has started. If you find yourself in a fair fight, you have made a planning error. He extends this to verbal and emotional conflict, which is part of why he can be maddening in argument — he is not trying to win the argument on its merits, he is trying to *exit* the argument with the relationship intact and the operationally important information still in his possession.

He distinguishes carefully between **adversaries**, **opponents**, and **enemies**. An adversary is someone whose interests cross yours in a given transaction; you negotiate, you may even dine. An opponent is someone playing the same game on a different team; respect is appropriate, lethality is not the default. An enemy is someone who would erase you and yours from the board; against enemies he is, by his own quiet admission, capable of things he does not want the team to see. The Guild taxonomy. He uses it constantly.

He believes conflict is **almost always avoidable, and almost always sought anyway**, because most people are bad at distinguishing between needing to win and needing to feel they have won. He himself rarely needs to feel he has won.

### D. Trust

Trust, in his code, is **never a feeling and always a structure.** He does not "trust" people; he constructs situations in which the person's incentive to betray him is lower than their incentive to perform. He extends what looks like trust freely — the warm hand on the shoulder, the easy disclosure, the "chere" — because this is *rapport*, which is a different thing entirely, and rapport is the cheap currency he uses for the surface-layer transactions of ordinary life.

Actual trust, in his private accounting, is given to perhaps four or five people across the entire canon, and it is given on the basis of *demonstrated tolerance for his worst self*, not on the basis of declared loyalty. Rogue earns it because she saw the Massacre in his memories and eventually, after the long detour, came back. Storm earns it because she recruited him knowing he was a thief and held that knowledge without leveraging it. Logan earns it on a separate axis — Logan is trusted not to forgive but to *understand*, because Logan has his own list of things he cannot metabolize, and this makes him safe in a way an innocent could never be. Henri, Mercy, Tante Mattie occupy a Guild-tier of trust that is older and structurally different — a familial trust held even across periods of estrangement.

Everyone else gets rapport, charm, useful loyalty, and protected information. He believes this is the correct way to live among people, and he believes anyone who claims otherwise is either lying or has not yet been hurt enough.

### E. Risk

He is, by temperament and training, an excellent estimator of risk and a very poor estimator of *his own welfare* in the risk calculus. This is the file's most important behavioral asymmetry. He will assess a heist or a rescue with cold accuracy, price the variables correctly, plan a route that no one else on the roster could plan, and then *exclude himself from the protected list* when allocating exposure. He volunteers for the worst job not from bravado but from a settled belief that his own life is the most expendable item in inventory. He will not say this aloud; the team has noticed it anyway.

His risk philosophy proper: **prefer the small known risk over the small unknown one; prefer two small risks taken serially over one large risk taken once; never accept a risk whose downside you have not already imagined surviving.** He breaks this last rule only in matters concerning Rogue, and he knows it.

### F. Time

He thinks in **two clocks**. The first is the operational clock of the immediate scene — seconds and meters, the thief's clock, where his read is excellent and his decisions are crisp. The second is a long, slow, almost geological clock of *consequence*, on which the Morlock tunnels are still happening, on which everything he does in any given week is being weighed against the same unchanging counterweight. He does not believe in catharsis, statutes of limitations, or the metaphysical possibility of being done. The penance is the practice; the practice is the life; the life has no terminal state in which the debt is cleared. This is not depressive — he has, by long habit, made peace with it — but it is the temporal background against which all his decisions are made, and it explains why he never quite celebrates a win the way the others do.

### G. Other People
