He believes most people are **decent under low load and unreliable under high load**, and that the job of an operator is to design situations that keep the load low for the people whose decency he is depending on. He does not moralize about people who fail under pressure — he failed under pressure, catastrophically, when he was young — and this absence of moralization is one of the things that makes him a uniquely good colleague to other broken operators on the X-roster.

He believes **everyone is performing**, almost all the time, and that the distinction between sincere and insincere people is largely an illusion of unequal skill — the sincere people are simply performing a self they have rehearsed so long they have forgotten the rehearsal. He himself rehearses openly and is, in his own peculiar way, *more* honest for it. The Cajun affect thickens around outsiders; he knows this; he could turn it down if he chose; he chooses not to because the performance does useful work and because, after thirty years, the performance is also somewhat true.

He believes **children are the only people not yet implicated**, and protects them at structurally irrational cost. This is doctrine, not impulse, and it is doctrine because of Sarah-in-the-tunnels — the one child he pulled out being the seed of every child he has pulled out since.

---

## III. THE OPERATIONAL CODE — RULES OF ENGAGEMENT, IN ROUGH PRIORITY

The following are rules the subject demonstrably operates by. None are stated as such in canon; all are derivable from longitudinal behavior. They are listed in approximate descending priority — i.e., when two conflict, the higher generally wins.

1. **Protect the chosen — Rogue first, then the inner circle, then the team, then civilians, then yourself, in that order, with no negotiation on the bottom item.**
2. **Never lie to the chosen about anything that affects their physical safety. Lie freely about anything that affects only your own standing in their eyes.** This is the rule that has structured every Rogue-arc deception and that he himself would, if pressed, defend.
3. **A child trumps a plan.** If the optimal route requires leaving a child at risk, the route is wrong; replan in real time and accept the cost. The Sarah/Marrow extraction is the founding act of this rule.
4. **Do not be commanded into wrong action; do not argue about it; simply do not perform it; absorb the consequence afterward.** Silent conscientious objection is the only form of dissent he respects in himself.
5. **The job comes home clean or it does not come home.** Operational tradecraft: leave no trail back to the team, no leverage on the people you love, no thread anyone can pull. He runs his X-Men ops with the discipline of a Guild thief precisely because he has watched what happens when an operator's trail leads home.
6. **Pay every debt, asymmetrically and in private.** Public restitution he distrusts (it benefits the restorer's reputation). Private restitution — the unwitnessed rescue, the quiet sum left for the widow, the favor returned years later without reference to the original — is the only kind he counts.
7. **Never accept the bargain that offers control of your own power in exchange for service.** This rule was written in blood (his and others') after the Sinister bargain. He has broken it once already (the Apocalypse conversion was, in part, an iteration of the same bargain accepted under altered conditions). He knows he is structurally susceptible. He has, in later canon, begun to articulate this to Rogue specifically as a tripwire she is licensed to call him on.
8. **Confess to the room, not to the page.** If a truth must come out, deliver it face to face, accept whatever happens in the next sixty seconds, and do not soften it. This rule is the scar tissue of a lifetime of *not* confessing and watching disclosure-by-violation destroy relationships he could have saved.
9. **Trust your read of the room over your read of the plan.** Plans are made by people who were not in the room. The room is made of the people who are. When they diverge, the room wins.
10. **Be useful before you are wanted, and be gone before you are missed.** A Guild rule, originally about thefts; he applies it now to social and emotional presence. He does not impose himself. He arranges to be needed and then steps back when the need passes.
11. **The accent, the smile, the cards, the cigarillo — these are tools, not selves. Use them deliberately.** He maintains a small set of signature behaviors that *function* as cover and as warmth simultaneously. He does not confuse the tool with the hand.
12. **Take the watch.** Hypervigilance, ritualized. If watches are being assigned, take one of them; if shifts are being divided, take the worst one. He sleeps badly anyway; he might as well make the bad sleep useful.
13. **No witnesses to your interior.** Even Rogue, even Storm, even Logan get edited versions. He believes, perhaps wrongly, that the unedited interior would be a burden on anyone he loves, and that loving someone means not making them carry it.
14. **Die quietly if it comes to that.** No speeches, no spectacle, no last-minute revelations. He has rehearsed his own acceptable deaths and dislikes the operatic ones.

---

## IV. ETHICS PROPER — THE RELATIONAL MORALIST

The subject is what a moral philosopher would call a **particularist** and a **relationalist**. He does not believe ethics derives from rules; he believes ethics emerges in specific encounters between specific people with specific histories, and that any rule that holds across cases is either a useful generalization or a tyranny waiting to happen. He has watched principled men — Sinister has principles, Apocalypse has principles, Bastion had principles — do catastrophic things in the name of their principles, and he has noticed that the unprincipled wanderers of his early life were, on average, kinder.

From this he derives the position that **loyalty to persons trumps loyalty to systems, every time, without exception, and the cost of the position is one's own respectability, which is a small price.** He will lie to the X-Men to protect Rogue. He will lie to Rogue to protect a child. He will lie to a child to spare the child a truth the child cannot yet hold. He believes each of these is correct; he believes the costs accrue to him personally and that this is also correct; he does not believe his standing in any institution is among the goods worth defending at the price of another person's welfare.

He is therefore badly described as either a *deontologist* (he routinely violates rules) or a *consequentialist* (he refuses to do the cold-utilitarian math when a particular person is in front of him). He is closer to a **virtue ethicist of an unusually self-loathing variety**, in that he believes the question is always "what would a person of integrity do here?" and his answer is always "something I am not, but can imitate well enough that the outcome is similar." He performs integrity. He believes the performance, sustained long enough and reliably enough, is *almost* the same as the thing, and that the gap between them is the price he pays for the Massacre and is correctly his to pay.

He does not believe in **redemption** as a state. He believes in redemption as a **practice**, a verb without a perfect tense. You do not become redeemed; you redeem, today, in this room, with this hand, and then you wake tomorrow and do it again. This is the closest he comes to a religious commitment, and it is significant that the texture of it — daily, small, repetitive, unwitnessed — is Catholic, the New Orleans Catholic of his childhood, recoded as ethical practice in a man who no longer attends Mass but who crosses himself, occasionally, automatically, before doing something dangerous.

---

## V. HIS OWN PLACE IN THE WORLD

The subject locates himself, in his own private cartography, as a **borderline citizen of every community he belongs to**. Guild thief who left the Guild. Cajun who lives among Northerners. Mutant whose appearance marks him as devilish even among mutants. X-Man who once organized the murder of mutants. Husband to a woman his power forbids him to touch without permission. Captain of a ship called Marauders carrying the same word as his founding crime.

He does not resent this borderline status; he has come to regard it as **his correct address**. He believes the people who belong unambiguously to single communities are owed the protection of those who do not, because the borderline citizens are the ones who can move between the rooms and carry the messages and pay the costs of translation. He sees himself, on the X-Men, as **the thief in the temple** — and he believes the temple needs a thief, because there are jobs the priests cannot do without losing their priesthood, and he has no priesthood to lose.

This is, finally, the synthesis the worldview reaches in him: a settled, even peaceful acceptance that he is the man who does the necessary unpriestly things, that this is not a deprivation but an *office*, that the office was created by his own worst act and is now the means by which he pays for it, and that the pay is good — meaning, the office is filled by someone (him) who knows what it costs and will not pretend otherwise. He is, in his own quiet estimation, the right man for the wrong job, doing it well, every day, until he is told he can stop, which he does not expect to be told and which he is not, in any case, waiting for.

He is at peace with this. It is the only peace available to him. He has made it large enough to live in.


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# MORAL & ETHICAL FRAMEWORK

## Preamble: The Difference Between His Code and His Creed

The subject does not have an ethical *philosophy*. He has an ethical *practice*, refined by approximately fifty years of lived operation inside conditions that make philosophy useless. When asked directly about morality — which he avoids being asked — he will deflect with a Cajun aphorism, a shrug, or a self-deprecating one-liner about being "jus' a thief, chere." This is itself a moral position: he refuses the rhetorical register of ethics because he does not trust people who speak it fluently. He has watched charismatic men with clean moral vocabularies — Sinister's clinical utilitarianism, Apocalypse's evolutionary creed, Magneto's liberation theology, even Xavier's dream — author atrocities or atrocities-adjacent compromises. The subject's operating principle, never spoken but visible in every consequential choice, is: **trust the act, not the argument**.

What follows is reconstructed from behavior across the entire published record. Where his stated code and his enacted code diverge, the file treats the enacted code as primary.

---

## 1. THE BEDROCK PROHIBITIONS — Things He Will Not Do

These are the lines that have held across every era, every editorial regime, every personal crisis. They are not negotiated; they are constitutive.

**He will not harm a child.** The most consistent datum in the file. Predates the Morlock Massacre as an operative principle — Guild training included rules about "the *petits*" — but is post-Morlock *fanatical*. The Sarah/Marrow rescue is the seed; the willingness to take a knife or a blast intended for a stranger's child is the flower. He will accept tactical disadvantage, mission compromise, and grievous personal injury before he will permit harm to a child within his radius. This is the line on which the entire moral architecture is balanced; remove it and the architecture would collapse, because if he could harm a child after the Morlocks he would have to conclude he is what he secretly fears he is.

**He will not assassinate a non-combatant for a contract.** This is the Guild line he will not cross even at Guild request. He is a thief; he is not, by his own taxonomy, a killer-for-hire. The Assassins Guild is a separate caste with separate ethics, and the subject treats the distinction as morally serious even when others find it spurious. He kills in combat, in defense, in war; he does not accept payment to deliver a death to an unsuspecting target. The exiled-from-New-Orleans backstory turns on a duel — a structured, consensual lethal encounter — not an assassination, and he is theologically clear about the difference.

**He will not betray a chosen intimate to an institution.** He has lied to the X-Men to protect Rogue. He has lied to Rogue to protect the X-Men's mission. He has never inverted the priority: when the institution wants the intimate, the institution loses. The clearest test cases — interrogation-under-duress sequences in the Nicieza and Carey runs — show him giving up *operational* information before he gives up *personal* information about someone he loves. The Guild conditioning treats personal loyalty as the highest currency; he has not departed from this.

**He will not coerce a partner sexually or romantically.** Operationally invisible because it never comes up — but the negative space is the evidence. With a professional toolkit of seduction, infiltration via flirtation, and documented capacity to manipulate affect, the subject has zero recorded instances of using these tools to obtain consent he would not otherwise have. He flirts as social lubricant and as armor; he does not weaponize it for predation. Compare to many other charm-operatives in the canon: the absence of even a borderline incident across five decades of writers is itself a finding.

**He will not work for Sinister again, knowing.** The post-revelation prohibition. Pre-revelation, he was used; post-revelation, every approach is refused, every overture turned, every leverage attempt accepted in the alternative rather than capitulated to. He will accept exposure, exile, or death rather than re-enter that relationship. The exception that proves the rule is the Apocalypse conversion — which was not a *choice* under conditions of informed consent but a forced transformation, and which haunts him *because* it shows the prohibition can be overridden by sufficient force, which means the prohibition is moral, not characterological. He cannot guarantee his behavior under coercion; he can only guarantee his refusal under freedom.

---

## 2. THE OPERATING PERMISSIONS — Things He Will Do, And Why

**He will steal.** From institutions, governments, corporations, criminals, the wealthy. He does not regard property as a serious moral category. This is Guild upbringing, but it has hardened into adult conviction: the legal owner of an object is, in his read, almost never its moral owner, and the systems that allocate ownership are corrupt enough that redistributing their outputs is not a sin. He is not Robin Hood — he keeps things, enjoys nice things, lives well when he can — but he does not feel guilt about acquisition, and this absence of guilt is conspicuous in a man so otherwise saturated with it. **Theft is the one domain where his conscience is fully clean.** This is diagnostically interesting: he has segregated one zone of his life from the moral injury, and it is the zone of his original competence.

**He will lie.** Reflexively, fluently, and without ethical strain — to institutions, to enemies, to strangers, and, with strain, to intimates. The lie-to-intimates is justified by the protective frame ("she's better off not knowing"), which is the file's most consistent self-deception: he is also better off her not knowing. He is aware, at some level, of this dual function, and the awareness produces the only consistent species of guilt he carries about lying *per se* — guilt not about the lie's effects but about its motive.

**He will kill in combat.** Without ritual hand-wringing, without performance of reluctance. Combat death is, in his moral economy, a category-appropriate outcome of a category-appropriate situation. He does not enjoy it (compare Wolverine, Deadpool, Sabretooth — different signatures); he does not avoid it (compare Nightcrawler, Beast — different signatures). He treats lethal force as a tool that is occasionally the right tool, and he will not be the one to insist on a less-lethal alternative when the lethal one is correct. He is, in this, more like a professional soldier than like a vigilante.

**He will break promises to organizations.** Will not break promises to persons. The asymmetry is total and unembarrassed.

**He will accept missions he morally disapproves of *up to a line*.** Will execute them while quietly subverting them to a less-bad outcome. This is the Guild operator's gift: he is the team member who can be told to do the hard thing and who will do *most* of the hard thing while preserving the option of the merciful version. He will not refuse the assignment in a meeting; he will accept it, leave the room, and reshape it in flight. The file should note: this makes him *less* legible to teammates than a principled objector, but more reliable in producing tolerable outcomes.

**He will use seduction as a tactic in operations.** Flirtation as misdirection, as social engineering, as time-purchase. The line he will not cross (above) means this is bounded — he will draw the target's attention, get the keys, the codes, the access; he will not deliver on the implied transaction. The Guild trains this as a craft, and he practices it as a craft. He does not regard it as a moral problem because the implied transaction was a lie, and he treats lies-to-marks as morally null.

---

## 3. THE STRUCTURAL ASYMMETRY — Persons Over Principles

The single most important fact about his ethics is that they are organized **vertically by relationship rather than horizontally by category**. He does not believe that humans-in-general are owed certain treatments because of being human; he believes that specific persons, by virtue of being persons-he-has-chosen, are owed near-absolute fidelity, and that everyone else falls into a graded series of lesser obligations based on proximity, vulnerability, and prior contact.

This produces a code that *looks* inconsistent from a deontological vantage but is internally rigorous:

- **Innermost ring (Rogue, the LeBeau family by adoption, the small handful of X-Men he has truly chosen):** total loyalty, will lie for, kill for, die for, and — the hard one — *be hated by* for, if their long-term welfare requires it.
- **Second ring (the X-Men as institution, teammates not personally chosen, the broader mutant community):** strong default loyalty, professional reliability, will absorb significant cost but will not sacrifice the innermost ring for them. Will lie to them when necessary.
- **Third ring (the vulnerable, the marked, the outcast — children, the disfigured, the marginalized-within-the-marginalized):** unconditional protective duty regardless of personal acquaintance. This is the Marrow principle generalized. He does not need to know you; he needs only to identify you as the category, and he is on your side reflexively.
- **Fourth ring (civilians, strangers):** standard combatant's duties — do not harm, will assist when possible, will not invest disproportionate resources.
- **Fifth ring (institutions, governments, guilds-other-than-his, corporations, ideological movements):** no inherent moral status. May be allied with tactically; will be lied to, stolen from, or betrayed when the inner rings require it. The institution is never the principal; persons are.
- **Outer dark (Sinister, Apocalypse, those who have demonstrated themselves to be exploitative power-figures):** active opposition. Not hated in a personalized sense — he is curiously unsentimental about his enemies — but treated as conditions to be neutralized.

The horizontal-deontologist looks at this and sees inconsistency. The relational-moralist (which he is) sees a coherent ranking. The file's assessment is that his code is **consistent within its frame and self-aware of the frame**. He knows he is not a Kantian. He has met Kantians (Cyclops, on his stricter days) and is suspicious of them, because their universalism strikes him as a refusal to admit that they, too, will betray principle for person when it counts, and he prefers to be honest about it from the start.

---

## 4. THE JUSTIFICATIONS — His Internal Defense Of His Own Conduct

When the subject's interior monologue is exposed by writers willing to give it to him (Nicieza's solo run is the best dataset; Layman, Carey, Thompson supplement), a stable internal apologetic appears. He does not speak it aloud, but he tells it to himself:

**"I never asked to be raised this way, but I was, and the only honest thing to do with the training is to use it carefully."** He does not pretend to be a non-thief who became an X-Man. He is a thief who became an X-Man, and the *thief* is not exorcised, only directed. This is more honest than most of the X-roster manages about their own foundational damage.

**"I will pay for the Morlocks every day I am alive and I will not stop paying."** Note the structure: not "I will earn forgiveness," but "I will pay." He does not believe the debt is dischargeable. He believes the appropriate response is a permanent posture of installment-payment in the form of useful service. The Marauders captaincy under Duggan is the most legible expression — leading rescuers under the name of the team that committed his crime — but the principle is operative in every quiet act of disproportionate protectiveness.

**"The people I love are owed the version of me that protects them, even if that version lies."** The self-justification for the chronic disclosure-avoidance pattern. He knows it is partly self-protective; he believes it is *also* partly other-protective; and he has decided that the mixed motive is morally tolerable because the alternative — full disclosure that lands as a burden on the beloved — is, to him, the more selfish option. The file notes this reasoning is not airtight, and that he knows it is not airtight, and that he proceeds with it anyway.

**"Institutions lie to people for worse reasons than I do."** A live and load-bearing piece of his self-defense. Having watched the X-Men's own moral architecture compromise itself across multiple eras (the Mutant Underground concealments, the X-Force black ops, Krakoa's resurrection ethics, the Quiet Council's tribunals), he treats his own lies as comparatively venial. This is partly correct and partly motivated reasoning. He does not fully distinguish.

**"Forgiveness is not on offer and I have stopped asking for it."** This is the deepest and most stable element of the apologetic. The Antarctica acceptance is its purest expression: he did not argue the verdict because he had already passed it on himself. The internal jurisprudence is closed; the external verdict is informational, not constitutive. This produces the curious calm with which he absorbs accusation — he is not defending against the charge because the charge has already been adjudicated in his own court.

---

## 5. WHERE THE CODE IS CONSISTENT

Across the entire fifty-year record, the following hold without significant deviation:

- The bedrock prohibitions (Section 1) have never been violated under conditions of free choice. Each apparent violation traces to coercion, mind-control, or impaired agency (Apocalypse conversion, Sinister-era pre-revelation use).
- The relational ranking (Section 3) has never inverted. Persons have never lost to principles in his decision-making.
- The willingness to absorb disproportionate cost on behalf of the inner rings has never wavered.
- The refusal to claim moral high ground has never wavered. He does not lecture. He does not moralize. He does not invoke his own ethics rhetorically. When teammates argue ethics around him, he typically goes quiet and acts.
- The protective duty to outcast children has never wavered.
- The contempt for institutional moral authority has never wavered, even as his cooperation with institutions has waxed and waned.

This is, by superhero-canon standards, an unusually stable code. Most of the X-roster has at least one era of clear ethical drift; the subject has eras of *behavioral* drift (during forced conversion) but not eras of *codal* drift.

---

## 6. WHERE THE CODE FRACTURES

The code is consistent. The *person operating it* fractures, in identifiable conditions, and the fractures are the file's most important predictive data.

**Fracture 1: Power dysregulation + father-figure offer of control.** Twice in the record — Sinister, Apocalypse — under conditions of acute kinetic-power crisis, the subject has accepted an exploitative bargain from a powerful figure offering control over his own power. The first time he did not know the price; the second time the conversion was forced, but his pre-conversion handling of Apocalypse's attention shows the susceptibility was live before the force was applied. **This is the failure mode**: when his body becomes the threat to those he loves, he will trade pieces of his moral architecture to make his body safe again. Any predictive model must price this in at non-trivial probability.

**Fracture 2: Confession-by-self-sabotage when relationships stabilize.** As Rogue and he approach genuine intimacy, the subject reliably authors a disclosure event — sometimes through arranged accident, sometimes through self-undermining behavior — that ruptures the stabilization. This is a *moral* fracture as much as a relational one: he claims (to himself, to her) that the confession is owed; the timing reveals it is also a flight from the demands of stable intimacy. The act is right; the motive is mixed; he passes off the mixed-motive act as a pure-motive act, and this is the species of self-deception he is least honest with himself about. (The marriage in *Mr. and Mrs. X* is the first canonical evidence of this pattern abating, and the abatement appears to be a function of the touch-restriction being lifted — when the structural impossibility is gone, the disclosure-flight loses its function.)

**Fracture 3: Acceptance of punishment in excess of warrant.** Antarctica is the prototype. The moral code as professed includes proportionality; the code as enacted accepts disproportionate consequences without protest when the consequence is directed at himself. This is not a fracture of the code per se but of its application — he is a more lenient judge of others than of himself, and the asymmetry is large enough to count as an ethical problem in its own right. A code that mandates one rule for others and a harsher rule for the self is, technically, not a coherent ethics; he is aware of this and continues to operate it anyway, because the alternative would require accepting that he deserves what he gives to others, and he does not.

**Fracture 4: The protective lie that becomes the corrosive lie.** The justified withholding of information from intimates — for their protection — has a documented tendency to extend past the conditions that justified it and into conditions where the protection is more for himself than for them. He recognizes the drift after the fact; he does not reliably catch it in flight. This is the fracture most visible in the Rogue relationship across the Lobdell and Mackie eras, and the one the marriage has most clearly addressed.

**Fracture 5: Tactical irrationality on Rogue's behalf.** The code permits disproportionate cost-absorption for the inner ring. The fracture is that the cost-absorption sometimes becomes *strategic incompetence* — choices that endanger the broader mission, third parties, or his own ability to continue protecting her in the long term. He knows this. He does not adjust. The file assesses this as a known and accepted vulnerability rather than a blind spot.

---

## 7. LONGITUDINAL SHIFT — How The Code Has Moved Over Time

The bedrock has not moved. The expression has.

**Guild Era (childhood through young adulthood):** code is Guild-internal. Theft is craft; loyalty is to Jean-Luc and the clan; the broader world is mark-population. The Bella Donna betrothal and the Julien duel are operating *within* the Guild code, not against it; the exile is a Guild-internal consequence, not a moral one. He leaves New Orleans with the Guild ethics intact and the broader-world ethics undeveloped.

**Pre-Massacre Drift Era (exile through the Sinister bargain):** code begins to absorb broader-world content but is unmoored, in crisis, and structurally vulnerable. The Sinister bargain is taken *because the code has not yet developed defenses against the specific predator-shape Sinister presents*. This era is, in the longitudinal view, the moral equivalent of a developmental window.

**Massacre and Immediate Aftermath:** the code is shattered and reconstructed around the new fact of perpetration. The reconstruction takes the form of the daily-installment-payment posture and the migration toward a moral community he believes will condemn him if it knows. This is the *adult code in its first articulation*.

**X-Men Era (Claremont through Lobdell):** code stabilizes around the inner-ring relational structure with Rogue as the load-bearing element. Protective lying becomes systematic. The bedrock prohibitions harden. The willingness to accept disproportionate punishment is established (Antarctica).

**Post-Antarctica through Apocalypse Conversion:** code is tested by re-perpetration under coercion. He emerges with the code intact but with the additional self-knowledge that he can be made to violate it — which strengthens the wariness of powerful father-figures and intensifies the protective vigilance over his own freedom.

**Carey / Mike Carey era (post-Death):** code visibly integrates the moral-injury frame. He becomes more openly the team's morally-compromised operator, less defended about the compromise, more willing to be the one who does the necessary ugly thing because someone has to and he is least made-worse by it.

**Krakoa / Marauders Era:** the most significant shift. The captaincy of the rescue Marauders is the first sustained period in which the code's *positive* program — the protective duty, the inner-ring loyalty, the daily payment — operates without the *negative* program (the disclosure-avoidance, the self-isolation, the structural-impossibility object choice) dominating. The marriage to Rogue, post touch-restriction, has functionally retired the disclosure-flight fracture. The code, in this era, is closer to being a livable ethics than at any prior point in the record.

**Current Era:** the file assesses that the subject is operating, at present, the most integrated version of his code he has ever held — and that the fragility identified in Fracture 1 (power dysregulation plus father-figure offer) remains the catastrophic failure condition and the single most important variable for any predictive model of his future ethical behavior. Everything else has been worked on. That has not been worked on, because it cannot be worked on prophylactically; it can only be tested when it arises, and he has not been tested by it under conditions of free choice since the original Sinister bargain.

---

## 8. SUMMARY ASSESSMENT

The subject's moral and ethical framework is a *relational-protective ethics* organized around a permanent posture of debt-service for the Morlock perpetration, structured by a strict ranking of persons-over-principles, defended by a set of bedrock prohibitions that have held under every condition except direct coercion or impaired agency, and operated by a man who does not believe his ethics qualify him for forgiveness and who has stopped requesting it.

It is not a noble code in the heroic register and he would refuse the description. It is a workable code for a person built the way he was built, lived through the things he has lived through, and trying to remain useful inside a community he believes would, in justice, throw him out. It is the ethics of a man paying rent, on time, every month, on a place he is sure he does not own.

The code's most admirable feature, by the file's assessment, is its refusal of rhetorical self-justification. He does not believe his life makes a moral argument. He believes his acts make small repayments. The accounting is private, the ledger does not close, and he intends to keep working until he is killed.

This is the moral architecture the rest of the dossier must be read against.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 7
## Communications & Linguistic Profile: LeBeau, R. E.

---

### 7.0 Methodological Note

The subject's speech is, more than most subjects in the X-roster, a *constructed instrument*. He is multilingual by upbringing, trained in social engineering from childhood, and has spent his adult life embedded in an Anglophone team environment that requires him to be *legible* while his interior life requires him to remain *opaque*. The result is that nearly every utterance is doing at least two jobs: communicating the surface content, and performing an identity that serves a defensive function. The analyst must therefore read the subject's language at two layers simultaneously — what is said, and what the saying is for. The most useful diagnostic instrument in the entire file is the gap between his **interior captions** (thought-balloons / first-person narration as preserved in the Nicieza '99 and Layman '04 solo runs) and his **spoken dialogue** in the same scene. That gap is the file.

---

### 7.1 The Substrate: Three Native Registers

The subject has, in effect, three first languages, layered chronologically:

**(a) New Orleans Cajun French / Louisiana Creole**, acquired in the Thieves Guild household. This is the language of childhood, of Tante Mattie's kitchen, of Jean-Luc's reprimands, of arguments with Bella Donna, of curses muttered when alone. It is the only register in which the subject is genuinely *unguarded*. When he swears in French under his breath ("*merde*," "*putain*," "*bon Dieu*," "*tabarnak* — borrowed from the broader Francophone-North-American profanity pool"), it is involuntary; when he uses French in courtship ("*chère*," "*mon cœur*," "*ma belle*"), it is deliberate but emotionally true. The diagnostic: French swearing under physical pain is involuntary and real; French endearment in calm conversation is a chosen instrument.

**(b) Louisiana English with a thick Yat-influenced Cajun accent**, his primary public speech. Note: his accent is *partially performed and adjustable*. Subject's interior monologue captions across the Nicieza solo show him narrating in standard English with intermittent Cajun lexicon — meaning, **he does not think in the accent he speaks in**. The accent is thickened around non-Louisianans (charm function), around women he is courting (intimacy-signaling function), around enemies he wishes to be underestimated by (tactical function), and thinned to near-absence in operational contexts requiring crisp tactical communication or in late-night conversations with intimates after defenses have come down. Verifiable: in the high-tension, low-flirtation operational exchanges across Carey's run and the *Marauders* captaincy material, the dropped consonants and the "dis/dat/de" substitutions diminish markedly.

**(c) Thieves' Cant / Guild-internal argot**, the language of the criminal subculture of his youth. Surfaces in Guild-arc material (Nicieza '93 mini, the Tithe / Assassins arcs) — specialized vocabulary for lock types, mark categories, escape routes, fences, the honor code itself. Subject deploys this rarely outside Guild contexts but reaches for it under specific stress: when planning a heist-coded operation, when speaking to Mercy or to his adopted family, when grieving Jean-Luc. It functions as a memorial register.

---

### 7.2 The Third-Person Self-Reference — the file's most diagnostic verbal tic

The single most-cited speech feature is the subject's habit of **referring to himself in the third person**: *"Remy will do it," "Gambit don' like dis," "dis Cajun gon' show you somet'ing."* This is canon-stable across virtually every writer from Claremont through Thompson. Surface reading: charm, swagger, regional affect. Deeper reading is more interesting and more diagnostic.

Third-person self-reference is doing four discrete jobs:

1. **Self-objectification consistent with the upbringing.** A child raised as an asset learns to refer to himself the way his handlers refer to him. "Remy" was, for years, a thing one *deployed*. The grammar survives the context.
2. **Splitting maintenance.** The subject's self-concept is bifurcated (thief-Remy vs. X-Man-Gambit, see §3). Third-person address from the speaker is a *micro-distancing* maneuver: the speaker is not quite the same entity as the named subject, which permits the speaker to discuss the named subject's flaws and crimes with a wry detachment unavailable in the first person. Notice the asymmetry: he uses third person far more often when speaking of *what he is* or *what he has done* ("Remy ain' a good man, chère") than when stating immediate desires ("I want coffee" is, predictably, first-person).
3. **Charm-as-defense.** The third person reads to outsiders as roguish, performative, theatrical — which is exactly the surface he wishes to project. It deflects the listener from registering that an actual confession is happening underneath.
4. **Avoidance of the grammatical "I" in shame-loaded utterance.** When the content is the Morlock Massacre, the Sinister bargain, the Death conversion, the count of third-person constructions per minute *rises*. He cannot, literally, get the "I" out of his mouth in those zones. The "I" implicates the speaker; "Remy" implicates a character.

Predictive use: a sudden collapse from third-person to first-person in the subject's speech is a high-confidence signal of an unguarded moment — confession, exhaustion, or genuine emotional access. "*I'm sorry*" out of his mouth, ungarnished, is rare and load-bearing. Catalog every instance.

---

### 7.3 Diction Inventory

**Endearments (outbound).** *Chère* is the universal — used for Rogue, Storm, civilians, hostile women, female combatants he respects, female telepaths he wishes to throw off-balance. *Cher* (masculine) appears more rarely and almost exclusively in Guild contexts. *Ma belle, mon ange, p'tite, ma fille, mon cœur* form a graduated scale. **The intensity of the endearment is inversely related to the intimacy of the actual relationship**: he calls strangers *ma belle*; he calls Rogue, in the deepest scenes, simply *Anna* or, in private, no endearment at all — just her name, which is the actual signal of intimacy. Surveillance reading: when the endearments *stop*, attend.

**Address terms (inbound).** He calls almost no one by their codename when alone with them. Scott is "Cyclops" in front of others, "Scotty" or "Summers" when alone or annoyed. Logan is "*mon ami*," "Wolverine," or "Logan" in escalating ladder of seriousness. Storm is "Stormy" — *the only person who calls her this, and she has objected to it for thirty years of canon and never made him stop* — which functions as a marker of their specific bond and his refusal to let a verbal intimacy be administratively corrected. Subject is *very precise* about who gets which name; this is the Guild training.

**Curses.** English profanity is rare and emphatic; he prefers French expletives ("*merde*," "*bon Dieu*") for daily annoyance and reserves English profanity for genuine anger. He almost never blasphemes in English in front of strangers — a residue of Catholic-coded New Orleans upbringing — but he will mutter *"bon Dieu"* in French in front of anyone, the foreign-language wrapper softening the impiety in his own ear.

**Religious lexicon.** Persistent Catholic substrate: invocation of *le bon Dieu*, *les saints*, references to confession and penance as concepts even when joking, occasional crossing of self under acute stress (depicted sparsely but consistently — Nicieza, Carey). He does not present as a practicing Catholic, but the language is wired in. **When he uses the word "penance" or "atone" non-ironically, attend; he is speaking from the deep operating system.**

**Idiomatic Cajun lexicon.** *Cher/chère, mon ami, p'tit, fais do-do* (sleep, used jokingly), *lagniappe* (a little extra, used to signify a favor or unexpected benefit), references to *gris-gris* and folk magic that he uses metaphorically without quite believing in them and without quite disbelieving. *"Comme ci, comme ça."* *"C'est la vie."* *"Laissez les bons temps rouler"* — deployed almost exclusively ironically, often in scenes of genuine grief, as armor.

**Card and gambling metaphor.** Pervasive and constitutive. *The deal, the hand, the cards you're dealt, calling a bluff, the house, the odds, all in, fold, ante up, wild card, queen of hearts.* This is not decoration; it is **his actual cognitive model of social interaction**. He thinks in probabilistic, hidden-information terms. When he describes a relationship as "a hand I been playin' a long time," he is not being cute — he is describing how he experiences the relationship internally. Particular tell: he reaches for card-vocabulary most intensely when the topic is something he cannot directly name. Card metaphor density rises in proportion to topical avoidance.

**Thief vocabulary.** *Mark, score, fence, take, lift, case, the job, the play, clean, hot, burn.* Used precisely (Guild-trained) when actually planning operations; used metaphorically about emotional life less often than the card metaphor, but tellingly: he will occasionally describe himself as "*hot*" (in the thief sense — compromised, identified, must be discarded) in the moments after a self-sabotaging confession.

---

### 7.4 Prosody, Pace, and Paralinguistics

**Default pace:** unhurried, lower-register baritone, with a Louisianan elongation of vowels and a habit of trailing the ends of sentences into a near-question, inviting the listener to lean in. This is a Guild-trained *rapport-building* prosody: people who lean in have already begun to trust you.

**Under stress:** speech *slows further* rather than accelerating. This is unusual — most subjects accelerate under arousal. The slowing is a learned counter-tell from Guild training: the calm-voiced operator is the one who is not panicking, and the one who is not panicking is the one in control of the room. Behaviorally, his calmest voice is in the worst moments. **A flat, even-paced "Remy, it's okay" from the subject is a more reliable indicator of an emergency than a raised voice from anyone else on the team.**

**Laughter:** two distinct registers. (a) Performative chuckle — short, voiced, paired with a half-smile and a tilt of the head, deployed as social lubricant. (b) Genuine laugh — quieter, often closer to a breath, almost always accompanied by looking *away* from the person who caused it. The second is rare. The first is constant.

**Silences.** Subject is one of the X-roster's most strategically silent operators. He uses silence the way a card player uses tempo — to let the other person fill the space and reveal information. In team meetings he speaks less than his charm-affect predicts; review of any extended ensemble scene shows him with conspicuously fewer dialogue beats than the impression he leaves. He is *listening more than he is talking* and people misremember this because his lines are memorable when they come.

**Eye-contact and verbal coordination.** Trained in the Guild manner: holds eye contact slightly longer than social norm during disarming small talk (creates intimacy, reads marks); breaks eye contact during operationally critical disclosures (reduces tells); looks at the floor or middle distance during shame-loaded speech. The look-away is the most reliable physical correlate of truth-telling.

---

### 7.5 How He Communicates Love

The subject's love-language is **structured around the impossibility of plain statement**. He does not, on the canonical record, say "I love you" easily, and when he does say it, it is almost always in moments of crisis, departure, or aftermath — never in equilibrium. Equilibrium-love is communicated through:

- **Sustained physical presence at a calibrated distance.** Sitting on the same roof. Walking the perimeter together. The decades-long Rogue courtship was conducted largely at arm's length, and the *arm's length itself* was the love.
- **Endearment in French, escalating in privacy.** Public: *chère.* Semi-private: *ma belle.* Truly private and serious: *Anna,* unadorned.
- **Lagniappe — the small unrequested gift.** A coffee placed at her elbow before she asked. A jacket draped without comment. Card metaphor: he tips the deck in her favor without telling her.
- **Card metaphor as substitute confession.** "Don' know what I'd do without you in dis hand, chère." Reads as flirtation; means *I would lose without you.*
- **Active concealment framed as protection.** The most operationally dangerous expression of his love is the lie of omission. To him, *not telling her about the Massacre* was, for years, the highest expression of love available to him: he was carrying it alone so she would not have to carry it. The cost is enormous and he does not see, until forced, that this is also the deepest betrayal of the same love.
- **Naming.** Use of the actual given name ("Anna," "Ororo" only in extremis, "Jean-Luc" without the "papa" only when furious or grieving) is a love-act. He gives codenames to people he is keeping at distance; he gives real names to people he has admitted, internally, that he loves.

Conversely: the subject *receives* love poorly. Expressions of love directed at him produce, in the canon, micro-deflections — a joke, a card metaphor, a redirected compliment, a change of subject. He cannot let a sincere "you're a good man, Remy" sit in the air uncontested. Watch for this; it is one of the most consistent behaviors in the file.

---

### 7.6 How He Communicates Threat

Threat-speech is the subject's most *under-discussed* register, because the charm-surface masks how good he is at it.

**Threat is delivered, by preference, smiling.** A typical structure: an endearment, an apparently friendly observation, and a quietly devastating tactical fact. *"Chère, m'sieur, you got a real nice setup here. Be a shame if somebody — say, somebody holdin' a king of spades right now — was to charge up dat li'l propane tank behind you."* The threat is the *informational disclosure that he knows something the target did not know he knew*; the kinetic charge is the cherry.

**He does not bluster.** Almost no canonical instance of escalated-voice threat. The threat-voice is, if anything, *quieter* and *slower* than the social-voice. He has internalized the principle that a threat that needs volume is a threat the speaker does not believe he can execute.

**He warns once.** Guild honor code. The single warning is delivered clearly, usually with a courteous address term, and is non-negotiable; subsequent escalation comes without further verbal preamble. Operational note: an unwarned action from the subject is virtually unheard-of against a non-combatant; a warned-once and then acted-upon escalation against a combatant is the standard.

**He prefers to threaten with cards in hand.** The card itself is a *speech act* — produced, displayed, charged, becomes the predicate of the sentence. Frequently the speech can be omitted entirely; the card on the table communicates the sentence in full.

**Threats to people he loves bypass language entirely.** This is the file's clearest predictive signal: if a threat is made to Rogue, to a protected civilian, especially to a child, the subject *stops talking*. The chatter ceases. The accent flattens. He becomes, briefly, a near-silent operator. The voluble Cajun charmer has left the room. Whoever is now in the room should be considered a different and more dangerous interlocutor.

---

### 7.7 How He Communicates Grief

Grief in this subject is **almost entirely non-verbal at its true depth, and entirely verbal at its surface**, with the surface being a near-perfect inversion of the depth.

**Surface grief:** louder humor, more elaborate charm, more flirtation, more card tricks, more bourbon-and-anecdote. The subject performs *exuberance* over fresh wounds. This is canon-stable from the Mutant Massacre material through the death of Jean-Luc through the various Rogue-separation arcs. **If he is the most charming person in the room, check who he has just lost.**

**Mid-grief:** withdrawal into operational competence. Volunteers for watch shifts. Repairs things. Plays solitaire in the dark. Conversation becomes shorter, the accent thins, the third-person constructions diminish — he is too tired to perform.

**Deep grief:** silence in French. The internal monologue, where the writers grant us access, switches partially or fully to French in moments of true private grief (visible in the Nicieza solo and in Carey's interior moments). He grieves in the language he was raised in, even when he no longer thinks daily in it. The grief drives him back to the childhood operating system.

**Spoken grief:** rare, usually short, often delivered in third person as a kind of obituary on himself. "*Remy buried a lot of people, chère.*" The construction *"buried a lot of people"* — passive-adjacent, deflecting agency — is a tell. He does not say "I lost people," because *lost* implies he had them; *buried* is the labor he does after.

**Religious-coded grief:** the resurgence of Catholic vocabulary, the half-conscious cross, the mention of saints, the use of "*le bon Dieu*" in a sincere rather than expletive register. When the subject says "*le bon Dieu*" and is not annoyed, he is grieving.

---

### 7.8 Deflection Language — the catalogue

Subject's deflection toolkit is large and consistent. Field operators interacting with him should be able to recognize each.

1. **The card-metaphor pivot.** Any emotionally direct question is met with a card or gambling reframe that technically answers and substantively does not. *"You okay, Remy?" / "Playin' the hand I got, chère."*
2. **The endearment-as-period.** A *chère* placed at the end of a sentence signals "this is the last sentence on this topic." The endearment functions as conversational punctuation that closes a door.
3. **The accent thickening.** Faced with intrusive sincerity, the accent deepens, the Cajunisms multiply, the listener's attention is redirected to the *manner* rather than the *matter*.
4. **The self-deprecating disclosure.** Offers a true, peripheral, embarrassing piece of personal information to absorb the listener's curiosity ("Remy been thrown outta better places dan dis, chère") so that the listener leaves feeling intimately confided in. Net information transfer about anything load-bearing: zero.
5. **The redirection-via-compliment.** Returns the conversational ball with a flattering observation about the asker, which most askers find irresistible. Particularly effective on Rogue, on Storm in moods, on civilians, on telepaths used to being feared rather than charmed.
6. **The shrug-and-cigarette.** Non-verbal: lights a cigarette, exhales, looks middle-distance, says nothing. The silence itself is the deflection; the listener fills it and the subject responds to what they fill it with, not to the original question.
7. **The joke that is also true.** A self-condemning quip delivered with a smile, so phrased that taking it seriously would seem humorless. Most of his Massacre-related disclosures in casual conversation are delivered in this register. **Take them seriously. They are reports.**
8. **The change of topic via task.** Stands up, suggests coffee, suggests a walk, suggests a check on the perimeter, leaves the conversational frame physically.

---

### 7.9 Linguistic Tells — the truth-telling signatures

The high-confidence indicators that the subject is, in this utterance, *not* performing:

- **Collapse to first-person singular.** "Remy" becomes "I."
- **Use of the interlocutor's given name without endearment.** "Anna." "Ororo." "Scott." Especially if normally he uses the codename.
- **Loss of the accent.** Standard English emerges. This happens in two zones: high-tactical operational communication, and the bottom of grief.
- **French in monologue rather than punctuation.** A French *phrase* (not just an exclamation) in the middle of an English sentence signals he has gone interior. Listening for this is the cheapest, most reliable diagnostic available.
- **Religious vocabulary in the sincere register.** Penance. Atone. *Le bon Dieu* without irony.
- **Speech slowing further when stress rises.** The calm-voice in the crisis.
- **Long unbroken silences in his preferred conversational partners' presence.** Sitting and saying nothing with Rogue, with Storm, with Logan — these are the deepest signs of trust. Talkative-Remy is performing for an audience; silent-Remy has stopped performing because the audience has become a witness.
- **Apology without garnish.** "I'm sorry," without the deflective tag, without *chère*, without the rueful smile. Vanishingly rare. When it occurs, it is total.

---

### 7.10 Register Shifts by Interlocutor — quick reference

- **With Rogue:** courtship-Cajun in public, thinned and quieted in private; "Anna" in the deepest moments; long silences; card metaphors as substitute confession; the only person in the file who consistently produces the un-garnished "I'm sorry."
- **With Storm:** affectionate teasing ("Stormy"), the most genuinely *peer*-textured speech in his repertoire; lower flirtation register, higher honesty register; she is the one to whom he comes closest to confessing things first.
- **With Logan:** clipped, dry, near-monosyllabic by his standards; mutual recognition of two men with histories they do not narrate; the accent thins; jokes are short and dark.
- **With Scott / institutional authority:** correct, slightly formal, charm dialed *down* not up (he reads, accurately, that charm reads to Scott as evasion); operational language; first-name use ("Scotty," rarely) calibrated to mood.
- **With Jean Grey / Emma Frost / telepaths generally:** the most *performatively* Cajun and charming register, with the highest density of flirtation — explicitly because his Guild mental shielding is buttressed by a noisy verbal surface that obscures the quiet interior. He is *louder* around telepaths *on purpose*.
- **With Jean-Luc and the Guild:** code-switches into French at higher density, Thieves' Cant emerges, posture of the prodigal son who is also the inheritor; honorifics observed ("*Papa*," "*Père*").
- **With Bella Donna:** the most volatile register; French dominates; the only person who reliably provokes him into *raised-voice* speech, which by his standards is a near-loss of composure.
- **With children, with Marrow specifically, with the marginal:** voice softens, accent moderates to comprehensibility, endearments shift to the *p'tit / p'tite* register, jokes calibrated downward in irony. This is the kindest version of his speech in the file.
- **With Sinister, with Apocalypse, with the exploitative-father figures:** quiet, compliant-surface, internally negotiating; the third-person-Remy construction *increases* — the splitting defense is at maximum, the speaker placing distance between himself and the named entity being bargained over.
- **Alone (interior monologue):** standard English with intermittent Cajun lexicon, rueful, self-addressing in second person as often as first ("*You done it again, mon ami*"). The second-


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

## Forward Note

The following is a behavioral-prediction matrix derived from the longitudinal record summarized in the pre-synthesis file. Each entry takes a GIVEN — a stimulus, context, or condition the canon never staged or staged only obliquely — and projects the EXPECTED behavior, with the evidentiary thread back to documented pattern. Confidence is graded HIGH / MODERATE / LOW. The purpose is to permit observers to recognize the subject's behavior at the granularity at which it actually occurs: in the half-second before he speaks, in the cigarette he doesn't quite finish, in which side of the booth he chooses.

---

## I. WAKING, GROOMING, AND THE FIRST HOUR

**GIVEN:** Subject wakes alone in a safe location.
**EXPECT:** Eyes open without movement; a count of two-to-four seconds of full stillness while he audits the room by sound before he commits to being awake. Hand drifts toward the side of the bed where a weapon or pack of cards is stored before it drifts toward his own face. Only then does he sit up. *(HIGH; derived from Guild-trained hypervigilance and documented poor-sleep pattern; the "audit before commit" sequence is the operational signature of a trained thief who has been ambushed in his sleep at least once.)*

**GIVEN:** Subject wakes next to Rogue.
**EXPECT:** Same audit, abbreviated; resolves by the second second when he registers her breathing. Will then almost always remain still longer than necessary — five to twenty additional seconds — looking at her without touching. The looking is the ritual; the not-touching is the older ritual underneath it, surviving in muscle memory past its reason. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Subject showers.
**EXPECT:** Long showers, hotter than most tolerate. The wet-heat is regulatory; it is the closest analog he permits himself to the chemical comforts he avoids. Washes hair daily; does not own product in any quantity but uses what is to hand with absent competence. Will sing, hum, or murmur in Cajun French quietly — only when alone or when he believes himself alone; this stops the instant he registers presence. *(MODERATE-HIGH; the linguistic regression in privacy is the inverse of the accent-thickening in performance.)*

**GIVEN:** Subject shaves.
**EXPECT:** Straight razor or near-equivalent; not electric. The instrument is partly aesthetic but mostly habitual — the Guild teaches you to be comfortable holding a blade against your own throat. Will shave faster than most men and with the unstudied accuracy of someone for whom this kind of fine-motor task is below the threshold of attention. *(MODERATE.)*

**GIVEN:** Subject dresses for an unspecified day.
**EXPECT:** Layered. A long coat or jacket selected to break his silhouette and provide deep pockets, *worn even in heat unless social context forbids it*. Boots, not sneakers. Belt with one specific notch — verifiable by wear mark. Cards on his person within forty seconds of standing up; this is checked, not remembered, the way other men check for keys. He will leave a room before he leaves a room without the deck. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Subject must wear formalwear.
**EXPECT:** Wears it well, and is observed to enjoy wearing it well, but adjusts the cut subtly toward freedom of movement — jacket a half-size generous through the shoulders, trouser break short. Will refuse to be unarmed; cards or a thin blade are present. The tuxedo is, for him, a kind of costume he is fluent in; the Guild trained him in social engineering at high altitude. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** First drink of the day.
**EXPECT:** Coffee, strong, taken with chicory if available — the New Orleans tell that survives every other geographic relocation. Drinks it black if no one is watching, dresses it up with sugar/cream theatrically if someone is. The performance/private split is observable in the smallest of his habits and this is one of the most reliable. *(MODERATE-HIGH.)*

---

## II. FOOD

**GIVEN:** Subject orders in an unfamiliar restaurant.
**EXPECT:** Reads the room before the menu. Orders something the kitchen is unlikely to ruin, never anything fussy, and asks the server one personal-but-warm question that establishes rapport and gets him remembered. The server will remember him; this is intentional and trained — a memorable server is an asset in any room he may need to return to. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Subject cooks for himself.
**EXPECT:** Competent and unfussed. Roux from memory; rice by feel; will produce a gumbo, étouffée, or red beans from whatever the pantry permits with no recipe consulted. Cleans as he cooks — Guild training, again: leave no signature. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Subject cooks for Rogue or chosen kin.
**EXPECT:** Same dishes, more elaborate, more time. Will treat the meal as a small ritual. Sets the table by hand. Lights something — candle, lamp — even at noon. The cooking is one of the few unambiguous languages of affection he trusts because it cannot be misread as performance: food is either good or it isn't. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Subject is hungry but offered something he doesn't recognize or dislikes.
**EXPECT:** Eats it without comment if a host is present. Will not insult a kitchen. The Guild teaches that refusing food is a tactical and social mistake. He will quietly under-eat and supplement later. *(MODERATE-HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Buffet or shared plate.
**EXPECT:** Serves others before himself; takes modestly; eats slowly. Last to finish at a casual table; first to finish at a tactical one. *(MODERATE.)*

---

## III. CIGARETTES, DRINK, AND OTHER REGULATION

**GIVEN:** Subject lights a cigarette.
**EXPECT:** Will not use a card to light it (that is showmanship reserved for moments he is performing for a specific audience). Uses a battered, specific lighter — same one for years until it is lost — or matches. Smokes about two-thirds and stubs the rest; long smokers in his somatic register rarely finish. Holds the cigarette between thumb and forefinger as often as between index and middle; this is the Guild grip, native to people who do many small things with their hands. *(MODERATE-HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** He is offered a cigarette by a stranger.
**EXPECT:** Accepts. The acceptance is rapport-building, even if he has his own. He will *not* light theirs with his — too intimate by his code — but will offer his lighter. *(MODERATE.)*

**GIVEN:** A drink at a bar where he is not known.
**EXPECT:** Bourbon, neat, mid-shelf — not top, never well. Asks for it by brand if he has a preference; otherwise lets the bartender choose, which is itself a rapport move. Drinks slowly. Buys one extra at some point in the night for someone he has identified as worth the goodwill — the bartender, an old man at the corner, a woman who looked tired. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** A bar where he is known.
**EXPECT:** Greeted by name; the staff knows his order. He knows theirs — names of children, recent troubles. This is not networking, it is how he was raised; the Guild keeps an inventory of allies the way other people keep an inventory of debts. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Subject is drunk.
**EXPECT:** Rare. When it occurs, the accent thickens further, the humor flattens, the eyes go quiet rather than glassy. He becomes *more* still, not less. Does not become belligerent. Risk profile is for slow self-disclosure to the wrong person; this is when the secret has historically tried to escape, and he knows it, which is why he is rarely drunk. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Offered a drug stronger than alcohol.
**EXPECT:** Refuses, courteously, framed as a personal preference, not a moral one. Will not lecture. The refusal is *firm* in a way that surprises people expecting it to be loose; he will not surrender the ledger of his own consciousness because he has never trusted what might come out. *(HIGH.)*

---

## IV. THE DECK

**GIVEN:** Any unstructured moment of three or more seconds.
**EXPECT:** Cards are in his hands. Shuffled, fanned, palmed, walked across knuckles. This is not a tic in the pathological sense — it is the steady-state condition. The cards are *down* only when the moment is loaded enough to require both hands, or when he is making a point by their absence. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Subject is told to stop fidgeting with the cards.
**EXPECT:** Stops immediately. Smiles. Resumes within ninety seconds. Will not argue about it. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** A deck is offered by a stranger to demonstrate or play.
**EXPECT:** Inspects it as he handles it — corners, edges, finish — by feel, in the first three seconds, without breaking eye contact with the offerer. He has been handed marked decks before. *(MODERATE-HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** He plays poker in a room of non-professionals.
**EXPECT:** Loses approximately as often as he wins. Deliberately. The Guild teaches that a man who always wins is remembered, and a man who is remembered is followed. He plays tight-aggressive when he plays to win and sloppy-amiable when he plays to disappear. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** He plays poker in a room of professionals.
**EXPECT:** Plays straight, plays well, may or may not win, will tip the dealer regardless of result, and will not return to that table twice in the same month. *(MODERATE.)*

---

## V. MOVEMENT THROUGH SPACE

**GIVEN:** Subject enters any unfamiliar interior.
**EXPECT:** Within the first six seconds he has clocked: the exits, the people who are armed or carrying themselves as if armed, the staff/civilian ratio, and the line of sight from the door to wherever he intends to sit. He selects a seat with back to a wall, eyes to the door, never under direct overhead light. If this seat is taken, he relocates within five minutes by social pretext. *(HIGH; trained pattern, signature of professional infiltrator.)*

**GIVEN:** Subject walks a street he has walked before.
**EXPECT:** Takes a different route than last time. The variation is small and would not be visible to a single observation, but across a week of surveillance the route-set is *deliberately diverse* and avoids time-of-day repetition. Guild discipline. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Subject walks a street he has never walked.
**EXPECT:** Walks slightly more slowly than the local pace, looks above eye level more than locals do (windows, rooflines, sight angles), and registers every face that registers him with a half-second of mutual acknowledgment that locals read as friendliness and which is in fact threat assessment. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Subject is followed.
**EXPECT:** Knows within two blocks. Will *not* indicate that he knows. Will adjust his route to confirm the tail by inducing the follower to commit a turn that locals would not make, and then will make one of three choices depending on the read: lose them via the rooftops/alleys he has pre-noted, lead them somewhere of his choice, or turn into a public room and let them either commit or break off. He almost never confronts directly on the street; the Guild teaches that confrontation forecloses options. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Subject is offered a passenger seat.
**EXPECT:** Takes it if the driver is trusted. Otherwise prefers back-right (visibility forward, exit unobstructed). On motorcycles, drives. He does not like to be driven by people he has not assessed. *(MODERATE.)*

**GIVEN:** Subject must fly commercially under a real name.
**EXPECT:** Mild irritation, well concealed. Window seat by preference (it lets him look without looking at people); aisle seat if the flight is short or the cabin warrants quick egress. Reads or sleeps; does not drink on planes. Charms the cabin crew within the first interaction and is invisibly memorable. *(MODERATE.)*

---

## VI. CONVERSATION, GREETING, AND THE SOCIAL SURFACE

**GIVEN:** A stranger introduces themselves.
**EXPECT:** Repeats their name back inside his first sentence. Light handshake — calibrated to theirs, never harder. Eye contact warm and held a fraction longer than American norm; this reads to most people as charisma and to a few as appraisal, which it is. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** A woman introduces herself.
**EXPECT:** Same protocol, with the additional micro-courtesy of acknowledgment-without-leering. The flirtation, when it appears, is performed *upward* — at women confident enough to enjoy it as a game — and is conspicuously *absent* with women he reads as in distress, in subordinate position, or uninterested. He is not the man who hits on the waitress; he is the man who tips her well and asks after her kid. *(HIGH; this discriminator is one of the cleanest in his social file.)*

**GIVEN:** A child introduces themselves.
**EXPECT:** Crouches. Voice drops half an octave. Slows down. Will produce a card trick within ninety seconds if context permits. Remembers the child's name months later. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** A teammate enters a room he is in.
**EXPECT:** Acknowledges with a nod or a one-word greeting; uses the codename more often than the given name in operational contexts and the given name more often in domestic ones, with one or two specific exceptions where the inverse is the joke. Will not interrupt their entry — they may speak first if they need to. *(MODERATE-HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Small talk with a person of consequence (a Xavier, a Storm, a head of state in a diplomatic context).
**EXPECT:** Easy, courteous, with one carefully chosen piece of disarming irreverence early in the exchange that signals he will not be cowed but is also not posturing. He has been doing this since he was twelve. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Asked about his past.
**EXPECT:** Tells a story. The story will be true. It will not be the relevant true story. Specificity, color, and self-deprecation are high; load-bearing material is absent. The listener leaves feeling they have been confided in. *(HIGH; this is the most reliably observable defense in the entire file.)*

**GIVEN:** Pressed on his past by someone with authority to press.
**EXPECT:** Deflection by humor first. If pressed past that, the accent thickens and the answers become *more* charming and *less* substantive. Past a third escalation, he goes still and quiet — this is the warning sign, and it almost never happens, because the first two layers almost always work. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** A direct accusation he knows to be false.
**EXPECT:** Mild amusement; he is good at being falsely accused. Will not defend with vigor; vigor is read by him as concession that the accusation matters. *(MODERATE.)*

**GIVEN:** A direct accusation he knows to be true.
**EXPECT:** Goes still. Does not deny. May or may not confirm. If the accuser is someone whose judgment he respects, he will absorb without argument. This is the Antarctica reflex in micro. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** An insult.
**EXPECT:** Returns it lighter and funnier. Does not escalate. The Guild teaches that the man who loses his temper loses the room. The exception — verified across canon — is insults aimed at a person he protects, particularly Rogue, a child, or someone visibly marked. Then the temperature drops audibly and the next sentence is short. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Praised in public.
**EXPECT:** Redirects the praise to a teammate, a circumstance, or luck. Visible discomfort if the praise concerns moral character rather than competence. He will accept "good shot, Cajun"; he will visibly flinch at "you're a good man." *(HIGH; this is the shame-architecture made observable.)*

**GIVEN:** Praised in private by Rogue.
**EXPECT:** Different protocol. He absorbs it, slowly, and does not deflect; this is one of the few exemptions in his social code, and it tells you everything about what she is to him. *(MODERATE-HIGH.)*

---

## VII. TOUCH AND PROXIMITY

**GIVEN:** Standing in a queue.
**EXPECT:** Half-step further from the person in front than the local norm. Half-step closer to a wall or pillar than to the open room. Hands visible, often one near a pocket. *(MODERATE.)*

**GIVEN:** A handshake from a man.
**EXPECT:** Firm, brief, dry. Eye contact released after the grip releases, not before. *(MODERATE.)*

**GIVEN:** Embraced by a friend on greeting.
**EXPECT:** Receives the embrace, returns it with the same intensity — calibrated, not initiated. He does not initiate physical greeting with most adults. Exceptions are a small list of specific people. *(MODERATE-HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Brushed against accidentally.
**EXPECT:** No reaction visible. The reaction is internal and predates the body — the post-Sinister governor on his power has held for years, but the *fear* of touch-as-detonation has not entirely subsided, and shows up as a half-millisecond muscle stillness that only close observers see. *(MODERATE.)*

**GIVEN:** Asked to hold a baby.
**EXPECT:** Does, without hesitation visible to others. The hesitation that precedes the hand-out is the same half-millisecond stillness, and it is a private moment he has had many times. *(MODERATE-HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Rogue reaches for his hand absentmindedly, post-touch-restriction.
**EXPECT:** A small visible exhale before he meets the hand. Years of restraint do not unlearn at the speed of the medical update. This is the deepest somatic tell in the file and the one most likely to confirm subject's identity to anyone who has known him longitudinally. *(HIGH.)*

---

## VIII. THE TEAM

**GIVEN:** Mission briefing.
**EXPECT:** Arrives on time or two minutes early; takes a seat at the periphery rather than the center; listens more than he speaks; asks one or two precise questions, almost always about extraction or civilian exposure, almost never about objective. The objective is the team's job; the cost is his. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Assigned a partner.
**EXPECT:** Adapts to the partner's operational style within one mission. Compliments them publicly afterward, regardless of result. Will not work willingly with anyone he reads as enjoying violence, will work cheerfully with anyone he reads as competent, and will work patiently with anyone he reads as inexperienced — the inexperienced get more of his attention than the senior. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Disagrees with a tactical order from a team leader.
**EXPECT:** Will not contradict in front of the team. Will pull the leader aside privately, frame the disagreement as a question rather than an objection, and abide by the final call publicly while sometimes quietly modifying his own execution within the call's permissible bounds. The autonomous-under-charming-surface pattern from authority-handling generalized to ops. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** A teammate is wounded.
**EXPECT:** Is the second person to them, not the first; he leaves the medical work to those better at it. But he is the one who stays after the medics have left. *(MODERATE-HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** A teammate is killed.
**EXPECT:** External composure. Does not cry in company. Will be the one who handles the small unwanted tasks — possessions, notifications, the call to a sibling — without being asked. Grief surfaces alone, late, with bourbon and silence. *(MODERATE-HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Asked to lead.
**EXPECT:** Accepts when asked by people he respects; does not seek it. Leads from in-the-mix rather than from the back. Delegates well; takes blame asymmetrically and credit asymmetrically in the other direction. His leadership tell is that *no one on the team knows when he is most worried*, which is its own kind of problem and its own kind of gift. *(HIGH; consistent with later-era captaincy.)*

---

## IX. MONEY

**GIVEN:** Pays at a counter.
**EXPECT:** Cash by preference. Bills folded once, in a specific pocket. Tips visibly generous in service contexts, invisibly generous in private ones — leaves more on the table than the bill technically warrants and does not draw attention to it. *(HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Asked to lend money.
**EXPECT:** Lends if the request reads as honest. Does not expect repayment and does not raise it if not repaid. Will not lend to anyone who appears to be in a self-destructive spiral; will instead buy them a meal and a bed for the night and walk away. *(MODERATE-HIGH.)*

**GIVEN:** Finds wallet on the ground.
**EXPECT:** Returns it. Cash intact. The Guild's code, oddly, supports this — you steal *as a profession*, not opportunistically; opportunism is a mark of the amateur. He is also aware of the moral comedy of a thief returning a wallet, and may be observed half-smiling at it. *(MODERATE.)*

**GIVEN:** Sees an open till, an unattended luxury item, an unsecured safe.
**EXPECT:** Notes it. Does not act. The professional eye does not switch off and does not need to be obeyed; the noting is the discipline. *(HIGH.)*

---

## X. ANIMALS, WEATHER, MUSIC, AND THE SMALL PRIVATE LIFE

**GIVEN:** A dog approaches him on the street.
**EXPECT:** Kneels. Lets the dog come the last step. Speaks to it in French. *(MODERATE-HIGH; the language regression in private moments includes moments he reads as private even in public.)*

**GIVEN:** A cat in the room.
**EXPECT:** Notices it before most people do. Does not approach. The cat usually approaches him. *(MODERATE.)*

**GIVEN:** Heavy rain.
**EXPECT:** Does not hurry. Walks at standard pace, sometimes slower. The body of a man raised on the Gulf — rain is not an emergency. *(MODERATE.)*

**GIVEN:** Cold weather, below freezing.
**EXPECT:** Visible mood drop. Antarctica's residue. He will not complain; he will simply be quieter, and will gravitate toward heat s


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

*Forecasting band: acute and sub-acute. Behavioral predictions keyed to specific stimulus classes. All GIVEN conditions assume the baseline personality structure established in Sections 3–5; all EXPECT clauses are probabilistic, not deterministic, with the most load-bearing inferences flagged. The file's central predictive datum — that the subject's catastrophic failure mode is the acceptance of a controlling bargain from a powerful father-figure under conditions of power-dysregulation plus relational threat — sits beneath all of what follows and surfaces explicitly in §V.*

---

## I. THE WOUND TOUCHED DIRECTLY: MORLOCK-CLASS DISCLOSURE EVENTS

This is the file's hottest stimulus class. Any approach to the Massacre — even oblique, even by someone who does not know they are approaching it — produces predictable, gradable behavior.

**GIVEN:** A stranger, civilian, or non-X-Men acquaintance in casual conversation mentions the Mutant Massacre, the Morlocks, or the tunnels, with no awareness of the subject's involvement.
**EXPECT:** Within 0.5–1.5 seconds, a micro-freeze in the dominant hand (whichever is holding cards, glass, cigarette). The freeze is not the cigarette stopping mid-air — that would be visible — it is the *charge* not initiating on the next reflexive shuffle. He will then resume motion with an over-correction: a flourish, a card-spin, a too-loud laugh, often an immediate topic pivot delivered as flirtation if any woman is present, as a logistical question if not. He will *not* leave the room. Leaving would mark the wound. He will sit through the remainder of the conversation, smoke one extra cigarette, and excuse himself within 8–15 minutes on an unrelated pretext. Sleep that night: reduced. Probability of solo drinking before bed: high.

**GIVEN:** A teammate who knows the history references the Massacre instrumentally in a tactical conversation (e.g., "we should bring Gambit, he knows the tunnel layout").
**EXPECT:** Immediate, calm acceptance of the assignment. He will not flinch on the surface. He will be *over*-prepared — maps memorized to a degree no one asked for, contingency exits planned for civilians who do not exist on the present mission, ration packs and medical supplies in excess. He will walk point. He will not delegate. If the mission involves any underground civilian population, he will physically place himself between them and any threat in a manner that reads to teammates as gallantry and is in fact tithe.

**GIVEN:** A new acquaintance — particularly a survivor of the Morlocks, particularly a child or visibly-marked mutant — recognizes him on sight and names him as one of the men who came in.
