Acceptance-of-the-worst-self is what no peer relationship can offer, because peers, knowing, would withdraw. The bad father knows and *welcomes*. This is irresistible to a subject organized as he is.
4. **A price framed as service rather than soul.** He will refuse a bargain framed as *give me your loyalty*. He will accept a bargain framed as *do this job for me*. The transactional frame allows him to preserve the fiction of contracted labor rather than surrendered self.

Any party with intelligence sophistication can construct this offer. Two historical adversaries did so without notable difficulty. The subject's susceptibility is **not** classified; it is, structurally, the most exploitable feature of his profile.

---

## 11.3 What the Collapse Looks Like, Hour by Hour, in a Worked Example

Reconstructed from the canon's pattern across the Marauders assembly and the Apocalypse conversion, here is the modal collapse, scaled to a hypothetical present-day instance:

- **H–168 to H–72:** Stage 1 indicators accumulate. He volunteers for an extra rotation. Cigarettes up. Rogue notes he is "quiet." He attributes it to a head cold. He is in fact running the early phase of an unmetabolized memory.
- **H–72 to H–36:** Stage 2. He takes a solo recon. He executes flawlessly. He returns and does not go to their quarters; sleeps in the captain's chair. Rogue does not press. He takes this as kindness and as evidence she is preparing to leave him.
- **H–36 to H–18:** Stage 3. Trigger event — say, a news report of a Morlock-descended community in distress, or a face in a crowd that resembles a Marauder. The tremor begins. He notices, performs unnoticing, holds his hand away from his hip. He flirts more. He tells a junior X-Man an unrelated old story about lifting a wallet at fourteen, framed as funny. He is rehearsing.
- **H–18 to H–6:** Stage 4. He wakes Rogue at 03:00 and tells her something true, badly. Or he doesn't, and he leaves. Either way, the relational regulator is now offline by his action.
- **H–6 to H–0:** The offer arrives. The offerer is competent, paternal, knowing, transactional. The subject — power dysregulated, relationally severed, internally convinced he is what the offerer says he is — accepts.
- **H+0 onward:** He executes. Competently. Quietly. Without resistance. The atrocity proceeds at the speed of his skill, which is considerable.

The window for interruption, end-to-end, is approximately one week. The window for *easy* interruption is the first 48 hours of it. The window for *desperate* interruption is the last 6.

---

## 11.4 What Recovery Looks Like, and What It Doesn't

Recovery from a completed Stage 5 — historically — does not look like guilt, does not look like remorse-display, does not look like collapse. **It looks like quiet return to function with a slightly heavier load.** The Morlock Massacre did not produce a visible breakdown; it produced a man who, for years, was *better* at being useful and *worse* at being known. The Death conversion produced the same.

This is the most counterintuitive feature of the subject's profile and the one most likely to be misread. **He metabolizes catastrophic moral failure by adding it to the rent he is paying** and continuing to pay rent. He does not stop, does not flee, does not refuse missions, does not externalize. He absorbs.

The cost is paid in:

- Marginal further compression of the affective range.
- Further intensification of the impossibility-of-deserved-happiness operating belief.
- A new tier of secret to be carried into the next intimacy.
- A slight increase in baseline cigarette consumption that never reverses.
- A new category of trigger added to the Stage 3 trigger set, which from then on includes whatever sensory or contextual material accompanied the new failure.

He does not get smaller. He gets *denser*. Each failure compacts.

The recoveries that actually heal, rather than absorb, have all involved the same structural element: **someone who already knew the worst, refused to leave, and required him to remain present rather than penitent.** Rogue, executing this across multiple arcs. Storm, in the recruitment and the long quiet partnership. Selectively, the small handful of teammates who learned the Marauders truth and stayed. The healing intervention is not forgiveness (he cannot receive it) and not punishment (he over-pays it). The healing intervention is **witnessed continuity** — the refusal to either absolve or expel.

---

## 11.5 Risk Calculus and Monitoring Recommendations

For any party — protective, custodial, or analytical — observing this subject longitudinally, the monitoring priorities, in order:

1. **Track the small-object charge tremor.** It is the earliest reliable somatic indicator that the Stage 5 triad is forming and the only one that cannot be performed away. Surveillance asset: any close-association observer with hand-eye attention. Rogue detects this without trying; most others miss it.
2. **Monitor Rogue's status and his belief about her status independently.** Her actual condition is one variable; his perception of it is another, and the perception drives the behavior.
3. **Watch for arrivals.** Any new authority-coded figure entering his orbit who satisfies the four sub-conditions of the paternal-competent offer is to be treated as a Stage 5 vector regardless of stated intent. Including ostensibly benevolent ones. Especially ostensibly benevolent ones, because the benevolent presentation lowers the subject's resistance further.
4. **Be suspicious of his good weeks immediately following a bad one.** The post-Stage-4 calm is the failure stage, not the recovery stage.
5. **Do not interrogate. Do not require disclosure. Do not offer absolution.** All three accelerate the curve. The intervention with evidentiary support is presence-without-demand from a known witness.
6. **Price in his consent to capture.** If the subject is ever delivered without struggle to an adversary, do not assume coercion. Assume he agreed. Plan extraction accordingly — the obstacle will not be his guards; the obstacle will be him.

---

## 11.6 Closing Note for This Section

The subject's failure mode is the failure mode of a person who has decided, at some level beneath argument, that he is on probation in his own life. His decompensations are not crises of self-preservation; they are crises of self-permission. He breaks not by losing his grip but by *letting go on purpose*, having concluded — wrongly, repeatedly, with the full conviction of a man who has rehearsed the conclusion for forty years — that letting go is the more honest thing to do.

The file's single most important predictive sentence, restated for closure:

**He will not resist the bad outcome. He will walk to meet it, courteously, because he believes it has been waiting for him the whole time, and he does not want to keep it waiting any longer than he already has.**

— UATU, Section 11 closes.


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# TRAJECTORY & FORWARD ASSESSMENT
## Subject: Remy Etienne LeBeau ("Gambit")
### File Section 11 of 14 — Forward-Looking Synthesis

---

## 11.0 Framing Note

What follows is not prediction in the actuarial sense; it is the projection of a *vector* derived from a sixty-year published record whose every inflection is now mapped in the preceding ten sections. The subject is not in acute crisis at the present file-date — he is married, employed in a leadership role aboard a vessel whose name (*Marauder*) constitutes the longest-running symbolic restitution in his life, and operating within a relational system that, for the first time in his documented history, *can be physically completed without disclosure-by-violation*. This is the strongest baseline of his life. It is also, by his own internal operating system, the most precarious — because the gap between "what he deserves" and "what he has" has never been wider, and the subject's historical response to that gap is to close it himself.

The trajectory therefore branches sharply. We map the branches, the fork points that select between them, and the indicators that — for any party with an analytic or benevolent interest in this subject's continued functioning — should be watched.

---

## 11.1 The Baseline Trajectory (Status-Quo Drift, 5–10 year horizon)

Absent shock, the subject's trajectory is one of **slow, asymmetric integration** — slow because the load is large, asymmetric because the integration is happening in the relational domain considerably faster than in the intrapsychic domain.

Externally: continued team leadership, continued operational excellence, gradual expansion of the protective-mentor role he has already adopted toward younger and marginal mutants. He will, in this drift scenario, become — and is already becoming — the X-roster's *consigliere*: the one senior operator with the social intelligence to broker between factions, the institutional memory to know which old debts are still live, the temperament to handle the cases nobody else has the patience for. This is a role he can hold for decades and is well-suited to. He will be increasingly sought out by younger members as a confidant precisely because his self-presentation reads as non-judgmental; this in turn will further stabilize him (the rescuer-of-the-marginal pattern feeding the reaction-formation defense, virtuously).

Internally: the gap between presentation and interior will *narrow* under the stabilizing effect of a marriage that can no longer be terminated by accidental memory-transfer disclosure. Some of the energy historically routed into charm-as-deflection will become available for other uses. Expect a slight *decrease* in dialect-thickening under social stress (one of the most reliable behavioral markers in the file), a slight *increase* in volunteered emotional self-disclosure to Rogue specifically, and a *plateauing* (not resolution) of the Morlock-related rumination — the thought will not stop arriving, but the cycle-time between intrusion and recovery will shorten.

The Marauders-ship leadership role is, in this scenario, the **most therapeutic environment available to him short of formal treatment.** It externalizes the inverse-of-crime metaphor into a daily lived practice. Every successful rescue is a quiet receipt against the ledger. The ledger does not zero out — it never will — but its rate of accrual against him is for the first time slower than the rate of repayment.

**Probability weighting (drift scenario): roughly 45–55%, conditional on the absence of the destabilizers itemized in §11.3.**

---

## 11.2 The Growth Trajectory (the harder, less likely, more valuable path)

A genuine growth trajectory — meaning *structural change in the underlying C-PTSD / moral-injury presentation*, not merely improved circumstance — requires the subject to do something he has historically refused to do: **voluntarily author his own confession, in language, to a witness who will not flinch and will not absolve.** This is the specific therapeutic move that moral-injury literature (Litz, Shay) identifies as the load-bearing intervention for perpetration-trauma. Forgiveness is not the mechanism. *Truthful, witnessed articulation, integrated into a continuing communal identity*, is the mechanism.

For this subject, the available witnesses are limited and each has a contraindication:

- **Rogue.** Already knows the load-bearing content via prior memory-absorption. But the *unvoluntary* nature of her knowing is precisely the wound — he has never *given* her the story; she *took* it. A growth move would be him telling her, in his own words, with no defensive humor, what he did and why. He has not done this in the published record. Doing it would constitute the single most therapeutically significant act of his life. The structural barrier: she already knows, so the conscious mind dismisses the act as redundant. The reason it is not redundant is precisely the reason he resists understanding it is not redundant.
- **Storm.** Has the moral standing (she rules judgments, she is trusted, she does not flinch). She is also the figure who, in regressed form, brokered his entry into the X-Men — meaning he owes the relationship a debt of foundation. A confession to Storm would be ritually appropriate. He will not initiate it. He might accept it if she initiated the conversation.
- **A surviving Morlock.** The hardest, most accurate witness. He has spent decades adjacent to Sarah/Marrow without ever explicitly speaking the thing. The growth move — speaking it to her — is so high-cost that it is unlikely without external catalyst.
- **A peer perpetrator who has done their own work.** Sabretooth is contraindicated (no work done). Magneto is partially indicated (perpetrator who has attempted moral re-architecture) but the father-figure dynamic disqualifies him as safe witness. Emma Frost is structurally interesting — perpetrator-history, telepathic discretion, no dependency dynamic — and is, on the file evidence, an underused potential interlocutor.

The other condition of growth is **decoupling the kinetic-charge problem from the relational-charge problem in his own self-model.** The neurological entanglement (§2) is real, but it has been over-extended into a *metaphor* that governs his intimacy: *to love is to risk losing control of the hands.* Sustained safe touch with Rogue, accruing month over month and year over year, is the slow-acting solvent on this metaphor. Five years of uneventful daily contact will do more for his attachment architecture than any single insight. Ten years will begin to alter the substrate.

**Probability weighting (growth scenario, in its full form): 10–15%.** Higher (perhaps 25–30%) for the partial form — material improvement in affect regulation and disclosure behavior without the full structural confession move.

**Indicators that growth is occurring**, watchable longitudinally:
- Decreased dialect-thickening under stress.
- Spontaneous use of the word "I" instead of "Gambit" or "Remy" (third-person self-reference is a documented avoidance marker in his speech).
- Smoking frequency reduced without environmental reason.
- Sleep duration extended.
- Volunteered emotional content in private dialogue with Rogue, *unsolicited*, on topics he has historically deflected.
- Willingness to be photographed / depicted without affect-management posture (the half-smile, the cocked hat, the cards-in-hand are *poses*; their reduction is data).
- A single act of articulated apology to a Morlock survivor.

---

## 11.3 The Catastrophe Trajectory (the failure mode, and how it would unfold)

The file's most important predictive datum, restated: under conjoint conditions of (a) acute power dysregulation, (b) loss of or estrangement from Rogue, and (c) a credible offer of *control over his own power* from a figure who reads as a powerful father, the subject has, twice in the documented record, accepted the bad bargain. He is structurally susceptible to a third instance.

The catastrophe scenario therefore has a known shape. It does not arrive as a single event; it arrives as a **convergence of three independent stressors that the subject is uniquely poor at absorbing simultaneously.**

**Stressor 1 — Power dysregulation.** The kinetic governor installed by Sinister is not a clean prosthetic; it is an excision-and-suppression. Across the canon, dysregulation episodes recur (X-Cutioner's Song fugues, Death-mantle relapses, post-Apocalypse residuals). Any new escalation event — a power-mutation, a M-Day-style global reshuffling, a Krakoan resurrection irregularity, a Sinister-related re-activation — re-opens the original wound. The subject responds to power-dysregulation not primarily with fear of harming others (though that is present) but with the older, deeper response of *believing he must accept whatever bargain is offered to make it stop.* This is the conditioned response and the file's gravest warning.

**Stressor 2 — Loss of Rogue.** Death, separation, possession, or — most dangerously — a *betrayal* in which Rogue is the agent (mind-control, Brood, evil-future-self, the catalogue is large). The subject's stability is disproportionately load-bearing on this single attachment. He does not have the diversified emotional portfolio that would absorb the loss without structural collapse. He has built a life in which Rogue is the *witness who knows and stayed*, and her loss would not only be grief but would functionally retract the permission to remain in a moral community that her continued presence has been granting him for two decades.

**Stressor 3 — The credible offer.** Sinister is the canonical author of these offers and remains, at any file-date, a live and recurring presence in the subject's environment. Apocalypse, in any of his iterations, also qualifies. So would, in a less obvious register, *any institution* that approached him offering not money or power but the specific currency he is susceptible to: **a clean conscience purchased by a single act of cooperation.** The shape of the offer is always the same: *do this thing, and the dysregulation will stop / the secret will be safe / the people you love will be protected.* He has, on this template, twice authored atrocity.

If the three stressors converge — and they have converged before, and will, in a publication continuity that recycles its rogues, converge again — the catastrophe scenario unfolds in a predictable sequence:

1. *Concealment.* He hides the dysregulation from Rogue and the team. This is the first failure point, and the one most amenable to intervention by anyone who knows him well enough to read the early markers (increased smoking, decreased sleep, increased operational solo-work).
2. *Approach.* The offering figure makes contact. The subject does not immediately accept; he reasons, he delays, he hopes to find another solution.
3. *Isolation.* He withdraws from Rogue specifically, ostensibly to protect her, in fact to free himself from the witness who could veto the bargain.
4. *Acceptance.* The bargain is taken, framed internally as *protective sacrifice*. This is the moment of catastrophic identity-collapse, but it is experienced subjectively as relief.
5. *Perpetration.* The act is performed. Often, as in the Morlock template, he does not fully know what he is authoring until it is too late.
6. *Concealment 2.* Post-act, he conceals the act from Rogue and team, beginning the cycle over.

**Probability weighting (catastrophe in full form, 10-year horizon): 15–25%, with the upper bound conditional on the activity level of Sinister and similar figures in the operational environment.** This is too high a probability to ignore in any forward planning involving this subject.

**Early-warning indicators**, watchable in real time:
- Renewed solo-work patterns inconsistent with mission tempo.
- Reduced contact with Rogue without stated cause.
- Geographic drift toward New Orleans, or toward locations associated with prior bargains, *without operational pretext*.
- Sudden interest in his own medical history / brain scans / power-output metrics (the dysregulation tell).
- Re-engagement with Guild contacts beyond what current operational needs require.
- Quietness. The single most diagnostic marker. This subject's pathology is loud only when it is manageable; when it goes silent, it is preparing.

---

## 11.4 The Open Questions

Several questions remain genuinely unresolved on the canonical record, and each represents a *fork point* — a place where future developments could swing the trajectory materially.

**Q1: Will Sinister make another approach, and in what form?**
Sinister is the structural antagonist of this life and is, in any current continuity, alive and operating. The form of the approach matters: a direct extortion is *less* dangerous than an indirect offer of help with a problem the subject already has. The latter is the historical template and the more likely vector.

**Q2: Will the Guild past come for him in restitution?**
Bella Donna, the Assassins Guild, the politics of New Orleans — these are unfinished. The subject has not paid the price for Julien's death in any way the Assassins Guild recognizes. A restitution arc is overdue in narrative terms and would force him to either accept further punishment (consistent with character) or refuse it (a growth signal). Either resolution is informative.

**Q3: Will the children he has rescued — Sarah/Marrow most centrally — ever explicitly speak the thing to him?**
This is, on the file evidence, the highest-leverage potential intervention in his life that does not require his own initiation. If a surviving Morlock confronts him with full knowledge and *does not destroy him*, the moral-injury substrate could meaningfully begin to integrate. If they confront him and *do* condemn him, he will accept it, and a small piece of the load will be — paradoxically — lifted, because *being held accountable by the person actually wronged* is the one form of moral payment his system recognizes as legitimate.

**Q4: What happens to him if Rogue precedes him in death?**
The most dangerous open question. The file's working answer: *he will not survive it well.* Not via active self-harm — that is not his pattern — but via the catastrophe sequence in §11.3, which his grief would activate by removing both the witness and the brake. Any contingency planning involving this subject should treat Rogue's safety as load-bearing on his own.

**Q5: Does he ever, voluntarily and in his own words, tell anyone the full Morlock account?**
Open. Historically, no. The growth trajectory in §11.2 turns on this answer becoming yes.

**Q6: Does he reconcile with Jean-Luc and the LeBeau family, and on what terms?**
The Guild relationship is conditionally stable but never fully reconciled. The father-figure who raised him strategically remains a complex object. A genuine adult-to-adult reconciliation, in which the subject neither performs the dutiful son nor refuses the relationship, would be a maturation marker.

**Q7: Does he ever want children of his own, and what would that do to him?**
Genetically and circumstantially complicated (the Becca arc, the genome issues with Rogue). But the question matters because the subject's protectiveness toward children is a defining feature, and the prospect of being a father to a child whose origin is *his choice* rather than *his being-chosen* would activate every unresolved layer of his attachment history. High-stakes question. Could be the single most powerful growth catalyst, or the single most powerful catastrophe vector, depending on outcome.

---

## 11.5 The Fork-Point Inventory

For ease of reference, the analytically significant fork points — events whose outcome will materially redirect the trajectory:

| Fork | Catastrophe-side outcome | Growth-side outcome |
|---|---|---|
| New Sinister approach | Accepts bargain | Refuses, *and tells Rogue* |
| Power dysregulation recurrence | Conceals from Rogue, seeks external "fix" | Discloses immediately, accepts collective management |
| Confrontation by Morlock survivor | Avoids, isolates | Stays, listens, articulates apology in own words |
| Loss / threat to Rogue | Collapses into solo-vengeance / catastrophe sequence | Accepts grief inside the community he has built |
| Offer of leadership beyond Marauders captaincy | Accepts to over-pay penance | Accepts proportionate to capacity, *or* declines from self-knowledge rather than self-punishment |
| Fatherhood opportunity | Refuses on grounds of unworthiness | Accepts, and tolerates the unworthiness while doing the work anyway |
| Bella Donna restitution claim | Accepts disproportionate punishment | Negotiates a proportionate one, refusing both flight and self-destruction |

The pattern across the table is instructive: the growth-side outcomes share a common structural feature — **proportionality**. The subject's defining failure mode is *disproportion*, in both directions (under-disclosing the secret, over-accepting the punishment). Every growth move, regardless of domain, is a move toward *measured response*.

---

## 11.6 What Would Push Him Toward Growth

In approximate order of leverage:

1. **Continued, uneventful, daily safe touch with Rogue, over years.** The slow solvent. Nothing else in his life does this work. Anything that preserves and protects this — including, frankly, the boring stability of the marriage as depicted in the Thompson run — is therapeutic at the substrate level.
2. **A witness who knows, does not flinch, and does not absolve.** Storm, Emma, a Morlock survivor, possibly a non-mutant clinician with appropriate clearance. The intervention is articulation-in-language to a non-flinching ear. Absolution would be counter-therapeutic; he would reject it and the relationship along with it.
3. **Sustained mentorship of younger mutants in the role he is already in.** The reaction-formation defense, properly channeled, *becomes* a virtue. It is, in his case, possibly the most efficient available conversion of pathology into function.
4. **A successful refusal of a Sinister-type offer, in real time, with witnesses.** Once accomplished, the conditioned response would weaken. The script in his nervous system says *accept*; an enacted *refuse* writes new memory over old.
5. **A formal therapeutic relationship.** Underrated and never depicted. The X-roster has resources (Doc Samson historically, others currently). The subject would resist on grounds of privacy, charm-out the clinician, and only do real work in approximately year three. He has never been given the years.
6. **Proportionate accountability for old debts** — paying what is actually owed, in forms the wronged parties accept, and *stopping when paid*. The stopping is the harder half.

---

## 11.7 What Would Push Him Toward Catastrophe

In approximate order of danger:

1. **Loss of Rogue, in any form.**
2. **Sinister-or-equivalent approach during power dysregulation.**
3. **Public re-litigation of the Morlock Massacre in a forum that condemns without permitting reparative response.** The Antarctica trial was survivable because Rogue's verdict, however harsh, was a *judgment delivered by a witness who continued to exist in relation to him*. A condemnation that *excludes* him from the community is the configuration that would activate the worst response.
4. **Mind-control or possession scenarios.** He has been Death; he has been Marauder-handler. He is unusually vulnerable to having his agency hijacked precisely because some part of him is always partly willing to be hijacked, on the conditioned belief that his agency is dangerous and should be relinquished to a stronger frame. Any party planning operations near this subject must price in his *low resistance to being made a weapon by someone he is conditioned to trust.*
5. **Confirmation of irredeemability from a respected source.** Not accusation — *confirmation*. He can deflect accusation; he absorbs confirmation. A respected figure telling him, sincerely, *you are what you fear you are*, would be destabilizing in a way that exceeds the apparent informational content of the statement.
6. **Prolonged separation from operational meaning.** Idleness. The Marauders role is therapeutic precisely because it converts his energy daily. Strip the role, and the energy reroutes inward, and the inward direction is the rumination cycle. He needs work the way some subjects need medication.

---

## 11.8 Synthesis: The Vector

The subject is, at file-date, on the best trajectory of his adult life, and on the most fragile. He has assembled, over forty published years, the *external* conditions under which his unresolved internal load could finally begin to metabolize: a marriage that admits touch, a role that inverts his founding crime, a community that has, in pieces, already absorbed his worst secret and kept him in it. The conditions are sufficient for slow drift toward integration. They are not, on their own, sufficient for structural healing.

The structural healing requires one move he has never made: *to speak the thing, in his own voice, to a witness who will not absolve him and will not leave.* The probability of his making that move unprompted is low. The probability of his making it if the right witness, at the right moment, asks the right question is meaningfully higher. Any party with benevolent interest in this subject's future should understand that the highest-leverage intervention available is not protection, not therapy in the abstract, not even continued Rogue-stability — it is *the cultivation of conditions under which the confession could be voluntarily spoken.* Everything else is downstream.

The catastrophe vector is not gone. It will not be gone in his lifetime. Sinister remains alive; Apocalypse remains alive; the power-governor in his head remains a surgical kludge whose long-term reliability is unestablished; Rogue remains mortal in the only senses that matter to him. The file's standing recommendation, for any decade in which this subject is under observation, is the same: **watch the quiet.** When this subject goes quiet, the file goes on alert. When he is loud, charming, dialect-thick, card-shuffling, half-smiling under the brim of his hat — he is, by his own design, telling you everything that is not the thing, and the thing is, by his own design, manageable. It is when the performance drops without replacement, when the smoking rises without occasion, when the geographic drift begins, when Rogue is no longer the first call — *that* is the configuration the file exists to flag.

He has spent his life paying rent on a place he believes he has not earned. The forward question, the only one that matters, is whether he will ever come to believe that the rent is paid — or, failing that, whether the people around him can build a structure stable enough that he can keep paying it indefinitely without it killing him. The drift trajectory says yes to the second. The growth trajectory says yes to the first. The catastrophe trajectory says he will, under the wrong convergence, burn down the building rather than admit he lives in it.

The vector, on balance, points toward integration. The watch, on balance, must remain.

---

*End Section 11. Cross-reference: §3 (Psychological), §4 (Psychiatric), §5 (Personality) for the substrate this projection rests on; §12 (Operational Recommendations) for the action items derived from this trajectory; §13 (Contingency Protocols) for response frameworks in each branch.*

## Relationship Graph
### [[Anna Marie LeBeau (Rogue)]]
- The chosen object; the load-bearing bond. Selected because untouchable - the avoidant strategy made flesh. The relationship lived for years in the yearning register where he is good at it. Eventually marriage post-touch-restriction (Mr. and Mrs. X).
- Current state: most regulated configuration of his life. She is the anchor and the daily reason to keep paying rent.
- Failure mode: if she absorbs another load of his secret without warning and flees again (the X-Men #7 template), he goes to Antarctica - literally or functionally. If she is killed or taken, he becomes tactically irrational and structurally available to the next father-figure offering control. The closer the bond, the worse the curdle: she is the only person whose disgust would confirm his self-verdict, and confirmation is what destabilizes him.
- Leverage: anything done to her routes through him at full amplitude. She is the single highest-yield pressure point in the file.

### Mr Sinister
- The original exploitative-father. The bargain that installed the central wound. Surgical intervention in exchange for the Marauders / Morlock Massacre.
- Current state: dormant but never extinguished. Subject has not metabolized this relationship; he has only put it in a drawer.
- Failure mode: a credible Sinister approach offering renewed control over the kinetic charge - or offering to undo the Death-conversion residue - reactivates the original conditioning. Historically he resists initially, struggles sincerely, and has accepted the bargain twice.
- Leverage: the single most dangerous pathway to operationalize this asset against his own team. Any planning involving the subject must price in Sinister-as-relapse-vector.

### Jean Luc Lebeau
- Adoptive father, Thieves Guild patriarch. The man who raised him as asset before son. Affection and exploitation share a vocabulary because Jean-Luc spoke them in the same sentences.
- Current state: ambivalent. Loyalty and resentment co-resident. Will answer the call; will not stay long.
- Failure mode: Guild politics dragging him back into a closed loop he cannot say no to.
- Leverage: any Guild-frame summons routes through him.

### Bella Donna Boudreaux
- First love, ex-wife, intermittent enemy. Killed her brother on their wedding day.
- Current state: oscillates ally / threat. The Assassins Guild's institutional grudge persists.
- Failure mode: she becomes the vector for a New-Orleans-frame trap; subject's guilt over Julien makes him slow to defend himself against her.
- Leverage: invoking Julien's name produces silence and slowness.

### Storm
- Original X-Men entry-broker. Met her amnesiac and de-aged - he chose a safe sister/mother figure to broker his return to a moral community.
- Current state: sister bond, deep and stable; one of the very few who has earned his interior register.
- Failure mode: her disapproval lands heavier than command structure; if she ever told him he was irredeemable, the damage would be order-of-magnitude.
- Leverage: she can summon him from anywhere; she will not abuse this.

### Sarah Marrow
- The one child he saved in the tunnels. His proof to himself that the man was not entirely the act. Unfinished business.
- Current state: protective on reflex; she does not always want it.
- Failure mode: her rejection of him as savior collapses the only self-redemption fragment he allows himself.
- Leverage: anyone threatening Marrow accesses him directly.

### Apocalypse
- The second exploitative-father. The Death conversion. The Sinister bargain rerun in higher key.
- Current state: residual conditioning dormant; conversion artifacts (sclera flares, intrusive imagery) intermittent.
- Failure mode: any reactivation of the Death programming is catastrophic and may not be reversible from outside.
- Leverage: secondary to Sinister but on the same pathway.

### X Men Collective
- Adopted moral community. The institution he is paying rent on.
- Current state: integrated, trusted, captain-rank in Marauders era.
- Failure mode: any institutional tribunal in which he is asked to account for the Morlocks - he will not defend himself, he will accept the verdict, and the team will lose him. The institution can destroy him by formalizing what he already believes.
- Leverage: route requests through chosen individuals, not through the institution.

### Wolverine
- Operational peer, similarly compromised history; reads him fast and does not flinch.
- Current state: trusted; one of the few who knows enough not to push.
- Failure mode: if Logan ever endorsed the irredeemable verdict, it would land like Storm's would - heavier than command.
- Leverage: Logan can ask him to do almost anything operationally.
